801 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Alabama Pub. Serv. Comm'n v. Southern Bell Tel. & Tel. Co.


No. 3 Div. 753


Supreme Court of Alabama


268 Ala. 312; 106 So. 2d 163; 1958 Ala. LEXIS 506; 26 P.U.R.3d 400



July 24, 1958 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 30, 1958, Reported at 106 So.2d 163 at 170.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the state and the public service commission (commission), sought review of a decree of the circuit court of Montgomery County (Alabama), which set aside the commission's denial of appellee phone company's scheduled intrastate rate increases.


OVERVIEW: The phone company filed with the commission a proposed new schedule of increased rates and charges for its Alabama intrastate telephone service, including both local service and intrastate toll service. These rates were to become effective on February 21, 1954. The commission, acting pursuant to Ala. Code tit. 48, § 54 (1940), suspended the operation of the proposed new rates for a period of 60 days in order to investigate their reasonableness. Thereafter, the commission entered its order denying the company's petition for an increase in rates. The company appealed. The circuit court found in favor of the company. The state and the commission appealed. The court reversed and held that the commission must in good faith give consideration to the element of reproduction cost as some evidence of the value of a utility's property for rate-making purposes. The commission did not consider this element to have any weight in its determination of the reasonable value of the company's property. On remand, the commission must take this into consideration.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decree of the circuit court and remanded the action to the commission for further proceedings in accordance with the court's opinion.

803 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. Lancaster


No. 7 Div. 300


Supreme Court of Alabama


267 Ala. 366; 102 So. 2d 1; 1958 Ala. LEXIS 336



April 10, 1958 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant litigant challenged a final decree from a trial court (Alabama) denying declaratory relief with respect to the constitutionality of a statute passed by the Alabama Legislature.


OVERVIEW: The litigant's bill of complaint had alleged that the statute was violative of Ala. Const. §§ 22, 45, and 106. In his prayer for relief, the litigant requested the court to declare the statute unconstitutional and void. The litigant filed with the court a brief stating the basis of the appeal. The court refused to hear the litigant's appeal. Ala. Code tit. 7, § 166 (1940) required any party who requested declaratory relief, alleging that a statute was unconstitutional, to serve the State's attorney general with a copy of the proceeding. Moreover, under Ala. Code tit. 7, § 166, the attorney general was entitled to be heard. The court reviewed the record and found no evidence revealing that the attorney general was ever served with a copy of the proceeding. Failure to serve the attorney general was a jurisdiction defect. Because the absence of appellate jurisdiction was clear on the face of the record, the court was required to take notice of the lack of jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal.

805 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Bramlett v. State


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


31 Ala. 376; 1958 Ala. LEXIS 550



January, 1958, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the Circuit Court of Benton, (now Calhoun.)

Tried before the Hon. William M. Brooks.

The prisoner, Larkin Bramlett, was indicted at the fall term, 1853, of the circuit court of Cherokee, for the murder of Benjamin F. O'Bannon; was arraigned at the same term, and pleaded not guilty. After several continuances, the cause was removed, on the application of the prisoner, to the circuit court of Benton, now Calhoun county, where a trial was had at the November term, 1857, which resulted in his conviction.

The verdict of the jury, as appears from the bill of exceptions, was in these words: "We, the jury, find the defendant guilty of murder in the first degree, as charged in the bill of indictment, and assess capital punishment." When this verdict was returned, "the court asked the jury, if they intended by their verdict that the prisoner should suffer death; and suggested that, if such was their verdict, they had better change it, so as to insert the word 'death,' instead of 'capital punishment.' Thereupon all the jury orally responded, that they had found by their verdict that the prisoner should suffer death; and forthwith struck out the words 'capital punishment,' inserted [**2] the word 'death' in the place thereof, and returned said verdict, so altered, into court. Said verdict was thereupon received by the court, and ordered to be entered of record, [in these words:] 'We, the jury, find the defendant guilty of murder in the first degree, and that he must suffer death.' The prisoner objected to this; but the court overruled the objection, and the prisoner excepted."

The certified transcript, sent by the circuit clerk of Cherokee, to the court in which the trial was had, purported to contain "a full, true and complete transcript of all the orders and entries, as stated of record," in the cause, "together with a true copy of the original bill of indictment"; but did not show the organization of the grand jury by which the indictment was found. The record does not show that the prisoner raised any objection, during the progress of the trial, to the sufficiency of the transcript; but the bill of exceptions states that, after conviction, he moved the court "to set aside the verdict, and arrest the judgment, on the following grounds: 1st, that the circuit court of Benton has no jurisdiction of the case; 2d, that no grand jury was summoned, charged and sworn,  [**3] before and upon the finding of the indictment; 3d, that it does not appear by the record in said cause that any grand jury was ever summoned, charged or sworn, on or before the finding of the indictment; 4th, that the transcript of the record from the circuit court of Cherokee does not contain any caption of the grand jury who found the bill of indictment; 5th, that said transcript of the record is defective; 6th, that there is no bill of indictment, or properly certified copy of an indictment, in this court; 7th, that there is no legal evidence to this court that there is any bill of indictment against the prisoner; and, 8th, that the judgment is not authorized by law." On the hearing of the motion, the prisoner produced the certified transcript, containing the defect above named, "which was the only transcript in the court; and thereupon the court refused to pass upon said motion, and suspend its judgment, and ordered that the clerk of the circuit court of Cherokee be ordered to send down to this court a full and complete transcript in said cause; to all of which the prisoner objected, and excepted to the overruling of his objection."

On a subsequent day of the term, "and after [**4] the sentence of the court had been passed upon the prisoner," the solicitor produced another certified transcript from the records of the circuit court of Cherokee, showing the organization of the grand jury in that court. "The defendant objected to the same, because it was illegal and irrelevant; because it was no part of the records in this cause; because it was not a paper belonging to this court; because it was not properly on file in this court; and because it was not made out, certified, or filed in this court, until after the trial of said cause, and after said cause was ended; and because the same was not properly certified. The court overruled all these objections; the transcript was read, and the defendant excepted. The court then overruled the motion in arrest of judgment, and the defendant excepted."



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.

 

806 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Myers v. Mobile Press-Register, Inc.


No. 1 Div. 648


Supreme Court of Alabama


266 Ala. 508; 97 So. 2d 819; 1957 Ala. LEXIS 574



October 31, 1957 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant alleged tavern operator sought review of an order from the trial court (Alabama), which sustained appellee newspaper's demurrer to both counts of the alleged tavern operator's libel complaint.


OVERVIEW: The alleged tavern operator was identified as such in an article in the newspaper and charged with planning, in concert with others, to petition or influence the city commission to "unionize" its policemen, firemen, and other city employees. The alleged tavern owner contended that the article was libel per se. The trial court sustained the newspaper's demurrer and the alleged tavern owner appealed. The appellate court affirmed. The court held that the words in the article were not libel per se. The article did not charge that the alleged tavern operator was opposed to all government. The conduct imputed to him did not constitute an indictable offense, and the court was unable to conclude that the charge of such conduct tended to bring the alleged tavern operator into public hatred, contempt, or ridicule, or charged an act odious and disgraceful in society. While some of the words used were harsh and not calculated to endear the newspaper to the subjects of the article, the publication complained of was not libelous per se.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order sustaining the demurrer.

 

807 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Busch Jewelry Co. v. Bessemer


No. 6 Div. 940


Supreme Court of Alabama


266 Ala. 492; 98 So. 2d 50; 1957 Ala. LEXIS 594



October 31, 1957 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant jewelry company sought review of the judgment of the Alabama trial court in its action seeking declaratory judgment against appellee city. The company attacked the validity of Bessemer, Ala., Ordinance 1112 (Feb. 9, 1954).


OVERVIEW: The company alleged that Bessemer, Ala., Ordinance 1112 (Feb. 9, 1954) was unconstitutional. The court held that Ala. Code tit. 7, § 166 (1940) required that the state attorney general be served with a copy of the proceeding, and no such service had been made. Therefore, the court held that the lower court never acquired jurisdiction to authorize the rendition of the decree appealed from and that said decree was void. The court held that because the decree in the lower court was void on the face of the record, the court was without jurisdiction to entertain the appeal.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal.

810 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Ex parte Anniston Personal Loans, Inc.


No. 3 Div. 742


Supreme Court of Alabama


266 Ala. 356; 96 So. 2d 627; 1957 Ala. LEXIS 527



July 26, 1957 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Peremptory writ of mandamus awarded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner company brought a petition for the writ of mandamus or other appropriate remedial writ to be directed to the Circuit Court of Montgomery County (Alabama) to require it to set aside and vacate the order entered by it for the production of records by the company.


OVERVIEW: Respondent State had filed a bill of complaint against the company that sought an injunction to restrain the company from making or entering into any loan contract or agreement whereby the rate of interest exceeded the statutory rate. At the same time the State had filed a petition for production of documents that sought production of the company records related to loans, and the circuit court granted the petition and ordered the production. On review, the court awarded the petition for a peremptory writ of mandamus. The court found that Ala. Code tit. 7, § 489, which was relied on by the State in support of the ordered production, did not include discovery as one of its purposes. The court reasoned that there was no reasonable basis for construing the authority given to a judge by § 489 as authorizing him to order production of documents by a party or by a person who was not a party for inspection by a party in advance of trial. The court further found that the purpose of § 489 was to provide for the production at the trial of documents in possession of a witness for use as evidence in the trial; it did not contemplate the production of documents in advance of trial.


OUTCOME: The court awarded the company its petition for a peremptory writ of mandamus.

 

811 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Larson v. State


No. 3 Div. 749


Supreme Court of Alabama


266 Ala. 589; 97 So. 2d 776; 1957 Ala. LEXIS 563



July 26, 1957 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 14, 1957.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, lending company and its partners, challenged decrees of the Circuit Court of Montgomery County (Alabama), which overruled their demurrer on respondent State's bill to enjoin the lending company and its partners from making any contract at a usurious rate of interest, in violation of Ala. Code tit. 9, § 60 (1940), and granted the temporary injunction as prayed for.


OVERVIEW: The State brought suit against the lending company and its partners, seeking a temporary injunction to restrain them from making contracts at a usurious rate of interest in violation of Ala. Code tit. 9, § 60 (1940). The trial court rendered decrees overruling the lending company and its partners' demurrer to the bill and granting the temporary injunction. The court affirmed, determining that the lending company and its partners were properly enjoined from deliberately charging highly usurious rates of interest on short term small loans made to necessitous borrowers, who were largely ignorant and not advised of their legal rights and were not able to employ counsel to represent them, because the activities were against the public policy of the State. The State did not have an adequate legal remedy under the Harris Act because the activity that it sought to enjoin was not violative of the Act, and the sanctions of the Act could not be used to suppress them. The trial court, acting in equity, had the authority to prohibit the lending company from using the courts in collecting more than the principal amount of the obligations by invoking Ala. Code tit. 9, § 65 (1940).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decrees that overruled the lending company and its partners' demurrer on the State's bill to enjoin them from making any contract at a usurious rate of interest and that granted the temporary injunction to the State.

 

812 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Brugh v. White


No. 2 Div. 344


Supreme Court of Alabama


267 Ala. 575; 103 So. 2d 800; 1957 Ala. LEXIS 520



June 27, 1957 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 19, 1958.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of an order by the Circuit Court of Greene County (Alabama), which entered an order of condemnation of the real estate, fixing the amount of damages and compensation for appellee property owners of the real estate at the sum of $ 5,500 by which judgment the city acquired title to the real estate.


OVERVIEW: Appellants contended that the statute providing for ascertainment and payment of value of life interest in land taken under eminent domain, which was in full force and effect prior to creation of condemnation award or fund, applied to such award or fund pursuant to Ala. Code tit. 47, § 64(1) (1940). The court determined that the trial court erred in holding that Ala. Code tit. 47, § 64(1) (1940), did not apply in the situation involved in the case; that the statute was unconstitutional in so far as it attempted to provide a method of distribution in the case; that the rights of the parties became fixed before the passage of the statute, and that the property owners had a substantive or vested right in the condemnation award subject only to the right of the life tenants to the income thereof until the death of the last surviving life tenant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, with instructions.

 

813 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Bolin v. State


No. 6 Div. 288


Supreme Court of Alabama


266 Ala. 256; 96 So. 2d 582; 1957 Ala. LEXIS 526



June 20, 1957 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted after a jury trial resulted in a verdict and judgment of guilty of the unlawful possession of an ingredient for the purpose of making stink or tear gas bombs, and he appealed. The Court of Appeals (Alabama), certified the question of the constitutionality of Ala. Code tit. 14, § 369 (1940), based on its belief that the statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with possession or placement of a stink bomb, and with possession of one of the ingredients necessary or commonly used in making such a stink bomb. The jury acquitted him of the first charge and found him guilty of possession of an ingredient. Defendant appealed, and the court of appeals certified the question of the constitutionality of that portion of § 369. The court determined that the statute arbitrarily pronounced as unlawful all possession, whether innocent or criminal, of any ingredient for the purpose of making stink or tear gas bombs. No standards of conduct were set up to guide the innocent or warn the criminal, or to advise a defendant of the nature and cause of the accusation or to guide the courts in administering that provision of the statute. To make the possession of a commonly used stink or tear gas bomb ingredient for the purpose of making such bomb a crime, was so vague and uncertain as to be disproportionate to the evil sought to be suppressed and was condemned as an unwarranted abuse of the police power of the state and offensive to the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution, and to Ala. Const. of 1901, art. 1, § 6.


OUTCOME: The court determined that the statute that criminalized possession of ingredients that could be used for the making of stink or tear gas bombs was unconstitutional.

816 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Ex parte Rice


No. 6 Div. 56


Supreme Court of Alabama


265 Ala. 454; 92 So. 2d 16; 1957 Ala. LEXIS 319



January 10, 1957 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Writ denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sought a writ of mandamus in order to review a decision from an Alabama trial court that denied his motion to strike subpoenas served by defendant.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff sued defendant for trespass, trover, and detinue. Defendant served subpoenas on plaintiff and one witness to take their depositions under 1955 Ala. Acts. 375. Plaintiff filed a motion to strike the subpoenas, alleging among other things that the statute was unconstitutional. The trial court denied the motion but stayed the taking of depositions pending review. On appeal, the court held that: (1) the act established discovery standards for civil actions at law in courts of general jurisdiction because it adopted the Federal Rules of Civil Procedure, (2) plaintiff's allegations were insufficient to overcome the presumption that the legislature complied with constitutional requirements in enacting the statute, (3) the title of the statute was sufficiently comprehensive, (4) any defects in the title could be cured by correcting the mistakes, (5) the legislature could provide for methods of conducting depositions without impinging on individual rights, and (6) the statute did not violate plaintiff's due process rights because it gave notice, a hearing, and judgment in accordance with the notice and hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court and denied plaintiff's petition for a writ of mandamus.

 

817 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Ex parte NAACP


No. 3 Div. 779


Supreme Court of Alabama


265 Ala. 349; 91 So. 2d 214; 1956 Ala. LEXIS 530



December 6, 1956 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Writ denied and petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner civil rights organization sought a writ of certiorari after a circuit court (Alabama) held the organization in contempt of court for its failure to comply with an order requiring the production of certain books and records for inspection in an action that had been brought by respondent state attorney general on behalf of the state.


OVERVIEW: The attorney general filed an action on behalf of the state that sought to enjoin the organization from conducting business in Alabama. The circuit court entered an order that required the organization to produce certain books and records for inspection by the state. The organization did not comply with the order. It was adjudged in contempt of court and was fined. The fine was increased when the organization did not thereafter fully comply with the discovery order. The organization then filed a petition for a writ of certiorari. The court denied the writ and dismissed the petition. The court stated that an order requiring the production of evidence in a pending matter could be reviewed by mandamus. Therefore, the organization was entitled to certiorari only if the contempt order was void on its face. The court concluded that the fines were valid because the organization was found to be in civil, not criminal, contempt. Therefore, the limitations on punishment contained in Ala. Code tit. 13, §§ 9, 143 (1940) were not applicable. The court also stated that the organization could not raise self-incrimination as a defense to the discovery order because it was a corporation.


OUTCOME: The court denied the writ of certiorari sought by the organization after it was held in contempt for failure to comply with a discovery order. The court dismissed its petition.

819 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Riley v. Smyer


No. 6 Div. 59


Supreme Court of Alabama


265 Ala. 475; 91 So. 2d 820; 1956 Ala. LEXIS 560



November 29, 1956 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 17, 1957.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner daughter of decedent sought review of the Probate Court of Jefferson County (Alabama), which sustained a demurrer to the petitioner's pleading, which claimed that the probate court's decree adjudging the decedent incompetent was void and coram non judice.


OVERVIEW: The probate court decreed the decedent to be mentally ill. A guardian ad litem was appointed. After 14 years and upon the decedent's death, the administratrix sought to overturn the decree of lunacy. The administratrix contended that one jurisdictional defect in the petition was present. The court held that it was not required that the petition allege that the decedent had "property" in Jefferson County "requiring the care of a guardian" because this requirement applied only to a person of unsound mind who did not reside in Alabama. The decedent was a resident of the state. Finding that the petition was sufficient to invoke jurisdiction of the probate court. The court failed to find that the lunacy petition or the decree adjudging the decedent to be of unsound mind to be void. Notice to the decedent of the proceedings was not required because if the person alleged to be of unsound mind was a resident of the county, and was at the time of the application confined in a hospital or asylum within or without the state, inquisition may be had and taken without notice to him.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the probate court's judgment.

 

820 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Dixie Finance Co. v. Demopolis


Nos. 2 Div. 303, 305


Supreme Court of Alabama


265 Ala. 267; 90 So. 2d 732; 1956 Ala. LEXIS 506



November 15, 1956 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, two small loan companies (licensees), sought review of the decision of the Marengo County Circuit Court (Alabama) that entered judgment in favor of defendant city in the licensees' action to recover the amount of a licensee fee assessed by the city in order for the licensees to do business in the city and paid by the licensees under protest.


OVERVIEW: The license was imposed by Demopolis, Ala., General License Ordinance § 169 (1951). The licensees argued that § 169 was arbitrary, unreasonable, and confiscatory. The licensees also argued that § 169 was unconstitutional because it resulted in the deprivation of their property in violation of the U.S. Constitution and the Alabama Constitution. The court affirmed the judgments, finding that the licensee tax was a revenue measure and that the amount of the tax was not so unreasonable and excessive in amount as to be confiscatory and prohibitory. The court noted that when determining whether a revenue tax was confiscatory or prohibitory, it was important to consider: The populousness of the municipality, the profitableness of the business, the character of the business proposed to be licensed and its effects upon the community, and the additional expense necessarily entailed by a police supervision of the business. The court explained that the power to license a privilege implied the right to fix the amount of the fees and that the action of a municipal body in fixing a fee was only to be disturbed in cases of manifest abuse of that power.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

821 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bay Towing & Dredging Co.


No. 1 Div. 595


Supreme Court of Alabama


265 Ala. 282; 90 So. 2d 743; 1956 Ala. LEXIS 507



November 15, 1956 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Mobile County (Alabama), which held that appellee taxpayer, a company, was not liable for use tax on any of its barges but approved the assessment of use tax on three tugs. The taxpayer cross-appealed the portion of the circuit court's ruling with respect to the assessment of the use tax on one of the tugs.


OVERVIEW: The Alabama Department of Revenue made a final assessment of use tax on equipment purchased outside of Alabama by the taxpayer. The circuit court held that the taxpayer was not liable for use tax on any of the barges but was liable for the assessments on the three tugs at issue. The State appealed and the taxpayer cross-appealed the ruling as to one of the tugs, which was used. The court affirmed. The court held that the Sales Tax Act and the Use Tax Act were required to be construed together and because the barges were not purchased within Alabama, and therefore not subject to the sales tax, they also were not subject to the use tax. To hold otherwise would have been a clear discrimination against the taxpayer's interstate sales transactions. As to the taxpayer's liability for use tax on the used tug, the circuit court correctly held that the tax was properly assessed. The tug was concededly an "automotive vehicle" and an amendment to Ala. Code tit. 51, § 788 (1951) clearly extended the operation of the use tax to include used automotive vehicles. As such, the court found an implied repeal of Ala. Code tit. 51, § 789(u), which exempted used automotive vehicles from the tax.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.

823 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


State v. Overby


No. 6 Div. 58


Supreme Court of Alabama


265 Ala. 39; 89 So. 2d 525; 1956 Ala. LEXIS 452



September 6, 1956 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State of Alabama challenged a decree in equity of the circuit court (Alabama) that overruled the State's demurrer to appellee taxpayer's bill appealing from an additional punchboard tax assessment by the Alabama Department of Revenue and seeking a trial de novo under the provisions of Ala. Code tit. 51, § 140 (1940).


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer argued that former Ala. Code tit. 51, § 579 (1947), under which the punchboard tax was assessed, authorized a lottery in violation of Ala. Const. § 65 (1901), that its repeal in 1953 without a savings clause meant no tax was due, and that it deprived him of due process of law. The court affirmed the circuit court's decree, holding that the trial court properly overruled the State's demurrer because one of the causes of action stated by the bill was good. The court held that Ala. Code tit. 51, § 579 (1947) was not unconstitutional because the court had previously held that it was a revenue measure that did not authorize illegal gambling and the 1947 amendment of § 579 made no material changes affecting its constitutionality. The 1953 repeal of § 579 did not affect the validity of the claim against the taxpayer pursuant to Ala. Const. § 100 (1901) because the amount of the claim had been fixed and was due prior to the repeal. Ala. Code tit. 51, § 732 (1940), under which the tax was assessed, satisfied due process requirements. The taxpayer waived notice irregularities by appealing for a trial de novo and waived a jury trial by failing to request one.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court decree that overruled the State's demurrer to the taxpayer's bill appealing from the additional punchboard tax assessment and seeking a trial de novo.

 

824 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


State v. Plantation Pipe Line Co.


No. 3 Div. 735


Supreme Court of Alabama


265 Ala. 69; 89 So. 2d 549; 1956 Ala. LEXIS 460; 6 Oil & Gas Rep. 961



August 2, 1956 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 13, 1956. Writ of Certiorari Denied December 10, 1956. See 77 S.C. 263.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Alabama State Department of Revenue (state), challenged a decision of the Circuit Court of Montgomery County (Alabama) declaring that the final assessment of franchise tax made for 1952 under 51 U.S.C.S. § 348 against appellee pipeline company was invalid in its entirety and ordering a refund to the company of the tax it had paid in order to appeal, as provided in 51 U.S.C.S. § 140, together with interest and costs.


OVERVIEW: The company ran a pipeline operation through several states and had support operations, such as pumping stations, in Alabama. The state argued that the company was subject to the franchise tax by virtue of such operations and its permit to operate in the state. However, all of the company's property and personnel in Alabama were committed to and used solely in interstate business. The trial court thus found the tax invalid because the company was engaged solely in interstate commerce in Alabama in 1952. The court affirmed, finding all of the company's business, activities, and operations in Alabama were carried on solely in furtherance of and were inherent, integral, and necessary parts of the interstate transportation of petroleum products. It was irrelevant that the company had qualified to do business in Alabama and had obtained an annual permit. It did so under protest and only to conduct business in interstate transportation. The court also found that a case involving the company's 1942 franchise taxes was not res judicata for the instant case. That case was settled, and there were no findings with which the court could determine whether the issues in the cases were similar.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's finding that the state's franchise tax assessment on the company was invalid.

 

825 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Woods v. State


No. 6 Div. 945


Supreme Court of Alabama


264 Ala. 315; 87 So. 2d 633; 1956 Ala. LEXIS 351



May 24, 1956 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In his habeas corpus action, petitioner sought review of a judgment from the trial court (Alabama), which declined to discharge him from the custody of a sheriff who had arrested him under a warrant directing his delivery to an agent of New York for parole violations.


OVERVIEW: At trial, the evidence showed that petitioner was arrested on the warrant, and on trial was ordered to be released to the New York authorities. The proceeding for his arrest and the order releasing him to the New York authorities were claimed by virtue of Ala. Code tit. 42, § 27 (1940). On the trial of the habeas corpus case, it was agreed in open court that pursuant to § 27, the Governor of Alabama and the Governor of New York entered into an agreement as recited in the statute. Petitioner contended that § 27 was void because it violated the due process clause of the Constitution, and that the order for his release to the New York officers was without legal authority. That contention was denied and overruled, and it presented the only matter shown by the transcript, which was the court's duty to consider on the appeal under Ala. Code tit. 15, § 369 (1940). Upon review, the court found that the trial court properly denied petitioner's contention. Ala. Code tit. 42, § 27 (1940) was not violative of due process. Therefore, there was no error in the order of the trial judge declining to grant the discharge of petitioner.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

826 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Wheeler v. Bullington


No. 8 Div. 839


Supreme Court of Alabama


264 Ala. 264; 87 So. 2d 27; 1956 Ala. LEXIS 335



April 12, 1956 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Reversed, rendered and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sheriff sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Colbert County (Alabama), which denied his motion to set aside the final decree ruling that 1955 Ala. Acts 174, p. 440 was unconstitutional in appellee taxpayer's declaratory judgment action. The sheriff's motion argued that the decree was void for failure to serve a copy of the proceedings on the state attorney general. The taxpayer filed a motion to dismiss the appeal.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer challenged the validity of the Act. The trial court declared the Act to be unconstitutional. The sheriff filed a motion to set aside the final decree. The trial court denied the motion. On appeal, the court reversed, finding that, in a declaratory judgment action alleging that a statute was unconstitutional, Ala. Code tit. 7, § 166 (1940) required the state attorney general to be served and given an opportunity to be heard. The court ruled that § 166 was mandatory and jurisdictional; thus, the trial court's jurisdiction was not properly invoked, and its decree was void because the record did not show that the attorney general was served with a copy of the proceeding, or that he had notice of the proceeding or participated in it in any way. The court denied the taxpayer's motion to dismiss the appeal, ruling that the motion was not merely an application for rehearing, but challenged the decree as void on its face and invoked the trial court's inherent power to vacate it. The court found that, when the trial court refused to vacate the decree on the motion, claiming that it was void on its face, the remedy for review was by appeal because the denial was a final decree.


OUTCOME: The court denied the taxpayer's motion to dismiss the appeal, reversed the trial court's order denying the motion to set aside the decree, entered judgment granting the motion to set aside, and remanded the case for further proceedings, including service of a copy of the proceedings on the state attorney general challenging the constitutionality of the statute.

 

827 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Personnel Board of Mobile County v. Mobile


No. 1 Div. 590


Supreme Court of Alabama


264 Ala. 56; 84 So. 2d 365; 1955 Ala. LEXIS 733



November 28, 1955 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 12, 1956.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner board brought an action against respondent city, seeking a declaration as to the constitutionality of 1953 Ala. Acts 370. The city filed a demurrer to the bill. The Mobile Circuit Court (Alabama) entered judgment sustaining the city's demurrer. The board appealed.


OVERVIEW: The board had jurisdiction over classified employees of the city, including the chief of police and the police department. After the approval of 1953 Ala. Acts 370, the board brought the declaratory judgment action alleging Act 370 took the board's power over classified employees away when certain conditions occurred. The board was within the only county in the state within the population range condition set out in Act 370. The board asserted Act 370 was a delegation of legislative power to the city. On appeal of the judgment that sustained the city's demurrer, the court affirmed because Act 370 did not confer the power to pass a law inconsistent with state law upon the city's authorities.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that sustained the city's demurrer to the bill filed by the board.

829 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Shell Oil Co. v. Edwards


No. 6 Div. 620


Supreme Court of Alabama


263 Ala. 4; 81 So. 2d 535; 1955 Ala. LEXIS 548



June 16, 1955 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Cross-appeal dismissed. Reversed and rendered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Complainant purchasers and respondents, lessor and corporation both appealed from a decision of an Alabama trial court enjoining the construction of a filling station. The court found that the station constituted a nuisance. The purchasers and respondent asserted that the court improperly found that Ordinance No. 797-F, which declared commercial property on which the proposed station was to be built, was valid.


OVERVIEW: A lessor and a corporation planned to construct a filling station on property that a city deemed commercial under Ordinance No. 797-F. Purchasers of property sought to enjoin the construction of this station. The trial court enjoined the station's operation, but the court reversed this decision. The court also dismissed the purchaser's appeal in which they challenged the validity of Ordinance No. 797-F, finding that a city may change an area from one use to another under Ala. Code tit. 37, § 779 and Ala. Code tit. 62, § 715. Additionally, the court held that a filing station can not be considered a nuisance per se even if located in a residential area. A filing station may become a nuisance if its operation disturbs the neighborhood where it is located, but the mere fact that its operation will cause depreciation is not enough for it to be declared a nuisance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision enjoining the lessor and corporation from setting up a filling station. The court also dismissed the cross-appeal.

 

830 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Gayden v. State


No. 3 Div. 722


Supreme Court of Alabama


262 Ala. 468; 80 So. 2d 501; 1955 Ala. LEXIS 501



May 12, 1955 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought certiorari review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Alabama), which reversed defendant's conviction for the crimes of obtaining morphine and opium by use of a false name, in violation of Ala. Code tit. 15, § 259 (1940).


OVERVIEW: The State, in an indictment, charged defendant with a violation of § 259 by tracking the statute and by alleging that the crime was against the public. The trial court overruled a demurrer of the indictment, and defendant was convicted. The appellate court held that the acts constituting defendant's alleged guilt were not set forth with reasonable certainty. The court affirmed the appellate court's reversal, holding that due process required that defendant be noticed of the true nature of the charges against him. Although defendant was sufficiently informed of the crimes for which he was charged, he was not sufficiently informed of the acts that allegedly constituted the crimes. Because defendant was charged with offenses against the "public" rather than against "persons" did not entitle him to less constitutional protection. The court found that the names of the persons to whom the property belonged had to be alleged, regardless of whether it was a "public" offense. Due process required that a fair hearing be granted prior to a deprivation of life, liberty, or property. A fair hearing was not possible unless defendant was notified of the charges to be defended against.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court that reversed defendant's conviction.

832 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Fikes v. State


No. 2 Div. 335


Supreme Court of Alabama


263 Ala. 89; 81 So. 2d 303; 1955 Ala. LEXIS 533



May 12, 1955 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 23, 1955.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of a trial court (Alabama), which convicted him of first degree burglary with intent to ravish and sentenced him to death. The trial court denied defendant's pre-trial motions to quash the indictment and the venire, in which he alleged that minorities were systematically excluded solely because of their race or color and that the indictment was based solely upon an involuntary confession.


OVERVIEW: Other indictments against defendant had been quashed because minorities were systematically omitted from the jury roll. The grand jury and venire in the case on appeal were drawn from a new revised roll, which the commissioners compiled after investigating available sources, such as the city and telephone directories, the list of registered voters, and by personal inquiry and personal contact, to identify qualified minorities who were not exempt. Affirming defendant's conviction and sentence, the court determined that the trial court properly overruled defendant's motions to quash the indictment and the venire because the indictment and trial were controlled by the revised roll and the evidence failed to show that the jury commission systematically omitted qualified and not exempt minorities because of their race or discriminated against them on that account and thereby deprived defendant of due process or the equal protection of the law. The court held that under Ala. Code tit. 30, § 86, defendant could show that there was no competent witness or legal documentary evidence to support the indictment, but that he could not challenge the sufficiency of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

 

833 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Talladega v. Ellison


No. 7 Div. 177


Supreme Court of Alabama


262 Ala. 449; 79 So. 2d 551; 1955 Ala. LEXIS 473



April 14, 1955 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of an order from the trial court (Alabama), which sustained appellee taxpayer's demurrer and dismissed the city's action against the taxpayer seeking to collect outstanding license tax.


OVERVIEW: The city filed an action against the taxpayer and alleged that he operated a grocery store within the city and that he owed and had not paid the city's license taxes. The city sought an order enjoining the taxpayer from operating his store, ordering an accounting for the amount of the license tax due, and granting a lien on the business for the unpaid tax. The taxpayer demurred and argued that the city's complaint was devoid of equity. The trial court sustained the demurrer and the city sought review. The court found that the complaint was not devoid of equity because it did not seek any specific amount and sought an accounting to determine the license tax amount, that the allegations in the complaint were sufficient to seek an injunction against the taxpayer, and that the demurrer was sustained in error.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's decision.

 

834 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Pike v. Southern Bell Tel. & Tel. Co.


No. 6 Div. 470


Supreme Court of Alabama


263 Ala. 59; 81 So. 2d 254; 1955 Ala. LEXIS 522; 9 P.U.R.3d 335



March 24, 1955 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 19, 1955. Further Rehearing Denied June 23, 1955.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff subscriber appealed from a judgment of the trial court (Alabama), which overruled her demurrers to defendant telephone company's plea that it lawfully discontinued service to the subscriber the subscriber's telephone was being used for illegal purposes and the municipal commissioner of public safety ordered the termination of service.


OVERVIEW: The telephone company discontinued the subscriber's telephone service pursuant to an order from the police commissioner stating that the subscriber's telephone was used for an unlawful purpose. The subscriber brought an action for damages for discontinuing her telephone service. The trial court overruled the subscriber's demurrer to the telephone company's plea that its action was justified by the police commissioner's order, and the subscriber appealed. The court reversed and remanded, holding that the police commissioner's order did not constitute a defense to the subscriber's claim that termination of her service without proof that she was using her phone illegally was a violation of the telephone company's obligation to provide every subscriber with equal service. A telephone company may not refuse to furnish service because of mere suspicion that it was being used for an illegitimate end, or merely because it received a notice from a law enforcement agency that the service was being used for illegal purposes. The company had the burden of establishing the fact, and to exercise such power ex parte violated due process of law and deprived the subscriber of her legal rights.


OUTCOME: The judgment overruling the subscriber's demurrers to the telephone company's plea that its termination of service was justified by orders of the commissioner of public safety was reversed and the case was remanded.

 

835 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Government & Civic Employees Organizing Committee v. Windsor


Nos. 3 Div. 702, 702A


Supreme Court of Alabama


262 Ala. 285; 78 So. 2d 646; 1955 Ala. LEXIS 437; 35 L.R.R.M. 2603; 28 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P69,172



March 10, 1955 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Act No. 720 is as follows:

"Section 1. As used in this act the term 'labor union or labor organization' means any organization of any kind, in which employees participate for the purpose of dealing with one or more employers concerning grievances, labor disputes, wages, rates of pay, hours of employment, or conditions of work; and the term 'public employee' means any person whose compensation is derived in whole or in part from the State, or any agency, board, bureau, commission or institution thereof.

"Section 2. Any public employee who joins or participates in a labor union or labor organization, or who remains a member of, or continues to participate in, a labor union or labor organization thirty days after the effective date of this act, shall forfeit all rights afforded him under the State Merit System, employment rights, re-employment rights, and other rights, benefits, or privileges which he enjoys as a result of his public employment.

"Section 3. This act shall not apply to persons employed as teachers by any county or city board of education or trade schools or institutions of higher learning, nor shall it apply to those employees of the State Docks Board referred to in [***2] Title 38, Section 17 of the Code of Alabama, 1940, nor shall it apply to employees of cities or counties.

"Section 4. Any public employee who prior to the passage of this act or to his public employment belonged to a labor union or labor organization and as a result thereof has acquired insurance benefits or any other financial benefits may continue to participate in such labor union or labor organization to the extent that he shall not lose any benefits thus acquired.

"Section 5. The provisions of this act are severable. If any part of the act is declared invalid or unconstitutional, such declaration shall not effect (sic) the part which remains.

"Section 6. All laws or parts of laws which conflict with this act are repealed.

"Section 7. This act shall become effective immediately upon its passage and approval by the Governor, or upon its otherwise becoming a law."



DISPOSITION: The decree in 3 Div. 702 is affirmed. The appeal in 3 Div. 702-A is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant unincorporated association appealed a decree by the Circuit Court of Montgomery County (Alabama), which declared that the association was a labor union or organization as defined in the Solomon Bill, 1953 Ala. Acts 974, and that the Solomon Bill applied to the association and its members including employees of appellee Alabama Alcoholic Beverage Control Board. The association also appealed an earlier decree overruling their demurrer.


OVERVIEW: The Solomon Bill required public employees to chose between their membership in a union or their rights under the State Merit System. The unincorporated association was an organizing committee of an larger organization composed of affiliated national and international unions, organizing committees, local industrial unions, and industrial union councils. Certain rules governing the unincorporated association were adopted and they set forth the objectives of the association. Those objectives included the creation of an international union and working toward better wages and benefits for workers. The court upheld the circuit court's conclusion that the association was a labor union within the meaning of the Solomon Bill. Testimony by an official on behalf of the association that the association was just a discussion group was undercut by the adopted rules of the association. The court dismissed the association's other appeal as untimely.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decree that declared the association to be a labor union or organization and dismissed the association's appeal from the decree overruling a demurrer.

840 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


State v. Robinson Land & Lumber Co.


No. 1 Div. 572


Supreme Court of Alabama


262 Ala. 146; 77 So. 2d 641; 1954 Ala. LEXIS 558



November 4, 1954 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 10, 1955.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State of Alabama sought review of a decree of the circuit court (Alabama), which overruled the State's demurrer to appellee taxpayer's bill of complaint alleging that a formula used by the State Department of Revenue for computing income taxes due the State from corporations also doing business in other states violated Ala. Code tit. 51, § 390 (1940).


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer was an Alabama corporation doing business in Alabama and Mississippi. On its income tax return, the taxpayer claimed a credit under Ala. Code tit. 51, § 390 (1940) for out-of-state income and taxes paid to Mississippi. The taxpayer claimed that no tax was due Alabama because its Alabama income tax computed on its total aggregate net income for the tax year from all sources was less than the product of its income derived from business transacted in Mississippi multiplied by the Alabama tax rate. The Department made an assessment against the taxpayer based upon its own formula that imposed two state income taxes upon one income. The taxpayer brought an action against the State challenging the Department's assessment. The circuit court entered a decree overruling the State's demurrer to the taxpayer's bill of complaint. The court affirmed the decree. Drawing upon judicial interpretations accorded to federal and state laws upon which Ala. Code tit. 51, § 390 (1940) was modeled, the court held that the Department usurped the legislature's authority by using a standard inconsistent with the statutory purpose of relieving taxpayers of the burden of double taxation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decree overruling the State's demurrer to the taxpayer's bill of complaint alleging that a formula used by the Department computing income taxes due the State from corporations also doing business in other states violated Alabama law.

 

841 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Ex parte Darnell


Nos. 6 Div. 698, 744


Supreme Court of Alabama


262 Ala. 71; 76 So. 2d 770; 1954 Ala. LEXIS 553



October 28, 1954 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 13, 1955.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Certiorari was granted from a decision of the Circuit Court of Jefferson County (Alabama), which covered all the proceedings in the cause between defendant employee and plaintiff county personnel director in which the employee was reinstated after being dismissed on the ground that the director was not authorized to prefer charges. The circuit court then held that the employee had forfeited his job by qualifying as a candidate for public office.


OVERVIEW: The employee had been dismissed for conduct unbecoming a public service employee. On appeal from the dismissal to the circuit court, it was argued that the circuit court had no right to hear the case de novo and substitute its own judgment for that of the director. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The circuit court referred to the many statutes in Alabama that provided for de novo trial in the circuit court on appeal from an order of an administrative board. Trial de novo was not synonymous with original jurisdiction, and, as such, there was no violation of Ala. Const. § 143 (1901). Nor was the appeal de novo violative of Ala. Const. §§ 42, 43 because the legislature could invest any person with powers of a judicial nature and could likewise authorize an appeal de novo from such proceedings to the circuit court. Thus, the circuit court had jurisdiction of the appeal from the order of the director. Further, the director could prefer charges against the employee under Ala. Code tit. 62, § 330(32) (1940). The court noted finally that through the employee's qualification for a public office, he had forfeited his position pursuant to Ala. Code tit. 62, § 330(45).


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the decree of the circuit court, which had held, in part, that the director was not authorized to prefer charges against the employee.

 

842 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Gayle v. Edwards


No. 3 Div. 659


Supreme Court of Alabama


261 Ala. 84; 72 So. 2d 848; 1954 Ala. LEXIS 579



May 20, 1954 



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city commissioners challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court of Montgomery County (Alabama), which ruled in favor of appellee widow and granted her payment for the period of her widowhood pursuant to Ala. Code §. § 528(3) (Cum. Pocket Part 1940). The commissioners claimed that the statute violated Ala. Const. art. IV, § 45 insofar as it was retroactive because the retroactive feature was not contained in its title.


OVERVIEW: The widow's deceased husband had been employed by the city's fire department and died in the line of duty. The trial court awarded her widow's benefits based on the retroactive provision contained within the body of Ala. Code §. § 528(3). The court, in considering the commissioners' appeal and reversing the judgment, noted that Ala. Const. art. IV, § 45 required that each law contained one subject, which was clearly expressed in its title. The purposes behind the constitutional provision were to prevent passage of accurate bills and to fairly apprise the people of legislation that was under consideration. Accordingly, the court agreed with the commissioners that Ala. Code §. § 528(3) violated the constitutional mandate because the retroactive feature of the act was not clearly expressed in its title, nor was it even suggested. Insofar as the retroactive feature of the statute was concerned, the law was unconstitutional and void.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the matter.

 

843 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Bozeman v. Hester


No. 8 Div. 755


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


260 Ala. 566; 72 So. 2d 61; 1954 Ala. LEXIS 348



April 15, 1954 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] The Act referred to in the opinion is as follows:

"Act No. 227 S. 226-Todd

"An Act

"Relating to Colbert County; abolishing the office of County Superintendent of Education, and creating the office of County Commissioner of Public Schools in lieu thereof; providing for the election, term of office, duties and powers, and compensation of the County Commissioner of Public Schools, and conferring upon the Commissioner the powers, duties, and functions of the County School Building Commission.

"Be It Enacted by the Legislature of Alabama:

"Section 1. The office of County Superintendent of Education in Colbert County is hereby abolished; and there is hereby created in lieu thereof the office of County Commissioner of Public Schools.

"Section 2. Immediately upon the effective date of this Act, the Governor shall appoint a Commissioner of Public Schools, who shall hold office until July 1, 1957. A Commissioner of Public Schools for Colbert County shall be elected by the qualified electorate of Colbert County at the general election to be held in November, 1956, and every four years thereafter. He shall take office on the first day of July next succeeding the election.  [***2]

"Section 3. The Commissioner of Public Schools shall have the same power and authority, and shall perform the same duties and functions now required by law to be performed by the Superintendent of Education and the County School Building Commission of Colbert County created by Act No. 702, approved September 5, 1951 (General Acts of Alabama, 1951 [p. 1210]).

"Section 4. The Commissioner of Public Schools shall receive the same salary and compensation now provided by law for the County Superintendent of Education of Colbert County.

"Section 5. This Act shall become effective immediately upon its passage and approval by the Governor, or upon its otherwise becoming a law."




DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator county superintendent of education appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Colbert County (Alabama), which ruled in favor of defendant county commissioner of public schools in the superintendent's quo warranto action challenging the commissioner's right to hold the office to which he was appointed pursuant to Act 227, Acts of Alabama 1953, p. 293.


OVERVIEW: Act 227 sought to abolish the superintendent's position and create in lieu thereof the commissioner's position. The superintendent asserted that the Act was unconstitutional and that the commissioner was unlawfully appointed to his position. The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment in favor of the commissioner. The Act did not violate Ala. Const. § 105 as that section did not prohibit the passage of local laws merely because the local law was different and changed the status of an elected position. Further, the Act did not violate Ala. Const. § 175 because it did not improperly abridge the term of office of the superintendent and did not authorize material and significant new duties and powers of office. While the title of the Act abolished the superintendent's office and created the commissioner's office, this did not mean that it had two subjects within the meaning of Ala. Const. § 45, and the subject was clearly expressed in the title. Thus, the circuit court correctly found that the Act was not unconstitutional, and judgment for the commissioner was warranted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

854 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


LANE v. McFADYEN


1 Div. 538.


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


259 Ala. 205; 66 So. 2d 83; 1953 Ala. LEXIS 26



May 21, 1953, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 30, 1953.


PRIOR HISTORY: Grocer brought suit in equity against Chief of Police of the City of Mobile and others to enjoin enforcement of reference ordinance based on the Sunday Closing Law, Code 1940, Tit. 14, § 420. The Circuit Court of Mobile County, Claude A. Grayson, J., entered a decree sustaining a demurrer to the bill, and the grocer appealed. The Supreme Court, Lawson, J., held that the Sunday Closing Law is not unconstitutional on ground that it violates the equal protection Clauses of the state and federal constitution.

Decree affirmed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Mobile County (Alabama) entered a decree sustaining a demurrer filed by appellee police officials in appellant grocer's action to enjoin enforcement of an ordinance based on a Sunday Closing Law. The grocer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The grocer contended that Ala. Code tit. 14, § 420 (1940), which prohibited merchants and shopkeepers from keeping an open store on Sundays, was unconstitutional. The grocer filed a bill seeking to enjoin the officials from enforcing a municipality's ordinance based upon the statute. The officials filed a demurrer, which the trial court sustained. On appeal, the grocer argued that the statute, as applied to him and others similarly situated, was so arbitrary and discriminatory as to be violative of the equal protection clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and the Alabama constitution. The court found that the grocer did not claim that the statute violated constitutional provisions in regard to religious liberty and freedom of conscience. The court also found that the only class of persons prohibited from carrying on business on Sunday was merchants and shopkeepers and they are only prohibited from keeping "open store." The court determined that the classification of "merchants or shopkeepers" was not an unreasonable classification. Therefore, the court held that the demurrer to his bill seeking an injunction was properly sustained.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment sustaining a demurrer filed by the officials in the grocer's action to enjoin enforcement of an ordinance.

856 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Atkins v. Curtis


6 Div. 452.


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


259 Ala. 311; 66 So. 2d 455; 1953 Ala. LEXIS 206



May 14, 1953, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 30, 1953.



DISPOSITION: Reversed, rendered and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, state officials, sought review of the judgment of the trial court (Alabama) which overruled the demurrer to the bill of complaint filed by appellee applicant seeking a declaratory judgment that 1951 Ala. Acts 694 was null, void, and unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: 1951 Ala. Acts 694 (Act) supplemented the benefits provided for in state law and provided for the poor who were in need of state aid. Under the Act, it was necessary for the county unit having jurisdiction to investigate the financial condition of the applicant's living husband, wife, father, mother, son, or daughter, including their income, and then fix each such relative's liability for contribution to the applicant's support. The applicant's bill sought a decree declaring the Act unconstitutional. The trial court overruled the state officials' demurrer to the bill. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that the demurrer should have been sustained. The Act did not violate Ala. Const. § 88 because there was no constitutional objection to the legislature creating a duty for family members to support indigents under its police power, that there was no fault in conferring jurisdiction in an equity court, and that it did not unconstitutionally bind persons outside the jurisdiction. The title was not so general and indefinite as to violate Ala. Const. § 45. The Act did not violate Ala. Const. § 23 by taking property for a private use as it only fixed a liability.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded, holding that the state officials' demurrer to the applicant's bill for a declaratory judgment should have been sustained.

Ex parte Joiner


6 Div. 462.


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


258 Ala. 466; 64 So. 2d 48; 1953 Ala. LEXIS 104



March 13, 1953, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Mandamus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a claimant as to the title on a certain parcel of property, sought a writ of mandamus regarding the decision to deny her motion to strike respondent trustee's application to order the claimant to appear and answer questions.


OVERVIEW: The claimant brought an action for quiet title to certain property against the trustee. The trustee presented the claimant with interrogatories, which she failed to answer. The trustee filed a motion for judgment on his answer. The claimant filed her answers and the trial court judge ordered her to appear for examination. The claimant filed a motion to set aside the order, which was denied. The claimant then filed a writ of mandamus. The claimant argued that her testimony could not be compelled because at the time of the order she was not an adverse party to the trustee. The court treated the claimant as an adverse party for the purpose of her motion. The court held that Ala. Code tit. 7, § 491 (1940) was intended to authorize the trial court to order the testimony of any party, whether they were adverse or not. The court stated that testimony could only be ordered after adequate notice was given and the court concluded that the claimant had adequate notice.


OUTCOME: The court denied the claimant's motion for writ of mandamus regarding the trial court's decision to order the claimant to appear and answer questions.

Klibanoff v. Tri-Cities Retail Clerks' Union


8 Div. 690.


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


258 Ala. 479; 64 So. 2d 393; 1953 Ala. LEXIS 107; 32 L.R.R.M. 2036; 23 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P67,468



March 13, 1953, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Sections 376, 383, 384, 385 and 390, Title 26 of the Code of 1940, are as follows:

"§ 376. The right to live involves the right to work. The public and working men and women must be protected. The activities of labor organizations affect the social and economic conditions of the state and the welfare of its citizens. It is declared to be the policy of this state, in the exercise of its police power and in the protection of the public interest, to promote voluntary and peaceful settlement and adjustment of labor disputes and to regulate the activities and affairs of labor organizations, their officers, agents, and other representatives in the manner and to the extent hereinafter provided".

"§ 383. Every person shall be free to join or to refrain from joining any labor organization except as otherwise provided in section 391 of this title, and in the exercise of such freedom shall be free from interference by force, coercion or intimidation, or by threats of force or coercion, or by intimidation of or injury to his family".

"§ 384. It shall be unlawful for any person by the use of force or violence, or the threat of the use of force or violence, to prevent or to attempt [***2] to prevent any person from engaging in any lawful vocation within this state."

"§ 385. It shall be unlawful for any person acting in concert with one or more other persons, to assemble at or near any place of employment in this state and by force or violence or threat thereof prevent or attempt to prevent any person from engaging in any lawful vocation, or for any person acting either by himself, or as a member of any group or organization or acting in concert with one or more other persons, to promote, encourage or aid in any such unlawful assemblage".

"§ 390. It shall be unlawful for any labor organization, any labor organizer, any officer, agent, representative or member of any labor organization, or any other person, to collect, receive or demand, directly or indirectly from any person, any fee, assessment, or sum of money whatsoever, as a work permit or as a condition for the privilege of work; provided, however, this shall not prevent the collection of initiation fees or dues."



DISPOSITION: Reversed, rendered and remanded.

8 Div. 644.

861 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Ex parte Dozier


No. 1 Div. 455


Supreme Court of Alabama


262 Ala. 197; 77 So. 2d 903; 1953 Ala. LEXIS 18



January 19, 1953 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 24, 1955.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and rendered discharging defendant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner attorney sought review of the decision of the Board of Commissioners of the State Bar (Alabama) to disbar the attorney from the practice of law for failing to do work which he had been retained to do by a client.


OVERVIEW: The attorney contended that the three year statute of limitations to disbar an attorney, Ala. Code tit. 7, § 24 was applicable. The Board contended that § 24 was unconstitutional because it infringed upon judicial power. The court was not willing to hold that § 24 was not an effective statute of limitations as to proceedings begun and conducted upon Ala. Code tit. 46, § 33. It was competent for the legislature to prescribe grounds for disbarment so long as it did not interfere with the court's inherent power to determine who could practice before it. The reprehensible conduct of the attorney, if there was any, was in receiving the fee and accepting employment to contest a will by one not authorized to do so, and at a time not allowed by law, and writing her that it was not too late when he knew it was too late. The court reversed the disbarment, finding that the inquiry in the attorney's mind evidenced by his correspondence was that there could be produced evidence to support a bill in the nature of a bill of review for fraud or to invoke, as he thought, the inherent power of the probate court. Thus, disbarment proceedings were barred by the statute of limitations.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the attorney's disbarment from the practice of law.

 

862 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Mullis v. Mathews


4 Div. 701.


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


259 Ala. 125; 66 So. 2d 105; 1953 Ala. LEXIS 275



January 19, 1953, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] On the Merits June 13, 1953.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Informant taxpayers brought an impeachment proceeding in their own behalf and in the name of the State of Alabama on their relation, wherein they averred in twenty-four specifications that respondent county sheriff was guilty of willful neglect of duty.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers sought to impeach the sheriff for willful neglect of duty under the apparent authority of Ala. Code §§ 181, 182 (1940). The court held that the sheriff was not guilty of willful neglect. The court held that the five resident taxpayers were permitted to institute an impeachment suit upon complying with Ala. Const. art. 7, §§ 181 and 182, and that the information required to be filed in doing so could be upon their relation, as authorized by § 180. The court held that private counsel could prosecute the action. The court found that the county solicitor advised the sheriff that pinball machines were not gambling devices and could be possessed and operated without violating the laws as long as there was not a payout for a successful score. The court found that the sheriff acted and relied upon the solicitor's advice in failing to take action against the owners or operators of the machines. The court held that the advice was both given and acted upon in good faith. The court held that the reliance upon the advice of the solicitor did not justify his conviction of willful neglect of duty in failing to move against the pinball machines or their owners or operators.


OUTCOME: The court held that the sheriff was not guilty of willful neglect and the taxpayers were authorized to bring an impeachment suit.

 

863 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Cunningham v. Cherokee County


7 Div. 167.


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


258 Ala. 30; 61 So. 2d 123; 1952 Ala. LEXIS 52



October 23, 1952, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In appellee county's action for relief regarding the duty of appellant, a clerk of the county law and equity court, to collect a trial tax and stenographers' fees, the clerk filed a cross-bill claiming that he had collected the fees and was entitled to be paid the sum he collected. The circuit court (Alabama) sustained the county's demurrer to part of the clerk's cross-bill, and the clerk appealed the circuit court's decision.


OVERVIEW: The county filed an action against the clerk for relief regarding the clerk's duty to collect certain fees. The clerk filed a cross-bill asserting he was entitled to the sum of fees he collected. The circuit court sustained the county's demurrer to part of the cross-bill and overruled the county's other demurrers to the cross-bill. The clerk appealed, and the court affirmed in part and remanded. In light of local acts, the clerk was not entitled to collect costs and fees of courts for his own use. It was his duty to collect them and to pay the money into the treasury of the county. He was without right to have judgment or decree for the sum. The claim of the clerk for nonpayment of his salary, a claim triable in a civil action at law, could not be the subject of a cross-bill, unless the legal right asserted arose out of the subject matter of the original bill. Since the case was still pending on the original bill and answer and cross-bill, the court deemed it proper to affirm the ruling on the demurrer to the disputed part of the cross-bill and to remand for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's decision on the disputed part of the cross-bill and remanded for further proceedings on the original bill and the remainder of the cross-bill.

866 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. State


5 Div. 537.


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


258 Ala. 86; 61 So. 2d 707; 1952 Ala. LEXIS 332



June 26, 1952, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 6, 1952.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded to the Court of Appeals.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a probate judge, sought review of a judgment from the Court of Appeals (Alabama), which upheld a decision that convicted defendant of embezzlement under Ala. Code tit. 14, § 127 after defendant issued a warrant on the county treasurer for the payment of a personal claim.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a probate judge, filed a claim against the county for fees in connection with defendant's duties and caused the clerk of the court of county commissioners to draw a warrant against county funds for the amount of the claim. Thereafter, the warrant was delivered to defendant and credited to defendant's account at a local bank. Consequently, defendant was convicted of embezzlement under § 127, and after the appeals court upheld the conviction, defendant sought review. Upon review, the court initially rejected defendant's contention that § 127 required intent to defraud. The court also held that § 127's use of the word "converted" required a conversion be knowingly done and that the indictment and the jury instructions had correctly conveyed this requirement. However, the court held defendant could not be guilty of embezzlement under the indictment because defendant had not been entrusted by law with the disbursement of county funds. In so holding, the court noted that the issuance of warrants for the payment of claims was a ministerial duty imposed on defendant, in the performance of which defendant had no discretion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment which upheld a decision that convicted defendant of embezzlement after defendant issued a warrant on the county treasurer for the payment of a personal claim.

Moses v. Tarwater

April 10, 1952, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 15, 1952.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner mental patient sought review of an order of a circuit court (Alabama), which denied his habeas corpus petition and remanded him to the custody of respondent superintendent of a state mental institution.


OVERVIEW: A jury had found that petitioner was insane and he was committed. Petitioner argued that Ala. Code tit. 45, §§ 208 and 210 were an unconstitutional violation of due process because Ala. Code tit. 45, § 210 left the right of petitioner to notice and hearing to the discretion of a probate judge. On appeal, the court held that it would not reach the issue of the constitutionality of Ala. Code tit. 45, §§ 208 and 210 because it was not essential to the decision of the case where the jury found that petitioner was insane, and the probate judge found that the evidence overwhelmingly supported the jury verdict.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

869 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Board of Educ. v. Kennedy


2 Div. 296.


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


256 Ala. 478; 55 So. 2d 511; 1951 Ala. LEXIS 154



December 6, 1951, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Board of Education challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Choctaw County, Alabama, which overruled its motion for a rehearing and that granted appellee tenured principal's application for a writ of mandamus to compel the Board to reinstate him to his former position.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court overruled the Board's motion for a rehearing and granted the principal's petition for a writ of mandamus to compel the Board to reinstate him from the position from which they removed him based on the charges that were brought against him. The court affirmed that grant, reasoning that the record showed that the circuit court was justified in holding that any action of the Board in sustaining the charges that were brought against the principal was arbitrarily unjust. The court held there was no need to remand the action to the Board for a hearing because the parties presented all of the evidence that they wished to. The court also concluded that the legislature clearly could provide for a review by mandamus to determine if the Board's action complied with the Teacher Tenure Law, Ala. Code § 351 et seq. (1940), and if such action was arbitrarily unjust. The court further noted that the undisputed testimony showed that, rather than embezzling the school's funds, the principal had made an unintentional and honest mistake that he rectified on its discovery, which occurred before a complaint was filed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of the principal's request for a writ of mandamus that sought to require the Board to reinstate him to his position.
