871 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


City of Cullman v. Farmers Mktg. & Exch. Ass'n


6 Div. 78.


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


256 Ala. 315; 54 So. 2d 586; 1951 Ala. LEXIS 83



October 18, 1951, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a judgment by the trial court (Alabama), which sustained a demurrer by appellee marketing association to the city's bill in equity to enforce a privilege license levied on the association as a retail merchant.


OVERVIEW: The city adopted an ordinance levying a privilege license on retail merchants. The association, although engaged in retail sales in the city, refused to pay the license on the ground that it was exempt from it by the provisions of Ala. Code tit. 2, § 129 (1940). The city filed a bill in equity, claiming that § 129 was unconstitutional and violative of Ala. Const. § 221. The trial court entered judgment in favor of the association. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's decision. The court held that, under Ala. Code tit. 2, § 129 (1940), the state and its political subdivisions were treated alike, except that the state was permitted to collect a nominal permit fee for the purpose of defraying the expenses incident to the issuance of a permit. The purpose of Ala. Const. § 221 was to prevent the legislature from levying a license tax for the use of the state and at the same time relieve licensees from the payment of all other taxes of like kind to counties and municipalities. The court concluded that the city's bill failed to show that the association was delinquent in the payment of a privilege license and was, therefore, without equity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

872 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Kendrick v. State


6 Div. 9.


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


256 Ala. 206; 54 So. 2d 442; 1951 Ala. LEXIS 63



October 4, 1951, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county commissioners sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Jefferson County (Alabama), which granted the petition of appellee taxpayer, as relator for the State of Alabama, and issued a peremptory writ of mandamus ordering the commissioners to furnish and provide voting machines for use in all primary, special, and general elections in the county in accordance with Ala. Code tit. 17, art. 7 (1940).


OVERVIEW: A majority of the voters in the county had, nearly nine years earlier, voted to require the use of voting machines in the county. The action was brought to require the commissioners to install the voting machines as mandated by the voters. The court, in affirming the trial court's grant of mandamus, rejected the commissioners' numerous points of error. The court determined, among other things, that the citizen had standing to bring the petition in the name of the State and also found that the commissioners had a clear duty to provide the machines under the provisions of Ala. Code tit. 17, art. 7 (1940). The court also found that the commissioners failed to assert as a defense the fact that some of the voting places allegedly had fewer than the 100 voters required for application of the statute. In addition, the court found that the commissioners were not excused from their duty to provide the machines because of any irregularity in the prior election or the remoteness in time thereof. The court also found noted that the commissioners did not raise as a defense the constitutional barrier, under Ala. Const. § 224, that the county's debt prevented the procurement of the machines.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that issued a peremptory writ of mandamus ordering the commissioners to furnish and provide voting machines for use in elections held within the county.

 

873 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Jefferson County v. Birmingham


6 Div. 276.


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


256 Ala. 436; 55 So. 2d 196; 1951 Ala. LEXIS 144



October 4, 1951, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 23, 1951, 256 Ala. 436 at 441.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of an order from the a circuit court in equity (Alabama), which denied its action against appellee city for declaratory relief that City of Birmingham (Alabama) Gen. City Code § 1602 did not prohibit the county from constructing a sewage treatment plant in the city's residential districts and which further denied injunctive relief to prohibit the city from enforcing § 1602 against the county to prohibit the plant.


OVERVIEW: The county brought an action against the city for a declaratory judgment holding that § 1602 did not prohibit the county from constructing a sewage treatment plant in the city's residential districts and injunctive relief to prohibit the city from enforcing § 1602 against the county with respect to the construction or operation of the plant. The trial court denied the county's petition and it appealed. The court affirmed, finding that the proposed plant was neither a permitted use within the city's residential districts under § 1602 nor, by definition, an accessory use because the principal use was not permitted. The county's assertion that it proposed use of the subject property for a governmental function precluded application of the city's zoning code was without merit because Ala. Code tit. 62, §§ 710, 711, 712 (1940) made full provision for the enforcement of the city's zoning ordinance, subject only to the limitation that such ordinance be comprehensive in scope and purpose and not in conflict with the laws of the state or the state and federal constitutions. The court concluded the city's zoning ordinance did not exceed its authority and was applicable to the county.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that denied declaratory and injunctive relief to the county.

 

874 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Hickman v. Mobile


1 Div. 436.


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


256 Ala. 141; 53 So. 2d 752; 1951 Ala. LEXIS 45



June 30, 1951, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] By reason of the fact that there are now sitting in the Supreme Court only six Justices and there being an equal division among them on questions material to the determination of the case, these facts were certified to the Governor, who thereupon appointed the Honorable Jack Crenshaw of Montgomery, a member of the bar of the Supreme Court, to sit as a Special Justice of said Court in the determination of said case. Code 1940, Tit. 13, § 15.



DISPOSITION: Reversed, rendered and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, city firefighters and police officers, sought review of the decision of an Alabama trial court, which granted the motion to dismiss filed by appellees, city, commissioners and governing board, and the chiefs of the police and fire departments, in the appellants' action to seeking to enjoin the enforcement of an ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The city passed an ordinance that prohibited any firemen or police officers employed by the city from belonging to a labor union. Appellants sought to enjoin the ordinance, alleging that it violated due process and would result in discharge, which would deny the benefits accruing to the appellees from their years of services, retirement, and other employment contract provisions. The trial granted appellees' motion to dismiss. On appeal, the court reversed, rendered, and remanded. The court held that the ordinance terminated an appellant's employment without notice, trial, or right to heard and appeal, which was contrary to 1939 Ala. Acts 470 § 22 of the Alabama Civil Service Act (Act), 1939 Ala. Acts 470, which provided for a procedure for dismissal of classified employees. The court, therefore, concluded that the ordinance ipso facto was inconsistent with state law and ultra vires the power of the board of commissioners. The court also concluded that the provisions of the Act did not provide any authority for a city's governing body to dismiss employees because the act contemplated administrative or ministerial action.


OUTCOME: The court reversed, rendered, and remanded the trial court's grant of appellee's motion to dismiss in appellants' action challenging the validity of a city ordinance.

 

875 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Paramount-Richards Theatres, Inc. v. State


3 Div. 564.


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


256 Ala. 515; 55 So. 2d 812; 1951 Ala. LEXIS 157



June 28, 1951, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 10, 1952.


PRIOR HISTORY: From an assessment for use taxes made by the State Department of Revenue Paramount-Richards Theatres, Inc. appealed to the Circuit Court of Montgomery County and filed a bill of complaint. The Circuit Court rendered a final decree affirming the assessment after sustaining a demurrer to the bill as amended and the taxpayer appeals.

The amended bill is in pertinent part as follows:

"During the period or periods involved the taxpayer was engaged in the business of operating motion picture theatres at Mobile, Alabama. In computing the assessment against the taxpayer, the State Department of Revenue erroneously and illegally included therein the amounts paid by the taxpayer under license agreement for exhibition of moving picture films and trailer films in connection therewith, which license agreements were made between taxpayer and various motion picture producers located outside the State of Alabama, under which agreements such films and trailers were shipped in interstate commerce by said producers to taxpayer at Mobile, Alabama, and pursuant to which agreements said films and trailers were exhibited or used by taxpayer in the conduct of [***2] said moving picture theatres; after which said films and trailers were returned by taxpayer to said producers by shipments thereof made in interstate commerce from Mobile, Alabama, to the points outside the State of Alabama from which the same were shipped, as required under terms of the agreements relating thereto.

"(5) Said films and trailers hereinabove mentioned were shipped in interstate commerce to the taxpayer under bona fide license agreements under which the taxpayer was given no right or option to purchase said films or trailers, but the title to which was retained by the producers; and said agreements were not used for the purpose of effecting any sale of said films or trailers to taxpayer; nor were said films or trailers sold or agreed to be sold by the producers to said taxpayer; that said transactions did not involve, in fact or in law, a sale or agreement to sell said films or trailers to taxpayer; that neither said films nor trailers were in fact or in law sold to taxpayer or purchased by taxpayer; that there was no purchase of said films or trailers by taxpayer within the meaning of the Alabama Use Tax Act; and there was no sale to taxpayer or sales price based [***3] on a sale to taxpayer of said films or trailers within the meaning of the Alabama Use Tax Act; and that therefore said assessment is erroneous, illegal and excessive in the amount and to the extent of $ 10,039.43, and interest thereon.

"(6) That each of the license agreements hereinabove mentioned and referred to were executed in writing; that said contracts or agreements, termed exhibition contracts or license agreements, were between various producers as distributors and the taxpayer as exhibitor, a copy of the form of which contracts or agreements is attached hereto, marked Exhibit 'A' and made a part of this bill of complaint as fully and particularly as if herein set out in full; that each of said agreements was substantially of like tenor and effect; that in each of said license agreements the name or title of the film was designated and the number of consecutive days the lessee or exhibitor was permitted to exhibit the pictures produced by the use of said films was designated and was limited to the day or days said films were permitted to be used for such purpose and the license fee or minimum guaranteed amount to be paid for such use or exhibition was in each instance [***4] specified with respect to the film, and was in each instance limited to a specific date or dates, usually one day or a series of several days, not extending over a period of more than a few days; and under the terms of said agreement in each instance the taxpayer as exhibitor was required to return said films to the producer, at a point outside of the State of Alabama, from which point said film had been shipped by the producer to taxpayer in interstate commerce pursuant to the terms of said agreement; that each of said producers in license agreements involved in this proceeding were non-residents of the State of Alabama; that each of said license agreements when executed by taxpayer were submitted to said non-resident producers for their acceptance, and upon the acceptance of such agreements and pursuant thereto, the particular photoplay, or trailer film, designated or described in said license agreement was shipped by said non-resident producer to taxpayer as exhibitor and upon the exhibition of said film for the day or days specified with respect thereto, the same was immediately shipped by the taxpayer, in interstate commerce, to said non-resident producer beyond or outside of [***5] the State of Alabama; that the amount specified to be paid by the taxpayer to the producers under said agreements was in each instance specified in the terms of said agreement, or the basis for the determination of such amounts was therein specified, as a minimum guaranteed license fee for the exhibition of each film, and in some instances involved the payment of a percentage of the gross receipts derived from the exhibition of such film; that the films were shipped to taxpayer separately, constituting single transactions, and they were not shipped under any long-term agreement calling for any large quantity of film shipments to be delivered at regular intervals or to meet the needs of the taxpayer in the conduct of its business.

"(7) That prior to and during the period involved herein, all of the motion pictures exhibited by the taxpayer were produced and distributed in the following manner:

"(a) Motion picture producers either in California or New York engaged actors and technicians and purchased negative film stock, which negative stock is a strip of celluloid coated with an emulsion which when exposed to light changes from white to black. This negative stock is exposed [***6] through cameras and photographs scenes enacted by the actors and records contemporaneous sound. This negative stock, after being so exposed, is by the producer subjected to a developing process which fixes the photographic images so that they will not fade or change. This negative is not suitable for exhibition purposes, for light projecting through it will cause the images to appear in reverse on the screen, that is the portion of the screen which should be dark would be light and the portion which should be light would be dark.

"(b) This negative after development is run through a machine which causes the print to be made on raw stock, which raw stock is similar to the negative stock, except that on it the images on the negative are reversed and the print is suitable for projection. Each day during the period of six or more weeks devoted to photographing a motion picture photoplay, one print is made of all negatives which have been developed, which prints are called rushes. As photographing progresses certain rushes are selected and there is made up from those selected, by joining them together a working print. Upon completion of photographing those portions of the negative [***7] from which the rushes in the working print were printed, are assembled in consecutive order and joined together to make a master negative of approximately 7000 feet. In the case of every motion picture exhibited during the period involved in this suit, the negative of each such motion picture was in most instances delivered by the producer to an independent company which made and sold to the producer prints therefrom, or in a few instances, the producer purchased raw stock and in its own laboratory made such prints itself.

"(c) In all cases the producer made or purchased several hundred prints of each film or motion picture photoplay. In cases where the producer purchased these prints from an independent printing company, the producer paid to the State of California or to the State of New York, as the case may be, a sales tax at the rate of 2% upon the purchase price paid by the producer to the independent printing company. In cases in which the producer made its own prints, it purchased the positive stock from an independent film manufacturer and paid upon such purchase a sales tax to the State of New York or to the State of California, as the case may be, at the rate of 2% of [***8] the purchase price of such negative stock. In each case whether the print was purchased from the independent printing company or positive raw stock was purchased from an independent film manufacturer, the cost to the producer was approximately 1 1/2 [cents] per foot in the case of black and white motion picture photoplays, or for a picture photoplay of average length a total of $ 105.00, and approximately 5 [cents] per foot in the case of colored motion picture films, or for a picture photoplay of average length a total of $ 400.00.

"(d) The above mentioned sales of positive raw stock by film manufacturing companies or the finished positive prints by the independent film printing companies to the producer are the only sales made of the prints which were used by the taxpayer in its exhibition of motion pictures during the period involved herein; and each such sale constituted a sale at retail; that the producers were the last persons to whom the property in said films and trailers passed in the course of ownership; that such sales to the producers are not made for resale; that there were in fact no further or other sales of such prints, in that after said prints had been used [***9] by the various exhibitors, including the taxpayer, they were taken by the producer-owners thereof and by them destroyed in smelters for the recovery of the silver contained in the emulsion on said celluloid films.

"(e) The master negative, after its return to the producer-owner, was always retained by the producer-owner in California or in New York and was not shipped to any other state. This retention lasted in different cases for different periods of time, depending upon the popularity of the exhibition, and in the case of those motion picture photoplays which were not popular, the master negatives were by the producerowner destroyed after a period of years.

"(f) The only article of tangible property which has been received by taxpayer from the producer has been the positive print in the case of each motion picture photoplay exhibited by it. In no case has it ever received any master negative. In all cases the taxpayer maintained insurance against fire on the prints while in its possession at an average value of $ 105.00 for black and white and $ 400.00 for technicolor prints, which in every case represented the approximate actual value of the respective prints.

"(g)  [***10] In the event that the tax is measured upon the basis of the sales price of the only retail sale of the tangible property involved, it would in each case be substantially less than the tax assessed on the so-called rental of said films, since the last retail sale price was at the rate of approximately 1 1/2 [cents] per foot for black and white and 5 [cents] per foot for technicolor prints.

"(h) None of the amounts paid to the producer was actually considered by the parties to be either for the purchase or rental of tangible personal property in that the value, or the retail sale price, of the tangible personal property involved was negligible compared to the amount paid by the taxpayer to the producer for the right publicly to exhibit the motion picture photoplay for profit, which right was granted in the contracts between the producer and taxpayer (Exhibit 'A' hereto attached) and which right is not tangible personal property but a limited license under the copyright of the producer publicly to exhibit the motion picture for profit; that all of the motion picture photoplays, films and trailers shipped to the taxpayer under such license agreements had heretofore been duly copyrighted [***11] by the respective producers.

"(i) In each case of the motion picture photoplays exhibited by the taxpayer, the print, the only tangible personal property, was delivered to taxpayer by express from outside the State of Alabama and after being exhibited by taxpayer at one of its theatres in Alabama for a period of usually three days, said print was by taxpayer immediately redelivered by express to the producer's branch office outside of the State of Alabama.

"(j) Taxpayer does not now and never has acquired any ownership or any interest in any of the positive prints of motion picture photoplays exhibited by it during the period herein involved; and at all times after the producer purchased said print at retail as hereinabove averred, the producer has remained the owner of said print and said motion picture photoplay. It was provided in all agreements between the taxpayer and the producers that in the event any print should be lost, stolen, destroyed or injured in any way between the delivery and the return thereof by the taxpayer, the taxpayer should pay to the producer a sum equal to the cost of replacement thereof at the producers' exchange. Said agreement further provided [***12] that such payment should not transfer title to or any interest in such positive print to the taxpayer or any other party; and in all cases payments under such provision by taxpayer to producer have been at approximately 1 1/2 [cents] per foot for black and white and 5 [cents] per foot for technicolor of positive print injured or destroyed by taxpayer, which represents the retail sale price to the purchaser.

"(8) Taxpayer alleges that said assessment is erroneous, illegal and excessive for the following reasons or upon the following grounds, separately and severally, namely:

"(a) That said Alabama Use Tax Act should not be construed as imposing a use tax upon or with respect to the amounts paid by the taxpayer for the privilege of using or exhibiting films, trailers or advertising matter in the conduct of its moving picture show business, under the facts and circumstances as hereinabove alleged, for the reason that under the terms and provisions of the Alabama Sales Tax Act a tax of 2% of the gross receipts derived from the exhibition of said films, trailers and advertising matter in the conduct of said business is imposed upon taxpayer, and the imposition of such use [***13] tax would constitute an additional intermediary tax, contrary to the true meaning and intent of said statute, and would lead to a construction that would make the levy of such use tax a discriminatory tax against interstate commerce contrary to Article 1, Section 8, Clause 3 of the Constitution of the United States, and would deny to taxpayer the equal protection of the law or deprive taxpayer of property without due process of law, contrary to the Fourteenth Amendment to the Constitution of the United States.

"(b) That the exhibition of said motion pictures exhibited under and by virtue of said contracts constituted taxpayer's sole stock in trade and the gross receipts of its business (except incidental sales of popcorn, candy and refreshments, upon which sales taxes have been duly paid) were derived solely from admission prices charged for the privilege of observing the exhibition; that upon the gross receipts of said business so derived a tax amounting to two per centum was levied pursuant to Code of Alabama 1940, Title 51, Section 753(b), which has been paid.

"(c) The amounts paid by the taxpayer to the producers under said license agreements or exhibition contracts were [***14] not for the rental or purchase of tangible personal property in that the value of, or the retail sale price, of the tangible personal property involved was negligible compared to the amount paid by the taxpayer to the producer for the right publicly to exhibit the motion picture photoplay for profit, which right was granted in the contracts between the producer and taxpayer (Exhibit A hereto attached) and which right is not tangible personal property but a limited license under the copyright of the producer publicly to exhibit the motion pictures for profit.

"(d) The amount of the assessment against taxpayer is excessive in that the tax measured upon the basis of the sales price of the only retail sale of the tangible property involved is substantially less than the tax assessed in this case on the so called rental of said films.

"(e) The amount of the assessment against taxpayer is excessive in that the sales price of the retail sale of the tangible property involved, namely the positive prints, to the producers as hereinabove averred represents the full retail sales price of said tangible personal property, and all amounts in excess thereof paid by the taxpayer to the producers [***15] were not for rental or purchase of tangible personal property but that the value, or the retail price, of the tangible personal property involved was negligible compared to the amount paid by the taxpayer to the producer for the right publicly to exhibit the motion picture photoplay for profit, which right was granted in the contracts between the producer and taxpayer (Exhibit A hereto attached) and which right is not tangible personal property but a limited license under the copyright of the producer publicly to exhibit the motion picture for profit.

"(9) Taxpayer alleges that the tax imposed by said statute is discriminatory against interstate commerce and therefore in conflict with Article 1, Section 8, Clause 3 of the Constitution of the United States in that it unduly burdens interstate commerce because there is exempted from said tax property the gross proceeds of sale of which are required to be included in the measure of the tax imposed by the provisions of Article 10 of Chapter 20, of Title 51 of the 1940 Code of Alabama, but there is not exempted from said tax property the gross proceeds of sale of which have been taxed by some State other than Alabama, and in this case [***16] in each instance the gross proceeds of sale of the films or trailers exhibited by taxpayer during the period involved herein had in fact been subjected to sales tax of the State of California and of the State of New York at the rate of 2% thereof, which tax had been paid; that therefore interstate and intrastate business did not reach the markets on identical terms, so far as the effect of the state taxes is concerned; that the cumulative effect of both taxes is discriminatorily burdensome on interstate commerce; and further that said assessment also deprives taxpayer of property without due process of law contrary to the Fourteenth Amendment of the Constitution of the United States.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Montgomery County (Alabama), which rendered a final decree affirming an assessment for use taxes made by appellee Department of Revenue pursuant to the Use Tax Act, specifically Ala. Code §§ 51-787 to 51-789 (1940).


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer operated motion picture theaters. The Department of Revenue included in its assessment under the Use Tax Act, specifically Ala. Code §§ 51-787 to 51-789 (1940), the amounts paid by the taxpayer under license agreements that were made with producers located outside the state. The trial court entered a final decree affirming the assessment for use tax and rendered judgment against the taxpayer. Construing the Use Tax Act and the Sales Tax Act in pari materia, the court reversed, holding that because the taxpayer's business was specifically and separately subjected to a tax under the Sales Tax Act on its entire gross receipts of its business, there was no reason to assume that the legislature intended also to tax under the Use Tax Act the license fees paid by the taxpayer for the privilege of exhibiting the photoplays. The Use Tax Act specifically exempted from the use tax any and all property purchased subjected to the sales tax and each and every incident or activity specifically subjected to the sales tax.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court and held that the taxpayer was not liable for the use tax assessed.

 

876 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Prichard v. Hawkins


1 Div. 372.


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


255 Ala. 676; 53 So. 2d 378; 1951 Ala. LEXIS 6



May 10, 1951, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Reversed, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After remand, defendant city appealed the judgment of a trial court (Alabama), which found in favor of plaintiff filling station in the filling station's action to declare an ordinance that imposed a license tax on gasoline unconstitutional. The city argued that the trial court erred in sustaining the filling station's demurrer to the city's plea in abatement that the filling station was not entitled to a refund.


OVERVIEW: The city enacted an ordinance that levied a license tax on gasoline sold within the city's jurisdiction. The filling station added the amount of the tax to the gasoline that it sold and filed an action against the city for refund of the money paid. The filling station claimed that the ordinance was unconstitutional and void as a revenue measure. A jury returned a verdict for the city, and the trial court overruled the filling station's motion for a new trial. The filling station appealed, and the court reversed because the trial court erred in presenting the question of the reasonableness of the ordinance to the jury. The ordinance as applied to the filling station was unreasonable and therefore void. On remand, there was a verdict and judgment for the filling station, and the trial court overruled the city's motion for a new trial. The city appealed, and the court reversed, holding that the trial court erred in refusing to permit the city to have its witness explain and contradict his answer to an interrogatory on whether the filling station had paid the tax. The witness's answer might have presented a question for the jury on whether the payment was made and a refund was due.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment that was in favor of the filling station, and it remanded the case to the trial court.

 

877 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


State v. Travelers Ins. Co.


3 Div. 586.


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


256 Ala. 61; 53 So. 2d 745; 1951 Ala. LEXIS 43



March 8, 1951, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 28, 1951.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the State of Alabama, challenged a decree overruling its demurrer to the bill of appellee taxpayer, an insurance company, filed in the Circuit Court (Alabama), in equity, to challenge an assessment made by the Department of Revenue for its annual franchise tax.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer had a home office in Connecticut. The taxpayer wrote life and accident insurance policies and collected premiums on those policies. The taxpayer sold those policies through independent agents who resided in Alabama. The insurance agents paid all expenses of maintaining an office and securing the policy. The taxpayer exercised no control over how the agents secured the policy. The taxpayer only had $ 1050 of capital in the state. It consisted of furniture and fixtures, typewriters, stationery, and other equipment located in an office in Birmingham. The Department imposed a franchise tax on the taxpayer using an allocation formula based on the premium income and the commissions paid to the agents. The court affirmed. The court held that the method that the Department used to assess the franchise tax was unconstitutional because Ala. Code tit. 51, § 348 (1940) only allowed the State to assess the tax based on the "capital employed" in the state. The statute did not permit the allocation that the Department used to compute the tax.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

880 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Mead v. Eagerton


3 Div. 581.


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


255 Ala. 66; 50 So. 2d 253; 1951 Ala. LEXIS 234



January 25, 1951, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Reversed, rendered and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of the decree of the trial court (Alabama), which sustained respondents', chief examiner of public accounts, the state treasurer, the state comptroller and the state auditor (state officials), demurrer to the taxpayer's request for a temporary and permanent injunction prohibiting the state officials from using state money to acquire the official bond of the chief examiner.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer sought injunctions to stop the state officials from using money from the State Insurance Fund to acquire the official bond of the chief examiner of public accounts, and to pay the premiums thereon. The trial court denied the requests for the injunctions and sustained the state officials' demurrer to the taxpayer's complaint. On appeal, the court reversed the decision of the trial court. And remanded the case and order the issuance of a temporary injunction against any further action by the state officials. The court held that the Surety Insurance Fund Act, Ala. Code art. 2, tit. 28, § 338 (1940) declared that its provisions would not be effective until the governor issued a proclamation. The governor did not have the authority to decide the effective date of an act duly passed. This was a delegation of legislative power in violation of Ala. Const. §§ 43 and 44. Ala. Code art. 2, tit. 28 § 329-338 was merely a method by which the state could set aside and hold for its purposes a certain amount of money, transferred from the state insurance fund for premiums on the official bonds required by law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court and remanded the case. The court issued a temporary injunction against the state officials prohibiting them from using and funds from the State Insurance Fund to pay premiums on official bonds.

 

881 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Nelson v. Donaldson


3 Div. 576.


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


255 Ala. 76; 50 So. 2d 244; 1951 Ala. LEXIS 235



January 25, 1951, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant neighbors sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court, Montgomery County (Alabama), which upheld an order from the city board of adjustment (board) directing the city building inspector to issue an apartment house building permit to appellee property owner. The board's order was grounded on the determination that the property owner was entitled to a variance from the terms of a new comprehensive zoning ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The new zoning ordinance restricted buildings in the property owner's district to single family dwellings, but the board determined that the property owner was entitled to a variance because of unnecessary hardship. The neighbors argued that the power given by Ala. Code tit. 37, § 781 (1940) to vary the effect of the zoning ordinance in specific cases did not include the power to authorize a nonconforming use. The court affirmed the judgment, rejecting the neighbors' assertion that the authority to permit variances was restricted to slight modifications such as height, area, and distance from boundaries. The court also held that § 781 did not unconstitutionally delegate legislative power to the board. Rather, § 781 gave the board the power to administer and execute the declared policy of the legislature within reasonably clear standards. The court concluded that the evidence supported the trial court's findings that the property owner had suffered an unnecessary hardship, that the spirit of the ordinance would not be violated by permitting construction of the apartment house, and that the construction would not depreciate surrounding properties.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, which upheld the board's order directing the city building inspector to issue a building permit to the property owner.

883 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mobile Stove & Pulley Mfg. Co.


1 Div. 378.


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


255 Ala. 617; 52 So. 2d 693; 1950 Ala. LEXIS 472



December 14, 1950, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Extended on Denial of Rehearing May 24, 1951, 255 Ala. 617 at 624.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed from the decision of the Circuit Court of Mobile County, which did not sustain the state department of revenue's assessment against defendant taxpayer of a deficiency of sales tax liability for the years 1943 through 1947 under 51 Ala. Code art. 10.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer was a corporation engaged in the business of operating an iron and steel foundry and machine shop. The taxpayer maintained a pattern shop or department for the manufacture of patterns to its customers' specifications. When customers inquired as to the cost of the pattern and the cost of the castings; the taxpayer quoted prices on the two articles separately. When the casting was shipped to that customer, he was billed separately for the pattern and the casting. The state determined a deficiency in the taxpayer's sales tax liability. The taxpayer appealed and the lower court did not sustain the deficiency. The state appealed and the court reversed and remanded. The court held that the evidence presented in the trial court was not sufficient to overcome the presumption of correctness of the assessment made by the state and that the trial court erred in vacating and annulling the state's assessment. The court found that the evidence did not show definitely that as to the patterns here involved, the purchaser and the taxpayer had any definite understanding or agreement that the patterns would definitely be moved outside of the state.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the decision of the lower court, which did not sustain the state department of revenue's assessment against the taxpayer for a deficiency of sales tax liability.

885 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Stokley v. State


2 Div. 283.


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


254 Ala. 534; 49 So. 2d 284; 1950 Ala. LEXIS 418



December 7, 1950, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Choctaw County (Alabama), which was entered in accord with a jury verdict convicting him of murder in the first degree. Defendant was sentenced to life in prison. The trial court also denied defendant's motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murdering an acquaintance, allegedly for striking the deceased in the head with a stick. There was evidence offered at trial that another person also hit the deceased with a stick. The court found that there was a conflict in the evidence as to whether defendant struck the deceased as charged in the indictment. That conflict, however, was an issue for the jury's determination. The court also found that the aiding and abetting statute, Ala. Code tit. 14, § 14 (1940), was constitutional. However, the court reversed the trial court's judgment, holding that the trial court erred in refusing to give defendant's requested instruction that if an offense was committed by defendant or another, without connection to a common object, the responsibility for that offense attached exclusively to its actual perpetrator.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the cause.

888 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. Smith


5 Div. 487.


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


254 Ala. 404; 48 So. 2d 546; 1950 Ala. LEXIS 388



October 26, 1950, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged a judgment from the Probate Court of Lee County (Alabama), which found him to be of unsound mind, and an order overruling his motion for new trial. Appellee son filed a motion to dismiss the appeal.


OVERVIEW: The son filed a petition of inquisition seeking to have his father declared to be of unsound mind. The son alleged that because of mental and physical senility and incompetence the father was incapable of governing himself and of conducting and managing his affairs. The jury rendered a verdict finding the allegations of the petition true and that the father was of unsound mind. The father's motion for a new trial was overruled. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court overruled the son's motion to dismiss the father's appeal. There was no requirement in Ala. Code tit. 7, § 786 (1940) that the appeal be taken by the father's newly appointed guardian. Because the object of the action was to determine whether the father was in fact a person of unsound mind, the father's counsel properly took the appeal on his behalf. It was for the jury to say whether the evidence reasonably satisfied them that the father was of unsound mind. The verdict was not clearly against the preponderance of the evidence. The father was not deprived of any constitutional rights in the proceedings. His property rights were not affected by the adjudication of insanity and Ala. Const. § 11 was not violated.


OUTCOME: The court overruled the son's motion to dismiss the father's appeal from a judgment declaring him to be of unsound mind. The court affirmed that the father was of unsound mind.

 

889 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Allinder v. Homewood


6 Div. 2.


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


254 Ala. 525; 49 So. 2d 108; 1950 Ala. LEXIS 417; 22 A.L.R.2d 763



October 26, 1950, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 7, 1950.


PRIOR HISTORY: The ordinance, insofar as it is attacked by the bill is as follows:

"Section 1. Every person, proprietor, owner, operator, lessee or his agent, conducting any tourist camp, tourist court, motor court or motel, in the city shall, at all times, keep and maintain at the main or central entrance or office thereof a book or register in which each and every person or patron occupying any room, or accommodations therein shall inscribe with ink or indelible pencil the name, age and home address of each and every patron or person occupying any such room or accommodations in any such place. Such book or register shall be signed at the main or central entrance or office of any such tourist camp, tourist court, motor court or motel, and not elsewhere on the premises, by each and every patron or person occupying any room or accommodations of any sort in any of the above-named places, and the proprietor, owner, operator or lessee of any such tourist camp, tourist court, motor court or motel, or his agent, shall thereupon write opposite such name so registered, the license number and make of automobile in which such patron or person traveled to such tourist [***2] camp, tourist court, motor court or motel, the date and hour of arrival and the room or quarters rented or assigned to such patron or person.

"Until all of the aforesaid entries have been made in such book or register at the main or central entrance or office of any such tourist camp, tourist court, motor court or motel, no patron or person shall occupy or be suffered, permitted or allowed to occupy privately any room, garage, driveway, or other accommodations in such tourist camp, tourist court, motor court or motel. When the patron, or occupant, of each room or accommodations so rented or occupied shall quit, surrender, or check out of same, it shall be the further duty of the proprietor of such tourist camp, tourist court, motor court or motel, or his agent, to enter the time of departure of said patron, or occupant, in such book or register opposite the name of such patron or occupant. The book or register of any such tourist camp, tourist court, motor court, or motel, shall be open to inspection at all times by the chief of police, or any police officer of said city, on duty at the time of any such inspection, for a period of two years after the making of each entry in such [***3] book or register.

"Section 2. It shall be unlawful for any person or occupant * * * to occupy any room, or other accommodations in such place, with a member of the opposite sex other than the lawfully wedded spouse or minor child of such person, or occupant, or to have sexual intercourse in such tourist camp, tourist court, motor court or motel with any person other than the lawfully wedded spouse of said person, or occupant.

"Section 4. It shall be unlawful for any proprietor, or any servant, agent, employee or lessee of any proprietor of any tourist camp, tourist court, motor court or motel, to rent, lease or let, or permit to be used, any room or other accommodations, in any such tourist camp, tourist court, motor court or motel, more than once between the hours of nine o'clock in the evening and six o'clock in the morning of the next or succeeding day to any person or occupant, and no room, or accommodations, in any such place shall be rented, leased, let or permitted to be used by any person, or occupant, for any period of time less than twelve hours in any consecutive period of time.

"Section 6. It shall be the duty of the proprietor, owner, operator or lessee [***4] or his agent, of any tourist camp, tourist court, motor court or motel, to keep and preserve the book or register, in which the entries required by section 1 hereof to be made therein for a period of two years from the date of each such entry and to keep the same available and open at all times during such period of time for inspection by the chief of police or any duly appointed police officer of said city on duty at the time of said inspection."

Appellant's assignments of error are that the trial court erred in refusing appellant a temporary injunction enjoining and restraining:

First, that provision in section 1 of said alleged ordinance No. 334 requiring the appellant or his agent to write opposite such name so registered the license number and make of automobile in which such person or patron traveled to such tourist court, the date and hour of arrival and the room or quarters rented or assigned to such patron or person.

Second, that provision in section 1 of said alleged Ordinance No. 334 purporting to make the book or register mentioned therein open to inspection at all times by the chief of police or any police officer of the City of Homewood, Alabama, on duty [***5] at the time of any such inspection for a period of two years after the making of each entry in said book or register.

Third, that part of section 2 of said alleged Ordinance No. 334 purporting to make it unlawful for any person or occupant of any room or accommodation in appellant's tourist court to have sexual intercourse in such tourist court with any person other than the lawfully wedded spouse of said person or occupant.

Fourth, that provision in section 6 of the said alleged Ordinance No. 334 purporting to make it the duty of the appellant or his agent to keep and preserve the book or register referred to in section 1 of said alleged ordinance for a period of two years from the date of each entry and to keep the same available and open at all times during such period of time for inspection by the chief of police or any duly appointed police officer of the City of Homewood on duty at the time of said inspection.

Appellee's cross-assignments are that the trial court erred in granting a temporary injunction enjoining and restraining the appellee, City of Homewood, from enforcing:

First, that provision in section 1 of said ordinance No. 334 which requires each [***6] person conducting a tourist court in said county to at all times keep and maintain in the main or central entrance or office thereof a book or register in which each and every person or patron occupying any room or accommodation therein shall inscribe in ink or indelible pencil the name, age and home address of each and every patron or person occupying any such room or accommodation in any such place.

Second, that provision in section 1 of said ordinance No. 334 requiring such book or register to be signed at the main or central entrance or office of the tourist court and not elsewhere on the premises of each and every person or patron occupying any room or accommodation of any sort in said tourist court.

Third, that provision in section 1 of Ordinance No. 334 making it unlawful for any patron to occupy or to be suffered, permitted or allowed to occupy privately any room, garage, driveway or other accommodation in complainant's tourist court until the entries allegedly required by said section 1 have been made in the book or register at the main or central entrance or office of complainant's tourist court.

Fourth, that provision in section 1 of Ordinance No. 334 which [***7] purports to make it the duty of complainant or his agent to enter the time of departure of each patron or occupant in such book or register opposite the name of each person or occupant.

Fifth, that provision in that part of section 2 of Ordinance No. 334 purporting to make it unlawful for any person to occupy any room or other accommodation in such place with a member of the opposite sex other than the lawfully wedded spouse or minor child of such person or occupant.

Sixth, that provision in that part of section 4 of Ordinance No. 334 purporting to make it unlawful for the complainant or his agent to rent, lease or let or permit to be used any room or other accommodation in his tourist court more than once between the hours of nine o'clock in the evening and six o'clock in the morning of the next or succeeding day.

Seventh, that provision in section 4 of Ordinance No. 334 purporting to make it unlawful to rent, lease, let or permit any room or accommodation in said tourist court to be used by any person or occupant for any period of time less than twelve hours in any specified period of time.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant motel owner and appellee city sought review of a decree of the trial court (Alabama), which granted in part and denied in part the motel owner's application for a temporary injunction with respect to Homewood, Ala., Ordinance 334.


OVERVIEW: The motel owner filed an action against the city to enjoin enforcement of an ordinance regulating motels. The trial court granted the motel owner a temporary injunction for part of the ordinance but denied a temporary injunction for the remaining portions. Both parties appealed the decree, and the court affirmed it. The court held that the city's right and authority regarding the ordinance rested upon its police power. The court found that the power contained in Ala. Code tit. 37, § 455, was broad enough to secure the object sought to be accomplished by the ordinance. The court noted that the ordinance was more restrictive than the state law regulating motor courts. The court held that it was not unreasonable, arbitrary, or oppressive to require the motel owner to keep a register of his guests showing the license number and make of automobiles and the date and hour of arrival. The court found that there were differences between hotels and tourist courts that justified regulations regarding one that were not needed for the other. The court held that the issues regarding where and how long the register was to be kept did not present questions that needed an immediate decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decree regarding the temporary injunction.

 

890 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


State v. Alabama Power Co.


3 Div. 569.


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


254 Ala. 327; 48 So. 2d 445; 1950 Ala. LEXIS 563



October 19, 1950, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant State of Alabama challenged a ruling from the Equity Court of Montgomery County (Alabama), which overruled the State's demurer to a bill in equity filed by plaintiff power company. The bill alleged discriminatory practices in the assessment of the power company's properties for ad valorem taxes.


OVERVIEW: For the tax year 1949, the State assessed the properties of certain railroad, public utility, and other like properties upon a basis of 60 percent of their value for tax purposes, while the property of other taxpayers was assessed upon the basis of less than 40 percent of the fair market value of their property. The power company filed the instant bill in equity, asserting that the assessment was discriminatory and void and violated Ala. Const. §§ 211, 217, 6, 13, 35, as well as the Due Process and the Equal Protection Clauses of the United States Constitution. The court agreed with the lower court and the power company. The court held that the use of the word "classes" in the statutes related to tax assessment, Ala. Code tit. 51, § 1-188 (1940), did not mean that any different ratio of assessment or valuation could be applied to any one species or class as distinguished from the others, but that all must be alike, equal, or uniform. Under Ala. Const. §§ 211, 217, there could be no distinction between taxpayers with different powers or who owned different kinds of real or personal property because all property had to be taxed at the same rate by whomsoever owned.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's decree in favor of the power company in the power company's action complaining of the State's tax assessment for the year 1949.

892 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Deal v. Tuscaloosa County


6 Div. 747.


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


253 Ala. 523; 45 So. 2d 691; 1950 Ala. LEXIS 297



April 13, 1950, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant executrix challenged an order from the Circuit Court of Tuscaloosa County (Alabama), which sustained the demurrer of respondents, the county, a probate judge, and others. The executrix had filed an amended bill for a declaratory judgment and to recover moneys paid to a probate judge, as custodian of county funds, by a testator, under § 161, 161A of the General Revenue Act of 1935, alleging that it was paid under protest and by mistake.


OVERVIEW: Under § 161, 161A of the Act, the compensation of tax collectors were limited to a certain amount and all earnings in excess thereof were required to be paid by a tax collector to the county treasurer, to the county general fund. In compliance therewith, a testator, who was a county tax collector, paid a certain sum over to a probate judge, as custodian of the county funds, representing the excess of fees collected. After his death, his executrix filed a claim with the county board of revenue to recover such sum alleging that the sum was paid under protest and by mistake. The board denied the claim, and the executrix filed a declaratory judgment action. On appeal from an order sustaining respondents' demurrer, the court held that: (1) the testator's claim accrued on the date the money was paid into the county treasury; (2) the claim was filed more 12 months after the money was paid to the probate judge; (3) as such, the executrix's claim was barred under Ala. Code tit. 12, § 118 (1940) because it was filed more than 12 months after the claim accrued; and (4) the claim was not allowed under Ala. Code § 186 (1923), under which reimbursement from county funds was discretionary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which had sustained the demurrer of the executrix, in her action against the county, the probate judge, and others for moneys allegedly paid under protest.

894 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Walls v. Guntersville


8 Div. 523.


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


253 Ala. 480; 45 So. 2d 468; 1950 Ala. LEXIS 283



March 30, 1950, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner sought reversal of a decree of the trial court (Alabama), which enjoined the violation of appellee city's comprehensive zoning ordinance. The trial court admitted the ordinance into evidence on the certificate of the city clerk and held that the ordinance did not unlawfully delegate power or violate federal due process and the mandates of equal protection of the Fourteenth Amendment.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court limited its consideration to the narrow questions of whether or not the ordinance was void as not having been proven to have been duly adopted and as to whether it was unconstitutional. The court adhered to an earlier ruling that the introduction of the ordinance book containing a zoning ordinance, with the statutory certificate under the hand of the city clerk respecting the adoption, publication, and existence of the ordinance, met the burden of proof resting upon the city and made a prima facie case. The court found that City of Guntersville, Ala., Comprehensive Zoning Ordinance § 12A delegated its administration and enforcement to the mayor and other officials, but that this delegation was not a forbidden delegation of power. The court held that Ala. Code tit. 37, § 777 et seq. (1940) gave the city ample power to zone to promote health and general welfare and that a zoning ordinance by necessity must be administered by subordinate officials. The court found that language as to offensive noise, smoke, and other nuisances was not overbroad, and that judicial review of any allegedly arbitrary or discriminatory acts by officials satisfied due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court decree that enjoined the landowner from violation of the city zoning ordinance.

897 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


In re Opinion of the Justices


No. 107.


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


252 Ala. 561; 42 So. 2d 81; 1949 Ala. LEXIS 486



August 29, 1949, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Opinion of the Justices of the Supreme Court in answer to questions propounded by the House of Representatives, as to the constitutionality of House Bill 1095, relating to the levy of an excise tax on gasoline in Jackson County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The House of Representatives (Alabama) propounded questions to the court as to the constitutionality of a pending bill relating to the levy of an excise tax on gasoline in Jackson County.


OVERVIEW: A bill was proposed to authorize a tax to be imposed by the governing body of a county to levy a gasoline tax, subject to a voter referendum. The tax proceeds would be used for the county's public roads, public buildings, and bridges. The house requested the court to give its opinion of the constitutionality of the bill and of a proposed amendment. First, the court held that the bill did not violate Ala. Const. § 45 (1901). There was nothing in the bill that was not referable to its title. Next, the court held that the fact that the governing body could not levy the tax unless and until there was a vote in favor of the tax by a majority vote did not invalidate the bill. The delegation of the power to tax to the governing body of the county was not the delegation of power to individuals. It left to the governing body the authority to determine whether the tax would be levied even though the election results indicated that the voters approved of the tax. Thus, the proposed bill was not violative of § 212. Third, the court held that a proposed amendment to strike the words "public buildings" was a material departure from the advertisement of the legislation and would violate § 106.


OUTCOME: The court answered the house's questions by holding that the proposed bill was not unconstitutional, but a proposed amendment was.

 

898 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Marshall County Board of Education v. State


8 Div. 471.


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


252 Ala. 547; 42 So. 2d 24; 1949 Ala. LEXIS 483



August 18, 1949, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Marshall County; J. S. Stone, Judge.

Petition of the State, on the relation of Bryan Williams and others, for mandamus to the Marshall County Board of Education, the individual members thereof, and the County Superintendent of Education, to require enrollment of certain children of relators in the Guntersville Elementary School. From a judgment granting the writ, respondents appeal.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, county board of education and associated individuals, sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court, Marshall County (Alabama), which granted a writ of mandamus in a petition filed by appellee state to require the enrollment of certain children in public elementary school.


OVERVIEW: The state attorney general had issued an opinion that the 1947 amendatory act, which stated the minimum age for school children, was unconstitutional. As a result, the school adopted Ala. Code § 298, tit. 52 (1940), and denied the admission of children who would were not six years of age on or before January 15, 1949. The state, on behalf of the children's parents, brought a writ of mandamus action against the board and its associated individuals to require the enrollment of those children. The trial court granted the writ. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that the attorney general incorrectly attributed the meaning of "school year." "School year" meant "scholastic year." Further, the 1947 amendatory act clearly stated that children who turned six on or before January 15th were entitled to be admitted into school. The court thus found that the trial court was correct in its decision that the 1947 act was not invalid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which issued a writ of mandamus requiring the school to admit certain children into public elementary school.

 

899 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Opinion of the Justices


No. 99.


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


252 Ala. 468; 41 So. 2d 771; 1949 Ala. LEXIS 460



June 29, 1949, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Opinion of the Justices of the Supreme Court in response to questions propounded by the House of Representatives under Code 1940, Tit. 13, § 34, as to validity of House Bill No. 729.

Aubrey M. Cates, Jr., of Montgomery, filed brief, amicus curiae.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In connection with pending legislation, the house of representatives of the state legislature propounded questions to the court, pursuant to Ala. Code tit. 13, § 34 (1940), as to the validity of the legislation.


OVERVIEW: The legislation: (1) authorized and directed the Director of Industrial Relations to enter into leases with the Alabama State Employment Security Corporation; (2) stated that, upon dissolution of the Corporation, the space in the building was to be assigned permanently to the Department to the extent that the appropriations or Federal grants enabled the Corporation to amortize and pay the interest on its indebtedness to finance the building; and (3) made contingent pledges of the interest and penalties on delinquent unemployment compensation contributions and of the insurance taxes levied under Ala. Code art. 12, tit. 51 (1940), which were void when federal grants or other appropriations paid the lease rentals. The court opined that §§ 1 and 2 were constitutional. As to § 3, Ala. Code art. tit. 267, § 213 and Ala. Const. § 44 prevented one legislature from enacting laws that presently depleted funds available and necessary to meet current operations in future years, and it was thus unconstitutional. Section 4 was unconstitutional because it unlawfully pledged taxes that were covered into the state treasury to the credit of the general fund, under Ala. Code tit. 55, § 28.


OUTCOME: The court opined that three sections of the proposed legislation was constitutional and that two sections were unconstitutional.
