Taxpayers & Citizens v. Board of Comm'rs


1 Div. 370.


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


252 Ala. 446; 41 So. 2d 597; 1949 Ala. LEXIS 453



June 23, 1949, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Mobile County; Claude A. Grayson, Judge.

Proceeding by the Board of Commissions of the City of Mobile against the Taxpayers and Citizens of the City of Mobile for validation of a proposed issue of bonds under Code 1940, Tit. 7, §§ 169-176. From a decree of validation, respondents appeal.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Mobile County (Alabama), which validated and confirmed a proposed issuance of Tunnel Revenue Refunding and Improvement Bonds for the City of Mobile for the improvement of a tunnel.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers and citizens challenged the issuance of bonds by the City of Mobile to fund improvements for a tunnel under the Mobile River. The circuit court validated and confirmed the proposed issuance. The court affirmed. The court found the improvement of the tunnel to be a permissible undertaking under the Municipal Revenue Bond Act, which allowed for revenue producing undertakings of highways, tunnels, and parkways. The court noted that where the action taken by the county was not clearly unconstitutional, the court's duty was to uphold the action of the state legislature unless it was clearly beyond a reasonable doubt in violation of the Alabama Constitution. This action did not meet that stringent standard.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.

 

901 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Court of County Revenues v. Richardson


8 Div. 516.


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


252 Ala. 403; 41 So. 2d 749; 1949 Ala. LEXIS 439



June 23, 1949, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Lawrence County; Jas. H. Crow, Jr., Judge.

Bill for declaratory judgment and injunction by J. B. Richardson against the Court of County Revenues of Lawrence County and others. From decrees overruling demurrer to the bill as a whole and granting a temporary injunction, respondents appeal and appellee cross-assigns error.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and in part reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, county, county depository, tax assessor, and tax collector (county), challenged a decree from the Circuit Court, Lawrence County (Alabama) that granted a temporary injunction, and overruled their demurrers to the complaint of appellee taxpayer, individually and for similarly situated taxpayers, for a declaratory judgment as to the county's right to make further collection of a special courthouse tax and as to the use of the proceeds.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer's bill of complaint sought a declaratory judgment as to the rights of the county to make further collection of a special courthouse tax, authorized by Ala. Const. amend. XXX, and as to the purposes for which proceeds of the tax on hand could have been used. The circuit court overruled the county's demurrers to the bill of complaint. The court affirmed the decree of the circuit court in part and reversed in part. The courthouse tax produced a surplus and the county diverted funds from the courthouse retirement fund to the general fund of the county. The court determined that there was no basis to collect the tax any further, and that the circuit court acted correctly in invalidating the levy for the then current tax year. However, the court held that when the purpose for which a constitutional tax was levied became accomplished and the money on hand was no longer needed for the original purpose, the legislature was entitled to authorize its use for another purpose where the constitution did not provide for this contingency. Further, the court sustained the demurrer pointing out that the bondholders of the courthouse retirement fund were not parties to the action.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decree of the trial court on its ruling as to standing and sustained the demurrer pointing out that the bondholders were not parties to the action. The court sustained the ruling of the trial court with reference to the injunction, and remanded the case, the taxpayer having the right of amendment for a period of 20 days.

 

902 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Sweet v. Wilkinson


1 Div. 354, 354-A.


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


252 Ala. 343; 40 So. 2d 427; 1949 Ala. LEXIS 274



April 21, 1949, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 26, 1949.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Mobile County; Cecil F. Bates, Judge.

Bill for declaratory judgment by Horace C. Wilkinson and Thomas E. Skinner against Henry W. Sweet, as Director of the Department of State Docks and Terminals. From an adverse decree, respondent appeals, and complainants cross-assign error.

The bill is in pertinent part as follows:

"3. On, to-wit, the 26th day of April, 1947, the said Henry W. Sweet, as Director of the Department of State Docks and Terminals, with the approval of the Governor of Alabama, employed the law firm of Wilkinson and Skinner to advise the Director of the Department of State Docks and Terminals about a proposed issue of revenue securities in the face amount of $ 4,000,000.00 and to prepare such instruments in writing and perform such other services as in their judgment would facilitate a marketing of said securities. In said contract it was provided,

"'That said attorneys shall be paid a reasonable fee for services rendered, to be agreed upon between them and the Director of the Department of State Docks and Terminals, and in event they are unable to agree, said fee to be fixed by the Circuit [***2] Court of Mobile County, Alabama, plus their reasonable traveling expenses.'

"4. Your petitioners aver that they have fully performed their part of said contract and in the performance of same they prepared needed legislation, which was later enacted by the legislature of Alabama; they prepared a request for the Governor of Alabama to submit to the Justices of the Supreme Court of Alabama for an advisory opinion on said legislation; that they prepared and submitted to said Justices briefs in support of the validity of said legislation; that they prepared the order of the Director for the sale of said securities and the form of said securities and the advertisement for the sale of said securities; the request of the Governor prepared by said attorneys together with a copy of the legislation prepared by them and the form of the order and the securities all set out in an opinion of the Justices reported in [249 Ala. 180] 30 So.2d beginning at page 715.

"5. In addition, the Department of State Docks and Terminals agreed to furnish prospective purchasers of said bonds with a validating opinion by the law firm of Chapman and Cutler in Chicago, Illinois and it was [***3] necessary for the plaintiffs to hold a number of conferences with said law firm of Chapman and Cutler in Chicago, Illinois, and to travel to and from Birmingham to Chicago and return for said conferences in order to aid in obtaining an opinion from them respecting the validity of said bonds.

"6. In the passage of said act through the legislature, the same was amended by adding thereto Section 7 1/2, which is in words and figures as follows:

"'Not more than $ 2,500 of the amount received from the sale of the bonds authorized by this Act or from any other funds of the State of Alabama or of any board, commission, bureau, or other agency of the State, shall be used or expended in payment for the services of an attorney rendered in any manner whatsoever pertaining to this Act, or pertaining to the issuance of the bonds authorized by this Act.'

"Said Act was approved on, to-wit, the 24th day of July, 1947, long after the aforesaid contract of employment was entered into.

"7. Your petitioners and the said Henry W. Sweet, as Director of the Department of State Docks and Terminals, have agreed that a fee of $ 7,500.00 for services rendered, plus $ 500.38 for expenses actually [***4] incurred by them in traveling from Birmingham to Mobile for conferences with the Director of the Department of State Docks and Terminals at his request, and for traveling from Birmingham to Montgomery and appearing before the Governor and the State Docks Board at the request of the Director and the Governor, and for traveling from Birmingham to Chicago for conferences with the law firm of Chapman and Cutler, whose validating opinion on the bonds was required by prospective customers, making a total of $ 8,000.38 for services rendered and expenses incurred in connection therewith up to the 23rd day of July, 1947, is fair and reasonable.

"8. Plaintiffs further aver that the Department of State Docks and Terminals called for bids on said bonds which were submitted and opened on, to-wit, the 23rd day of July, 1947. The Governor of Alabama rejected said bids and later called for new bids by advertisement. He and the Director called on plaintiffs to perform additional services under the aforesaid contract of employment including the preparation of the necessary documents in connection with the second call for bids and to hold further conferences with said law firm of Chapman and Cutler [***5] and to make numerous trips to Mobile, Alabama, and to prepare contracts and agreements between the Department of State Docks and Terminals and the firm of Sterne, Agee & Leach who represented a syndicate of prospective purchasers; that plaintiffs incurred traveling expenses in so doing; and said bonds were sold on December 16, 1947, and plaintiffs further aver that the defendant is ready and willing to agree with plaintiffs on an amount that is reasonable for the additional services rendered and the expenses incurred in connection therewith, but is prevented from doing so by said Section 7 1/2 of said Act 211.

"But for the purported addition of Section 7 1/2 to the aforesaid act, known as Act No. 211, the said Henry W. Sweet, as Director of the Department of State Docks and Terminals, would pay said law firm of Wilkinson and Skinner the aforesaid sum of $ 8,000.38 and agree with them on a reasonable fee and expenses for said additional services rendered. He claims that said section is a valid enactment and is a limitation on his authority to pay said law firm, and a limitation on the power of the Governor of Alabama to pay or approve the payment of any sum to any law firm in excess [***6] of $ 2,500.00. The Director of the Department of State Docks and Terminals has paid said law firm the sum of $ 2,500.00 and is ready, willing and able to pay them the difference between $ 2,500.00 and $ 8,000.38, if said Section 7 1/2, above referred to, is an invalid enactment.

"Your petitioners aver that said Section 7 1/2 is unconstitutional, null and is no limitation on the power or authority of the Director of the Department of State Docks and Terminals or the Governor of Alabama to pay your petitioners the amount it has been agreed is fair and reasonable for services rendered, plus their expenses for the following reasons:

"(a) Said Section 7 1/2 is a subject not clearly expressed in the title of said act as required by Section 45 of the Constitution of Alabama, and, therefore, violates said section of said Constitution and is null and void.

"(b) Said Section 7 1/2 of said Act No. 211 violates Section 22 of the Constitution of Alabama prohibiting the legislature of Alabama from enacting any law impairing the obligation of contracts, in that petitioners' contract with the Director of the Department of State Docks and Terminals, which was approved by the Governor [***7] of Alabama, was made, entered into and approved and partially performed long before the enactment of said Act No. 211.

"(c) Said Section 7 1/2 of Act No. 211 has no application to a contract for the services of an attorney and approved prior to passage and approval of said Act No. 211.

"9. The Director of the Department of State Docks and Terminals declines to pay your petitioners the difference between $ 2,500.00 and $ 8,000.38, and declines to agree with them on a reasonable fee for the additional services rendered and on a reasonable amount for expenses in connection therewith for the reasons aforesaid, and claims and contends that he is without lawful authority to pay said difference to said law firm because of the alleged limitation imposed on him by Section 7 1/2 of said Act No. 211."

The prayer of the bill is for a decree declaring:

"1. That Section 7 1/2 in Act No. 211 violates Section 45 of the Constitution of Alabama and is unconstitutional, null and void.

"2. That Section 7 1/2 of Act No. 211 does not apply to petitioners' contract for services, which contract was entered into and approved long prior to the enactment of said act.

"3. That Act [***8] No. 211 is no limitation on the authority of the Director of the Department of State Docks and Terminals to pay petitioners a reasonable fee for services rendered under the contract referred to in the petition.

"4. That it is the duty of Henry W. Sweet, as Director of the Department of State Docks and Terminals to forthwith and immediately pay petitioners $ 5,500.38 and to agree with them on a reasonable fee for the additional services rendered and on a reasonable sum for expenses incurred in connection therewith; and petitioners pray for such other, further, general, special and appropriate relief as they may be entitled to, for which they will as in duty bound ever pray."

The trial court decreed as follows:

"This cause coming on to be heard was submitted to the Court upon the sworn petition of the petitioners and the answer of the defendant, and same being argued by counsel and understood by the Court, the Court is of the opinion that the petitioners are entitled to the relief prayed for in the petition. It is therefore, Ordered, Adjudged and Decreed by the Court as follows:

"1. That Section 7 1/2 in said Act No. 211 violates Section 22 of the Constitution of [***9] Alabama in that it impairs the obligation of an already existing contract between the law firm Wilkinson & Skinner, Attorneys, and the Department of State Docks & Terminals.

"2. Said Section 7 1/2 being null and void and of no effect is no impediment to the payment of the fee agreed upon between the petitioners and the defendant and is no limitation upon the authority of the defendant to pay the petitioners a reasonable fee for services rendered under the contract set forth in the petition.

"3. It is the duty of Henry W. Sweet, as Director of the Department of State Docks and Terminals to undertake to agree with the law firm of Wilkinson & Skinner on a reasonable fee for additional services rendered as alleged in the petition and on a reasonable sum to be paid them for expenses incurred for traveling in connection with the performance of their duties under their employment.

"4. Inasmuch as the Court has ruled that Section 7 1/2 in said Act No. 211 is null and void because it violates Section 22 of the Constitution of Alabama, it is not necessary to determine whether or not said Section offends Section 45 of the Constitution of Alabama.

"5. The costs of this proceeding [***10] are hereby taxed against the defendant."



DISPOSITION: Modified and affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Director of the State Department of Docks and Terminals sought review of a decree from the trial court (Alabama), which ruled in favor of appellee attorneys in their declaratory judgment action against the Director for fees payable to them under a contract for services in connection with the preparation of an act for the legislature and a bond issue. The trial court ruled that 1947 Ala. Acts 211, § 7 1/2 violated Ala. Const. § 45.


OVERVIEW: The attorneys entered into a contract with the Director, prior to the enactment of 1947 Ala. Acts. 211, to provide legal services to the Department. The attorneys brought a declaratory judgment action, alleging that they had fully performed under the contract but that the Director had not paid them the balance of the contract. The trial court made a declaration favorable to the attorneys and the Director appealed. The court held that the suit was not prohibited by Ala. Const. § 14 because the Director was unsure of his duty to pay out the funds under his control. Although he was a state officer, the suit was for guidance in the discharge of his duties. The court held that 1947 Ala. Acts 211 § 7 1/2 could not serve to impair the contract between the attorneys and the Director in violation of Ala. Const. § 22. The court also held that § 7 1/2 violated Ala. Const. § 45 in that it pertained to a subject that was not mentioned in the caption of Act 211. The exclusion of § 7 1/2 from Act 211 did not affect its validity with respect to the subject included in the caption.


OUTCOME: The court modified the trial court's decree to expressing include in the judgment the declaration that it was the Director's duty to immediately pay the attorneys the unpaid balance of the contract. As modified, the trial court's decree was affirmed.

 

903 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Riley v. Bradley


6 Div. 672.


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


252 Ala. 282; 41 So. 2d 641; 1949 Ala. LEXIS 414



April 14, 1949, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 252 Ala. 282 at 292.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Opinion of April 22, 1948, Reported at: 252 Ala. 282.



DISPOSITION: Application for rehearing filed August 14, 1948 granted; judgment of reversal set aside and judgment of affirmance first entered is reinstated. Motion to expunge and application for Rehearing filed April 22, 1949 overruled.

905 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Paramount-Richards Theatres, Inc. v. State


3 Div. 504.


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


252 Ala. 54; 39 So. 2d 380; 1949 Ala. LEXIS 333



March 17, 1949, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Montgomery County; Walter B. Jones, Judge.

The State Department of Revenue having made an assessment for use taxes against Paramount-Richards Theatres, Inc., the taxpayer appealed to the circuit court in equity and filed a bill of complaint. From a decree sustaining a demurrer to the bill, the taxpayer appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action brought by appellant taxpayer to challenge the validity of use taxes assessed against it, the taxpayer sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court, Montgomery County (Alabama) that sustained appellee State of Alabama's demurrer to the complaint.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer operated movie theaters and as part of its regular course of business it leased films from out of state producers to exhibit in its theaters. As alleged by the taxpayer, the leases were strictly leases and not sales of the films. The taxpayer was obliged to return the films to the producers, and the leases did not contain any purchase options therein. The State assessed use taxes on the taxpayer based upon Ala. Code tit. 51, § 788 (1940). In challenging such assessment, the taxpayer alleged that the renting or leasing of the films shipped in interstate commerce to the taxpayer did not constitute a purchase of tangible personal property for use or storage or other consumption in the state and that to apply the levy would unconstitutionally burden interstate commerce. The trial court sustained the State's demurrer to the complaint, and the court affirmed. It held that the levy of the tax attached after the act of transportation ended; thus, it rejected the argument that the tax burdened interstate commerce. The court also ruled that the taxpayer did not meet and overcome the prima facie statutory presumption of the legality and correctness of the assessment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

906 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Ex parte State ex rel. Attorney Gen.


1 Div. 340.


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


252 Ala. 149; 39 So. 2d 669; 1949 Ala. LEXIS 365



February 24, 1949, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 14, 1949.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original petition of the State, on the relation of A. A. Carmichael, as Attorney General, for mandamus to Claude A. Grayson, as Judge of the Circuit Court, Mobile County, requiring him to dismiss an appeal from the State Department of Revenue.



DISPOSITION: Writ awarded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an original action instituted by the State of Alabama, the Attorney General sought the writ of mandamus or, in the alternative, a writ of prohibition, directing or commanding the Judge of the Circuit Court of Mobile County (Alabama), sitting in equity, to dismiss an appeal by appellant taxpayer from the State Department of Revenue.


OVERVIEW: A taxpayer brought an action to protest his tax assessment in the total amount of $ 3725.86 by virtue of the provisions of the Sales Tax Act. In an original action the taxpayer questioned his assessment. The State sought a writ of mandamus to have the action dismissed because the taxpayer had not paid the taxes. The court granted the writ, finding that the Alabama Constitution required the payment of the taxes before an appeal.


OUTCOME: The court granted the petition for a writ of mandamus.

908 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


State v. Albritton


1 Div. 348.


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


251 Ala. 422; 37 So. 2d 640; 1948 Ala. LEXIS 768



December 1, 1948, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 3, 1948.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original application of the State of Alabama against Robert B. Albritton and others, as presidential electors of the State of Alabama, for a common-law writ of certiorari, or in the alternative for an injunction or other extraordinary writ to review or control the performance of respondents' official duties.



DISPOSITION: Petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner State of Alabama applied for a writ of certiorari, or in the alternative for an injunction or other extraordinary writ to review or control the performance of official duties by respondents, presidential electors of the State of Alabama.


OVERVIEW: The State sought the issuance of the writ of certiorari to review an announcement made by respondents while running as candidates for presidential electors before the people in the primary election held by the Democratic Party of Alabama through and by authority of its central committee to the effect that if nominated and elected they would not cast their ballot for Harry S. Truman, for President of the United States, if he was nominated by the National Democratic Convention on a platform advocating or pledging enactment of law denying to the states the right to regulate race segregation and advocating social equality between the races. Respondents contended, inter alia, that the court did not have jurisdiction to hear the petition. The court found that the petition failed to present a controversy within the jurisdiction of the court. The petition concerned a political matter that was outside the jurisdiction of the court.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the petition.

911 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Newton v. Tuscaloosa


6 Div. 733.


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


251 Ala. 209; 36 So. 2d 487; 1948 Ala. LEXIS 701



June 30, 1948, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Granted July 31, 1948.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Tuscaloosa County; W. C. Warren, Judge.

Bill for injunction by Herbert E. Newton against the City of Tuscaloosa, the Commission Board of said City and the individual members thereof, Tuscaloosa County, the Board of Revenue of said County and the individual members thereof, and the Probate Judge of Tuscaloosa County, as such and as ex officio president and member of the Board of Revenue, to enjoin collection of taxes and issuance of warrants under Local Acts 1947, p. 281, and a cross-bill by respondents for a declaratory judgment with respect to said act. From an adverse decree, complainant appeals.

Statement of the Case.

This appeal brings up for review Act No. 424 of Local Acts of Alabama 1947, p. 281 et seq. By said act the legislature levied in Tuscaloosa County license and excise taxes paralleling such taxes now imposed by the general law of the State, with the rate of taxation of 50% of the amount of such State taxes, for the purpose of establishing a public hospital in Tuscaloosa County. Section 8 of the act consecrates the revenue accruing from the taxes exclusively for the establishment, maintenance [***2] and operation of such public hospital to be owned and operated jointly by the two municipalities and authorizes the city and county to issue and sell interest-bearing warrants to be paid solely from these tax revenues. The act further provides that the proceeds of the sale of these warrants shall be utilized for this exclusive purpose and gives authority to pledge for the payment of the principal and interest to be due by said warrants of a per centum of this tax levy, but stipulates that the obligation of these warrants shall not be a general obligation of either the city or the county and shall not be charged to the constitutional debt limit of either municipality.

Act No. 540, Local Acts of Alabama 1947, p. 364 et seq., approved soon after Act No. 424 at the same regular session of the legislature, created the Druid City Hospital Board, "an agency of Tuscaloosa County and the City of Tuscaloosa," for the purpose of acquiring a site for the constructing, equipping, maintaining and operating of a public general hospital to be owned jointly by the city and county, to be known as the Druid City Hospital, and which board was to receive the revenues from the tax levy under Act No.  [***3] 424 and charitable gifts from all sources.

When Act No. 424 was passed, there was a public hospital known as Druid City Hospital being then operated jointly by the city and the county, and after the enactment of Act No. 540 the Druid City Hospital Board, created by this latter act, was organized and thereupon began to operate and is now operating the hospital.

The original bill also shows that the two municipalities, the City of Tuscaloosa and Tuscaloosa County, through their respective governing bodies, propose (a) to issue and sell interest-bearing warrants as provided in the act in the aggregate amount of $ 1,500,000 as joint obligations of the city and county and payable solely from the revenues to be derived from the tax levied as authorized by the act; (b) to pledge for payment of said warrants so much of the per centum of the revenues derived from said tax, as permitted by the act, as will be necessary for said purpose; (c) to make said payment a first charge on that per centum of the revenues; and (d) to use the proceeds from the sale of said warrants for the purpose of acquiring a site and constructing and equipping the said hospital.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and in part [***4] reversed and rendered on rehearing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizen sought a declaratory judgment that Tuscaloosa, Ala., local act, p. 281 (1947) was unconstitutional and an injunction against its enforcement by appellees, the city, its commission board and its members, the county, its board of revenue and its members, and the county probate judge. The Circuit Court, Tuscaloosa County (Alabama) sustained the validity of the act and denied the injunction. The citizen sought review.


OVERVIEW: The disputed act provided for the issuance of warrants and excise taxes for the building of a public hospital. The citizen claimed that the act was invalid because it made a direct levy that unlawfully invaded the discretion of the county governing body and illegally preempted local authority. The court affirmed the lower court's judgment in part and reversed it in part. The court held that the right of taxation was vested in local authority by state permission and that the act was presumed to have the sanction of the local taxpayers acting through their duly elected representatives. However, the court agreed that the part of the act providing for the issuance of anticipating interest-bearing warrants should have been condemned. The court further held that the remainder of the act was severable and constitutional. The court also rejected the citizen's arguments that the entirety of the act violated the provisions of Ala. Const. § 45. The court found that the subject of the act was clearly expressed in the title, that the act did not improperly contain more than one subject, and that the act did not inappropriately refer to other provisions of the Alabama Code.


OUTCOME: The court reversed that part of the lower court's judgment that upheld the constitutionality of that part of the act providing for the issuance and sale of warrants; the court rendered a judgment that this part of the act was unconstitutional. In all other respects the court affirmed the lower court's judgment.

 

912 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Decatur v. Robinson


8 Div. 431.


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


251 Ala. 99; 36 So. 2d 673; 1948 Ala. LEXIS 713



June 24, 1948, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 31, 1948, 251 Ala. 99 at 121.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Morgan County; Newton B. Powell, Judge.

Bill for declaratory judgment by the City of Decatur against Paul Robinson, D. E. Frederick, and Charles H. Eyster, for construction of, and advice with respect to, an ordinance of said city authorizing establishment of parking meter zones and operation of parking meters. From a decree declaring the ordinance unconstitutional and void, complainant appeals.

On May 5, 1947, the appellant, City of Decatur, entered into a contract with Duncan Meter Corporation, organized and existing under the laws of the State of Illinois, denominated in the contract "The Meter Company," the city agreeing to lease from the meter company and said company agreeing "to lease to the city, subject to the terms and conditions hereinafter set forth 200 more or less Miller Multiple-Coin Parking Meters (hereinafter called 'meters'). The agreed value of the meters shall be Seventy-five ($ 75.00) Dollars per meter F.O.B. Chicago, which includes standard and bell base plus actual advances made by the meter company as hereinafter provided. The city shall at any time have the [***2] option to purchase the meters by applying the rentals which have been paid in by the city to the meter company against the agreed value of the meter and paying the balance due thereon." The contract which is denominated "Parking Meter Trial Lease" further provides:

"2. The Meter Company shall advance all freight, supervision, and installation costs in connection with the delivery and installation of said meters. The installation supervisor will train the City-appointed maintenance man to properly maintain all meters installed under this agreement. The Company furnishes three (3) complete meter mechanisms and one (1) meter housing free for each one hundred (100) meters installed, for service purposes. * * *

"4. Payments by The City to The Meter Company shall be solely from the receipts, funds and revenues obtained from the operation thereof and there shall be no obligation on the part of The City to pay for the same from any other source. The manner of payment of rental for said meters shall be as follows: The City shall deduct from the first receipts from the operation of said meters the actual cost of freight, supervision, and installation, and reimburse the Meter Company [***3] therefor. After the aforesaid deductions, all remaining receipts, funds and revenues from the operation of said meters shall be considered not revenue. Upon the fifteenth (15th) day after the installation of said meters and each and every thirtieth (30th) day thereafter The City shall pay as rental to The Meter Company fifty (50%) percent of the net revenue from all meters so installed until The City exercises its option to purchase the meters and/or The Meter Company has received rentals and reimbursements for advances in the aggregate amount of the agreed value of the meters or until or unless this agreement is terminated or cancelled under the provisions of paragraph five (5) and six (6) hereof.

"5. The Meter Company extends and grants unto the City the option to terminate this agreement at the expiration of the trial period by giving The Meter Corporation written notice thirty (30) days prior to the expiration of said period; but in that event, The Meter Company shall nevertheless be entitled to receive from The City and to retain as rental for the use of the meters fifty (50%) percent of the net revenue from said meters, as aforesaid, which shall have accrued during that [***4] entire period, and until the meters are removed; and in the event of such cancellation or if The Meter Company shall exercise its right to cancel as provided in paragraph six (6) hereof, The Meter Company will, at the expiration of said period, at its own cost and expense, promptly proceed to remove said meters and repair any damage to the places in the pavements or other premises in which said meters were installed, and all obligation under the terms of this agreement shall cease and terminate, except as herein otherwise provided.

"6. If at any time prior to the payment in full to The Meter Company of the agreed value, as aforesaid, of all said meters, rentals to The Meter Company since the installation of said meters, shall have averaged less than three ($ 3.00) Dollars per month, per meter, or if The City shall violate this agreement or default in the full and faithful performance of this agreement, then The Meter Company may at its option cancel this agreement by giving to The City written notice of its intention to do so, and at any time after the tenth (10th) day following the giving of such notice, The Meter Company shall have the right, at its option with or without legal [***5] process or further notice of any kind, to enter upon the premises where said meters may be installed or kept and remove and retake the same for its own use, and to receive from the City as rental for the use of the meters the fifty (50%) percent of net revenue from said meters as aforesaid which shall have accrued up to the time said meters are removed. Nothing herein contained shall be construed in any way limiting or affecting The Meter Company's right to pursue or enforce any remedy provided by law in the event of a breach of this agreement by the City.

"7. If at any time prior to the payments in full to The Meter Company of the agreed value, as aforesaid, of all said meters any taxes are levied on meters, installed, such as personal property tax, sales tax or use tax, such taxes will be advanced by The Meter Company, and The City shall reimburse The Meter Company in full from the gross receipts of the meters, before the net revenue is computed for the purposes of paragraph four (4) hereof.

"8. It is understood and agreed that the title to all said meters shall be and remain in The Meter Company until and unless the full agreed value thereof, as aforesaid, shall have been [***6] paid in cash to The Meter Company, including the rentals aforesaid.

"9. The Meter Company agrees that if The City pays it as rentals the full agreed value of said meters as aforesaid, it will deliver to The City a bill of sale therefor, free and clear of all encumbrances.

"10. The Meter Company further covenants and agrees that it is the lawful owner of said meters and that the same are free and clear of all liens, contracts or conditional sales, chattel mortgages, and other encumbrances, and that The Meter Company has a lawful right to lease, dispose of, and sell the same, and that it will warrant and defend its title thereto against all claims whatsoever.

"11. The Meter Company agrees to furnish the said meters with a mechanism regulated as to time as shall be mutually agreed to between The City and The Meter Company, and equipped with two slots, if so ordered by The City to receive coins of the denomination of 1 [cent] and 5 [cent], and will be set to allow:

12 minutes for 1 penny

24 minutes for 2 pennies

36 minutes for 3 pennies

48 minutes for 4 pennies

60 minutes for 5 pennies, or

1 nickel

72 minutes for 6 pennies, or

1 [***7] nickel and 1 penny

84 minutes for 7 pennies,

or, 1 nickel and 2 pennies

96 minutes for 8 pennies, or

1 nickel and 3 pennies, or,

108 minutes for 9 pennies,

or 1 nickel and 4 pennies,

120 minutes for 10 pennies, or,

2 nickels.

or at any other available rate combination which may be mutually agreed upon. * * *

"14. The City warrants that all necessary and proper steps have been or will be taken by the duly constituted Governmental and Municipal authorities authorizing the execution of this agreement and that all necessary or proper ordinances and/or resolutions have been or will be adopted authorizing and providing for the installation of said meters and the operation thereof, and agrees it will police the said meters after installation, and shall properly enforce all ordinances and resolutions pertaining thereto.

"15. The City agrees to set up a special parking meter fund into which all receipts from all meters furnished hereunder shall be placed and kept. No withdrawals from said special parking meter fund shall be made until The Meter Company has been paid the cost of freight, supervision, and installation, and the fifty (50%)  [***8] percent of the net revenue has been paid to The Meter Company as hereinbefore provided, after which The City shall have the right to the remaining fifty (50%) percent of the net revenue to use as they see fit.

"16. This agreement shall be for a trial period of six months, commencing from the date of complete installation. The City shall have the option at the expiration of said trial period of entering into a further trial period.

"17. * * * The Meter Company further covenants and agrees to defend the City in any law suit brought to test the legality of parking meters in the City and to pay all expense of such litigation, including attorneys fees and court costs and in the event the City is prohibited by court order from operating parking meters this contract shall be terminated as provided in section 5 hereof. The Meter Company further covenants and agrees to pay, without reimbursement, all freight and installation costs in excess of $ 3.50 per meter. * * *." [Italics supplied.]

On the date of the execution of said contract, excerpts taken from the minutes of the city council state:

"Mr. W. Howard Netterville, Southwest Distributor for Duncan Meter Corporation [***9] of Chicago, Illinois, was present and discussed with the Council 'Parking Meters.' Mr. Netterville demonstrated and explained the Miller Meter and the contract in detail (Here the contract as approved by the City Attorney is set out in the minutes in full). After some discussion Councilman McRae made a motion, seconded by Councilman Speake, that the City enter into a contract in the foregoing form with the Duncan Meter Corporation and the Mayor, upon the approval of the City Attorney be and is hereby authorized to sign said contract. * * *"

Three months later, August 5, 1947, the city council adopted and promulgated its parking meter ordinance in pursuance of said contract, which purports to grant and confer on the meter company certain rights and privileges, towit: Section 3 of the ordinance confers on the chief of police of the city the duty to direct and authorize and mark off individual parking spaces in the "parking zones designated and described in Section 2 of this ordinance and in such other zones as may hereafter be established, said parking spaces to be designated by lines painted or durably marked on the curbing or surface of the street. * * *." Section 4 of said ordinance [***10] provides:

"Section 4. Installation of Parking Meters. In said parking meter zones there shall be installed parking meters upon the curb or sidewalk immediately adjacent to the parking places provided in Section 3 of this ordinance, said installation to be placed not more than two (2) feet from the curb nor more than four (4) feet from the front line of the parking space as indicated, and the Chief of Police shall be responsible for the regulation, control, operation, maintenance and use of such parking meters. Each device shall be so set as to display a signal showing legal parking upon the deposit of the appropriate coin or coins, lawful money of the United States of America, for the period of time prescribed by this ordinance. Each device shall be so arranged that upon the expiration of the lawful time limit it will indicate by a proper visible signal that the lawful parking period has expired and in such cases the right of such vehicle to occupy such space shall cease and the operator, owner, possessor or manager thereof shall be subject to the penalties hereinafter provided.

"Section 5. Operation of Parking Meters. Except in a period of emergency determined by an officer [***11] of the Fire or Police Department, or in compliance with the directions of a police officer or traffic control sign or signal, when any vehicle shall be parked in any parking space alongside or next to which a parking meter is located, the operator of such vehicle shall, upon entering the said parking meter space, immediately deposit or cause to be deposited in said meter such proper coin of the United States as is required for such parking meter and as is designated by proper directions on the meter, and as required by the directions on the meter, the operator of such vehicle, after the deposit of the proper coin or coins, shall also set in operation the timing mechanism on such meter in accordance with directions properly appearing thereon, and failure to deposit such proper coin, and to set the timing mechanism in operation when so required, shall constitute a violation of this ordinance. Upon the deposit of such coin (and the setting of the timing mechanism in operation when so required) the parking space may be lawfully occupied by such vehicle during the period of time which has been prescribed for the part of the street in which said parking space is located, provided that any [***12] person placing a vehicle in a parking meter space adjacent to a meter which indicates that unused time has been left in the meter by the previous occupant of the space shall not be required to deposit a coin so long as his occupancy of said space does not exceed the indicated unused parking time. If said vehicle shall remain parked in any such parking space beyond the parking time set for such parking space, and if the meter shall indicate such illegal parking, then, and in that event, such vehicle shall be considered as parking overtime and beyond the period of legal parking time, and such parking shall be deemed a violation of this ordinance.

"Section 6. Parking Time Limits. (a) Parking or standing a vehicle in a designated space in Parking Meter Zone 'A' shall be lawful for twelve minutes upon deposit of a one-cent coin, twenty-four (24) minutes upon the deposit of two (2) one-cent coins, thirty-six (36) minutes upon the deposit of three (3) one-cent coins, forty-eight (48) minutes upon the deposit of four (4) one-cent coins, or sixty (60) minutes upon the deposit of five (5) one-cent coins or one (1) five-cent coin of the United States of America, all upon the consequent setting [***13] in operation of the timing mechanism on such meter pursuant to the provisions written thereon. * * *." [Italics supplied.]

The ordinance makes parking contrary to the ordinance or for a time longer than specified on the meter or failure of a person parking to turn on the mechanism of the meter an offense punishable by fine and imprisonment, one or both, "not exceeding $ 50.00 or by imprisonment not exceeding 30 days," without specifying where the offender is to be imprisoned, and this penalty applies to any person in whose name any such vehicle is registered, whether or not such person parked the vehicle in such parking space. [§§ 7 and 11 of the Ordinance.]

Section 1(e) of the ordinance provides: "The word 'park' or 'parking' shall mean the standing of a vehicle, whether or not, upon a street otherwise than in obedience to traffic regulations, signs or signals or an involuntary stopping of a vehicle by reason of causes beyond the control of the operator of the vehicle."

Section 1 of the ordinance also provides: "Parking Meter Zones. The following named and described areas, streets, or portions of streets and such other areas, streets, or portions of streets as may [***14] hereafter be included in this Section by amendment thereto, lying within the corporate limits of the City of Decatur, shall be and constitute 'Parking Meter Zone "A,"' namely: * * *."

Following this provision the ordinance designates certain portions of Second Avenue East and a part of Moulton Street and a part of Bank Street as parking Zone "A." And after repeating the last above quoted provisions designates part of Grant Street and a part of Johnston Street as parking Zone "B."

Section 10 provides: "Use of Funds. The coins deposited in parking meters are required and shall be used to defray the expense of proper regulation, control, and inspection of traffic upon the public streets of the City of Decatur, Alabama; to provide for the costs of supervision, regulation, inspection and control of traffic upon the public streets and to defray the cost of supervising, regulating and inspecting the parking of vehicles in the parking meter zones and the cost of the purchase, supervision, protection, inspection, installation, operation, maintenance, control and use of the parking meters installed hereunder, and the special funds in which such fees shall be placed shall be devoted [***15] exclusively to these purposes." [Italics supplied.]

No provision is made in the ordinance for drive-ins or walkways for use of the abutting property owners as a means of egress and ingress. Such rights or privileges if recognized at all are left to the discretion of the chief of police. (Italicization in the foregoing statement is by the writer for emphasis.)

The original bill in this case was filed on August 7, 1947, by the City of Decatur to which the contract with the meter company and the ordinance passed in pursuance thereof were attached as exhibits, against Paul Robinson and W. W. Dinsmore, seeking a construction of said ordinance and praying that the court, "advise complainant and respondents whether or not the complainant has the right and authority under and by virtue of said ordinance to make, set up and establish parking meter zones within the limits of the City of Decatur as therein defined and set up, operate and maintain parking meters along or near the curb or sidewalk in said parking meter zones in the manner and mode likewise set out and described in said ordinance attached hereto, and further whether or not the said complainant is authorized and empowered [***16] under and by virtue of the terms and provisions of said ordinance to enforce the parking of vehicles as required and set out in said ordinance referred to and to penalize and fine or imprison as therein provided violators of said ordinance in any particular." [Italics supplied.]

And as to the said W. W. Dinsmore that the court "will construe and determine whether or not said ordinance attached as Exhibit '2,' and the establishment of parking meter zones, as herein defined, and the operation and maintenance of parking meters, as therein contemplated, has the effect of and is an unauthorized use of the public street, Second Avenue East, upon which his place of business fronts and abuts and which is in said parking meter zone 'A,'" and for other relief.

On October 13, 1947, the bill was amended by striking the name "W. W. Dinsmore" wherever the same appears in paragraphs 8 and 9 and inserting in lieu thereof the names of the respondents "D. E. Frederick and Chas. H. Eyster."

On August 25, 1947, the bill was amended by striking W. W. Dinsmore as a party respondent and by striking paragraph 7 of the bill of complaint and in lieu thereof inserting like allegations as to [***17] the ownership of the property by Eyster and Frederick.

The original bill after alleging that complainants have entered into the contract attached to the bill as Exhibit 2, the substance of which has heretofore been stated, avers that the complainant is a municipal corporation, organized and existing under the laws of the State of Alabama; that Paul Robinson is a resident of Morgan County, and is part owner of premises located at 402 Bank Street upon that part of Bank Street abutting on parking meter Zone "A" designated and defined in said ordinance and exhibit "2" and more particularly described in the bill by metes and bounds. That said Paul Robinson is part owner and operator of the firm known as Robinson Furniture Company established and conducting a going business at said premises into which business house each day many persons from and about the City of Decatur and elsewhere go and come for the purpose of buying or selling goods, wares or merchandise therein and of conducting trade and business with the said Paul Robinson, his agents, servants or employees. That said Robinson on divers and sundry times has asserted and stated in effect that he would contest the validity of [***18] said ordinance and seek to enjoin the operation of said ordinance or any ordinance of such character providing for installation of parking meters and has threatened to file such suit. On information and belief the complainant alleges that Paul Robinson is claiming and contending that the passage and operation of said ordinance and the operation of parking meters as therein contemplated has been held to have the effect and tendency to and does deprive him of his property without due process of law and that said ordinance is an unauthorized exercise of the taxing power invested in the complainants. The bill further avers that Chas. H. Eyster is a part owner and tenant in common of the property described as 100' X 140' in Decatur, Morgan County, Alabama, on the Southeast Corner of the intersection of 2nd Avenue East and Moulton Street (describing the same) as "Lots 9, 10, 11 and 12 of Block 6 of Addition 3 of the Decatur Land Improvement and Furnace Company to Decatur, Alabama, as shown by map or plat of said Addition on file and of record in the office of the Probate Judge of Morgan County, Alabama," and as such. lets and rents a portion of the same to D. E. Frederick and his associates [***19] doing business under the firm name and style of "Exchange Furniture Co.,"

That D. E. Frederick is part owner and operator of said business known as Exchange Furniture Company and located at No. 209 East Moulton Street, Decatur, Alabama. That D. E. Frederick is the lessee and tenant of Said Chas. H. Eyster. That said Frederick daily conducts and operates said business known and designated as Exchange Furniture Company and into said business house or establishment located on the south side of Moulton Street between Second and Fourth Avenues, East, in Decatur, Alabama, and in front of which a parking meter zone known as Parking Meter Zone "A" has been established, many persons from and about Decatur go and come each day for the purpose of buying and selling goods, wares or merchandise, and of conducting trade and business therein with the said D. E. Frederick, his associates in business, his agents, servants or employees.

On information and belief the bill further avers that Eyster and Frederick contend that the passage and adoption of the said ordinance and its operation and effect tends to and does deprive them of their property without due process of law and is an obstruction [***20] of free ingress and egress in and to the property described; and is an unauthorized exercise of the taxing powers vested in the complainant; that said Eyster and Frederick each contend that the establishment and operation of a parking meter zone in front of, abutting or adjacent to the property above described is an unauthorized use of the public highway or street by reason of a provision written into the dedication of said street by the Decatur Land Improvement and Furnace Company, the owners of said land upon which the property and streets were situated at the time of the dedication thereof by preparing and filing a man delineating lots, blocks and streets and having the same recorded in the office of the Judge of Probate of Morgan County, Alabama, in the year 1887, containing the following reservation:

"* * * 'The Decatur Land Improvement & Furnace Co.' hath dedicated the said streets, avenues and alleys to and for the use of a highway but the same are not to be used for other purposes without the consent of the said 'Decatur Land Improvement & Furnace Co.' nor must the said alleys and avenues be used for the construction and operation of said Street railways therein or thereon,  [***21] nor for laying the water mains or water pipes or gas pipes or for the erection and keep up the post and wire for electric lights without the consent of the said Decatur Land Improvement & Furnace Company and with this reservation the said plat or map is acknowledged and certified. * * *"

A similar dedication was alleged as to property owned by Robinson on Bank Street in "Old Decatur" territory in 1877.

The defendants Robinson, Eyster and Frederick filed answer admitting allegations of paragraph 5 to the extent that it alleges said parking meters have not as yet been fully installed, that said meters are in the process of being installed in various portions of said parking meter zones, and that posts or standards to support the meter mechanism have been installed as alleged. It is also admitted that said parking meters and the use thereof as contemplated in said ordinance will produce surplus revenue "that is to say, revenue over and above the amount required to defray the expense of the installation and purchase of said parking meters and the maintenance, supervision, inspection and control, and use of said parking meters." All of the other allegations of paragraph 5 are [***22] denied.

The answer alleges: "The defendant Robinson, as alleged in paragraph 6 of the bill of complaint, is a part owner of the property described in said paragraph 6 of the bill of complaint, which said property fronts a distance of 25 feet on the westerly line of Bank Street and abuts a distance of 82 1/2 feet on the southerly line of Church Street, which said streets are public streets in the City of Decatur, and the said Robinson owns to the center line of each of said streets, subject to the easement of travel and use of said streets by the public, and the said Robinson conducts a going business on said property and sells thereon goods, wares and merchandise, and his customers and those with whom he does business park alongside of said streets and alongside of said property owned by him, and leave the vehicles so parked by them on said streets while engaged in doing business with the said Robinson, and he and his said customers with whom he does business have the right that said persons and the said Robinson park their vehicles along the curb adjacent to said streets and leave them there, so parked for a reasonable time and subject to valid regulations which may be ordained [***23] by the complainant, without the payment of any toll or fee, for the privilege and right of so parking said vehicles. There are various other business establishments in the City of Decatur, some of which come in direct competition with the said Robinson, and which are not within any parking meter zone established by the ordinance exhibited with the bill of complaint, and as to which the complainant had not enacted any ordinance or made any requirement that a fee or toll be paid to the complainant for the privilege of parking vehicles in the streets alongside said business establishments.

"11. As alleged in paragraph 7 of the bill of complaint, the defendant Eyster is a part owner of the property described in said paragraph, which said property fronts upon and abuts on Second Avenue East and Moulton Street, both of which are public streets in the City of Decatur, and the said Eyster owns the property to the center line of each of said streets, subject to the easement for travel and use of said streets by the public, and the said Frederick, together with his associates, is the lessee of said property and conducts a business thereon, under the name and style of Exchange Furniture [***24] Company, and various customers of the said Frederick and persons with whom he does business, and the said Frederick, have the right to park motor vehicles along the curb of said street, subject to reasonable regulations of the City of Decatur, without the exaction of any toll or fee for the privilege and right of parking said motor vehicles along the curb of said streets. There are various persons in the City of Decatur who do business in the City of Decatur and who compete with the said Frederick and his associates, whose businesses are located alongside of public streets in the City of Decatur and are not within any parking meter zone established by said ordinance exhibited with the bill of complaint, or by any other ordinance enacted by the City of Decatur." [Italics supplied.]

Said answer alleges that there are other business properties near or adjacent to the property of defendants in which no parking zones are established and in which automobiles and other vehicles are allowed to park without any toll or fee for the privilege of so parking.

That the property of the defendant Eyster is located in Addition 3 of the Decatur Land Improvement & Furnace Company of Decatur,  [***25] Alabama, which was laid off into lots, blocks streets, paths and avenues in 1887, which were dedicated by map filed in the office of the Judge of Probate of Morgan County, Alabama, and lots sold therefrom and further:

"The defendants further show unto the Court that while said ordinance is couched in language giving it the appearance of an ordinance designed to regulate traffic under the police power of the City of Decatur, said ordinance was enacted for the purpose of obtaining and raising revenue for the City of Decatur. These defendants show further unto the Court that at the time of the adoption and enactment of said ordinance the City of Decatur had in effect ordinances to control and regulate traffic in the territory designated in said ordinance as parking meter zones, which said ordinances then in force and effect established parking places along the curbs of the streets in said zones, which said parking spaces were marked off and defined, and which said ordinances limited the time during which a vehicle could remain parked in said parking spaces, and provided a penalty for any person leaving a vehicle parked in said parking spaces in excess of the time allowed. These defendants [***26] further show unto the Court that the complainant by enacting said ordinance is attempting to convert the said streets and avenues within the parking meter zones designated by said ordinance into parking lots, and to charge the people a fee or toll for the use of said streets. These defendants further show unto the Court that the said parking meters constitute obstructions or nuisances on said streets and will interfere with the free flow of pedestrian traffic alongside and to and from the property owned and leased by the defendants, and that said parking meters constitute a public nuisance." [Italics supplied.]

"15. The defendants take the position, and contend and show unto the Court, that the said ordinance exhibited with the bill of complaint is invalid and void for the following reasons, separately and severally, that is to say:

"(1) Said ordinance and the proposed operation and enforcement thereof deprives the defendants of their property without due process by law, and violates Section 6 of the Constitution of Alabama and Amendment XIV of the Constitution of the United States.

"(2) Said ordinance and the proposed operation and enforcement thereof denies the defendants [***27] of the equal protection of the laws and violates Section 1 of the Constitution of Alabama and Amendment XIV of the Constitution of the United States.

"(3) Said ordinance and the proposed enforcement thereof constitutes a taking of the property of the defendants by the City of Decatur for public use without the payment of just compensation therefor, and violates Section 235 of the Constitution of Alabama.

"(4) Said ordinance was enacted not only for the purpose of regulating traffic, but for the purpose of raising revenue for the City of Decatur, and is an unlawful, arbitrary, unreasonable and unauthorized exercise of the taxing powers of the complainant.

"(5) Said ordinance as to the property of the said Eyster is in conflict with and a violation of the dedication of Moulton Street and Second Avenue as public streets in the City of Decatur by the said Decatur Land Improvement and Furnace Company.

"16. The defendants join in the request of the complainant that the Court render a declaratory judgment and decree as to the validity of said ordinance, and pray that the Court will declare the same to be null and void."

After the case was at issue the parties entered [***28] into a stipulation of fact from which we take the following.

"There are 348 parking meter spaces painted on the streets in the parking meter zones. In painting the parking meter spaces upon the streets, as directed by Section 3 of the ordinance in question, the Chief of Police has left open spaces at each fire hydrant in the parking meter zones, and at each loading zone in front of business establishments in the parking meter zones as the same existed prior to the enactment of said ordinance.

"No figures are available to show whether the average parking time after the installation of parking meters in Decatur will be reduced or increased, but three separate surveys made in other towns having parking meters have shown that the average parking time of each vehicle upon the installation of parking meters was reduced from 52.8 minutes to 32.7 minutes, from 23.6 to 19.9 minutes and from 46 to 40 minutes, respectively. Likewise, no figures are available as to what, if any effect the installation of parking meters in Decatur will have upon the increase or decrease of available parking space. Surveys made in two other towns have shown that after meters were installed, four cars found [***29] parking space where three had prior to meters, and in another city a turn-over was recorded of 6.8 cars per parking space per day prior to parking meters as compared with 8.3 cars per space per day following installation of meters.

"Section 10 of the ordinance restricts the use of funds which are deposited in said parking meters and attention of the court is invited to said section. Should there be any excess receipts over and above the amount required to carry out the provisions of said Section 10 of the ordinance, then complainant proposes that such should be used in acquisition of free parking lots, widening of streets, maintenance and erection of proper traffic markers and signs, pavement of alleys and improvement of approach in the rear of the congested business area and the opening of alleys similarly situated but presently unused. Such alleys are in existence behind and back of each of the blocks involved in the parking meter zones and extend either partially or completely through the entire block and only three of such alleys are improved or paved. * * *"

On a subsequent day the parties entered into the further stipulations, that: "It is estimated that each parking [***30] meter in Parking Meter Zone 'A' will gross $ 5.67 per month and that each meter in Parking Meter Zone 'B' will gross $ 2.84 per month. It is further estimated that the life of each parking meter will vary from ten to fifteen years." It is agreed that these stipulations of fact may be supplemented at the hearing by other testimony.

It is without dispute that steel posts or standards for the several meters are installed--set in concrete--in the sidewalk approximately 20 feet apart and from 4 to 5 feet in height, two feet from the street curb, allowing loading space and space for bus stops in the zones set apart by the ordinance for meters. The meters are also of steel, standing 17 inches in height, 8 inches in width and 6 inches in thickness.

The testimony was given ore tenus with exception of the depositions of witnesses Swann, Griffin, Roach and Gains, City Officials of Columbia, Tennessee. This testimony goes to show that there are only a small number, from 6 to 7, manufacturers of such equipment in the United States. That the manufacturers do not install such equipment but the right to install and set up said equipment is "farmed out" to sales agencies for different groups [***31] of states and that such sales agencies are interested in establishing the right to install such equipment through legislation or judicial decision in the territories of the states covered by such agencies, forming an interlocking high pressure salesmanship group which aids and gives comfort and support to any group where the right to install such equipment has not been established or is disputed.

The witness Roswell Smith testified for complainant that he had been associated with parking meter companies since 1938 and that he and his brother were the district representatives of the "Car-Park Meter Company" with jurisdiction over North and South Carolina, Georgia, Florida, Alabama and Mississippi. That they appoint state managers in the several states and that other sales groups do likewise. That he was interested in meters located in Florida, Georgia and Mississippi. That they have none in Alabama. That they are interested in this suit to establish the legality of such parking meters under contracts similar to the one here involved. That such groups "have direct supervision over our representatives and all of the installations. We are not only interested in getting installations [***32] but we are interested in the progress made, the effect of the installation on the cities, the profits derived from them so far as we are able to judge and the revenue collected and the allocation of the revenues. We are generally interested in the development of the meter business. * * * We are very much interested in what the meters are doing and how they are functioning, not only ours but those of our competitors. * * *." The testimony goes to show that the effect of establishing and using parking meters necessitates the employment of persons of mechanical skill to keep the meters in order and increases the expense of police supervision of meters; the purchase of a machine at a cost of $ 250 to separate or aid in the counting of the revenues and other expenses. The witness testified as to the cost of the meters and their installation and the duration of their use. That the patrol of the streets where meters are established is a continuous performance. He further testified that usually where the company gets 50% of the gross revenue the other 50% that the city gets is usually used for maintenance and costs.

Speaking as an expert on his redirect examination this witness testified:

 [***33] "Q. You mean that in 18 to 30 months the city would not be able to take their costs off? A. Yes, sir. I think you will find that in your contract, unless it is different than most, the company's take is 50% of the gross revenue * * *."

On being asked how he got in touch with the City of Decatur and who requested him to come in this case he stated: "I came voluntarily to see Mr. Shanks. I didn't know him at the time, * * * whoever was representing the city, because we are interested in the final conclusion of this suit. * * * Yes, sir and in every state where there is any question we always come in and see what we can do. Some-times it is done by legislative enactment and sometimes by decisions of courts. * * *"

The witness Speake, a member of the City Council of Decatur, testified that the question of signing the contract was "very considerably" discussed and especially at the meeting where Mr. Neterville, the representative of the meter company, was present and the use to which the revenue would be put, stating: "Well, as I recall, it would just go into the general fund, funds are short at the time. It wasn't going to be earmarked funds after we paid for them. * * *"

The [***34] witness Swann, whose deposition was taken by the official court reporter acting as commissioner by agreement of the parties, testified that he was superintendent of the streets and acting manager of the City of Columbia, Tenn., where meters had been installed and stated: "The deposit of one penny in a meter will purchase 12 minutes parking time and the deposit of a nickel will produce 60 minutes parking time. * * *" This witness further testified in respect to the city of which he is the manager that: "It didn't increase the police force but that they had to put on more men. * * * It (the installation of meters) gave us a place for them. * * * If it hadn't been for the advent of parking meters, you would have to lay off some of them? A. Yes sir. * * *" [Italics and parathensis supplied.]

The witness Gaines testified that he was a fire truck driver and had been looking after the meters at Columbia, Tenn. That he had been looking after the meters since they were put in. That he was appointed driver on April 10, 1931, and since meters were installed, he was the driver of the fire truck and collected the coins from the meters. He was the man who maintained the meters in proper condition.

 [***35] On submission for final decree on pleadings and proof the circuit court entered a declaratory decree holding, among other things: "Upon consideration of the pleadings and proof the Court is of the opinion, and it is so ordered, that there exists a justiciable controversy between the Complainant and the Respondents within the meaning of the Declaratory Judgment Act, and that the parties have the right to have their rights declared in this cause.

"No one questions the general police power of the Complainant to regulate traffic in a reasonable manner on its streets. This power is so ancient that no authority need be cited in its support. There are, however, certain limitations upon this power, and in this case the Court is called upon to determine just how far the powers of a municipality extends, and where the rights of individual citizens begin. Rights and powers of both the individual citizen and the government must be mutually respected, and if either is permitted to invade the rights or authority of the other we do not have that type of government which is guaranteed by the Constitution.

"The Court is of the opinion that the questions here presented were settled by [***36] our Supreme Court in January, 1937, in the case of City of Birmingham et al. v. Hood-McPherson Realty Co., 233 Ala. 352, 172 So. 114, 108 A.L.R. 1140. This case was a bill to abate a nuisance which the complainant alleged was created by the erection of parking meters on the streets of Birmingham adjacent to the complainant's property. In holding that the erection of parking meters on the streets of Birmingham created a nuisance the Supreme Court said that the municipality holds the streets in trust not only for the municipality and its citizens, but in trust for the public at large. It was said that the owner of property on a public street has the right to have his family, guests, or customers come and go within reasonable limitations and without the exaction of a fee."

The decree of the circuit courts holds, in part, as follows:

"In the Birmingham case, as in this case, there was a dedication of the street to public use by a private corporation with a provision that the street could not be used for any other purpose except with the consent of the corporation. In this case there was the same kind of dedication of the streets involved in 'New Town'. The Supreme [***37] Court held in the Birmingham case that the erection of parking meters on this street without the consent of the corporation which dedicated it was an unauthorized abandonment of the terms of the dedication deed.

"Our Supreme Court in the same case held that the use of parking meters in the manner proposed at that time was an unauthorized exercise of the taxing power of the City.

"This Court is of the opinion that the pleadings and proof in the case under consideration bring its under the same rules as laid down in the Birmingham case, and, therefore, that the ordinance authorizing parking meters in the City of Decatur is unconstitutional and void, and the Court hereby finds and declares the following:

"1. That the City of Decatur does not have the right or authority to erect parking meters and establish parking meter zones in the City of Decatur as outlined in the bill of complaint.

"2. That the adoption and passage of the ordinance authorizing the use of parking meters in the City of Decatur, and its effect deprives the Respondents of their property without due process of law in violation of both the State and Federal Constitutions.

"3. The adoption and passage [***38] and effect of the ordinance authorizing the use of parking meters in the City of Decatur is an unlawful and unauthorized exercise of the taxing power of the City.

"4. The adoption and passage and effect of the ordinance authorizing the use of parking meters in the City of Decatur as proposed is, as to the Respondents, Eyster and Frederick, in conflict with, and in violation of the dedication of Moulton Street and Second Avenue as public streets of the City of Decatur by the Decatur Land Improvement & Furnace Company. * * *."

The complainant has appealed from this decree and frankly states that the purpose of the appeal is to induce this court to overrule the case of City of Birmingham et al. v. Hood-McPherson Realty Co., 233 Ala. 352, 172 So. 114, 108 A.L.R. 1140.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and rendered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city sought review of an order of the Circuit Court, Morgan County (Alabama), which entered a judgment declaring an ordinance for the establishment of parking meters unconstitutional and void.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff city filed a suit against defendant property owners seeking a judgment regarding the validity of an ordinance establishing parking meters. The lower court entered a judgment for defendants and declared the ordinance unconstitutional and void. However, on appeal, the court reversed the lower court's order holding that the emergence of more sophisticated means of transportation necessitated the enactment of the ordinance. The court further held that the ordinance was consistent with the state constitution as well as Ala. Code § 32 (1940). Finally, the court held that because the ordinance was a reasonable exercise of plaintiff's police power, defendants' property rights were subservient to such power.


OUTCOME: The court reversed an order of the lower court, which entered a judgment declaring plaintiff city's ordinance for the establishment of parking meters unconstitutional and void. The ordinance was a reasonable and constitutional exercise of plaintiff's police power.
