914 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Opinion of Justices


No. 87


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


250 Ala. 399; 34 So. 2d 598; 1948 Ala. LEXIS 575



April 1, 1948 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Governor of Alabama propounded questions under the 13 Ala. Code § 34 (1940), as to whether an amendatory Act of the Legislature, requiring presidential electors to cast their ballots for the nominee of the national convention of the party by which they were elected, was violative of constitutional provisions. The Justices of the Supreme Court filed its answer.


OVERVIEW: The Governor sought an answer to the question: Did the amendment to § 226 violate any provision of Article II of the Constitution of the United States or Article XII of the Amendments of the Constitution of the United States? The Justices stated that the language of the Constitution clearly showed that it was the intention of the framers that the electors chosen for the several states would exercise their discretion in the performance of their duty in the election of the president and vice-president, and in determining the individuals for whom they would cast the electoral votes of the states. The Justices held that history supported the interpretation without controversy. The Justices also held that when the legislature attempted to go further than its power of appointment of electors, and dictate to the electors the choice which they must make for president and vice-president, it invaded the field set apart to the electors by the Constitution.


OUTCOME: The Justices of the Supreme Court held that the statute was unconstitutional.

 

915 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Anniston v. Douglas


No. 7 Div. 948


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


250 Ala. 367; 34 So. 2d 467; 1948 Ala. LEXIS 561



March 18, 1948 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Calhoun County; Lamar Field, Judge.

Action to recover salary as police officer by John Douglas against the City of Anniston. From a judgment for plaintiff, defendant appeals. Transferred from Court of Appeals under Code 1940, Tit. 13, § 102.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed conditionally.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city challenged the decision of the Circuit Court, Calhoun County (Alabama), which found in favor of defendant policeman in his action that alleged that the city owed him his salary for the time that the policeman was illegally suspended without pay.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff policeman was suspended from his job without pay for 45 days. The policeman filed an action against defendant city for back pay and alleged that the suspension was illegal. The trial court found in favor of the policeman. On review, the court found that the policeman was not serving under contract, but under law. Furthermore, the policeman had a common law action of debt because his suspension was invalid. The court reasoned that Ala. Code Tit. 62, § 392 et seq. (1940) provided that a policeman could only be suspended for 30 days without a hearing. The policeman did not receive a hearing and his suspension was in excess of 30 days. Therefore, the trial court's decision was affirmed though modified to reflect the accurate amount of wages that remained unpaid.


OUTCOME: The trial court's decision that found in favor of the policeman was affirmed and modified to reflect an accurate figure regarding the amount of money owed to the policeman as unpaid wages.

 

916 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Land v. Cooper


No. 2 Div. 239


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


250 Ala. 271; 34 So. 2d 313; 1948 Ala. LEXIS 537



February 26, 1948 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Choctaw County; Joe M. Pelham, Jr., Judge.

Bill in equity by L. M. Cooper, and revived in the name of Jennie Cooper and others as substituted complainants, against Robert Land and John Land, to set aside a mortgage foreclosure and to redeem. From a decree overruling a demurrer to the bill as amended, respondents appeal.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and in part reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mortgagee sought review of a judgment by the Circuit Court of Choctaw County (Alabama), which overruled his demurrer to a complaint by appellees, a personal representative and the heirs of the original plaintiff, on a bill in equity to set aside a mortgage foreclosure, or in the alternative, to exercise a right of redemption.


OVERVIEW: The original plaintiff was the son of the mortgagor of property. Prior to the mortgagor's death, the mortgagor allegedly entered into a timber contract with the mortgagee that extended the time for payment of the mortgage by five years. When the mortgagor died before the passage of five years, the mortgagee held a foreclosure sale. The son brought a bill in equity to set aside the foreclosure sale or to exercise the right of redemption. The circuit court overruled the mortgagee's demurrer. The court rejected the circuit court's ruling that a bill in equity could be brought to exercise the right of redemption. The court held that the right of redemption abated at the death of the mortgagor and subsequent legislation could not revive the right that had already abated at the time of the legislation's enactment. Thus, the demurrer should have be sustained as to the exercise of the right of redemption. The court upheld that portion of the ruling relating to the request to set aside the foreclosure sale. The alleged timber contract did not violate the statute of frauds because it was capable of being performed within one year even though it was for a term of five years.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that part of the circuit court's judgment as to the request to set aside the mortgage foreclosure, but reversed that part of the judgment relating to the exercise of the right of redemption. The cause was remanded for further proceedings.

 

917 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Weill v. State


No. 3 Div. 479


SUPREME COURT OF ALABAMA


250 Ala. 328; 34 So. 2d 132; 1948 Ala. LEXIS 554



January 15, 1948 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 11, 1948.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court, Montgomery County; Walter B. Jones, Judge.

Proceeding in the nature of quo warranto by the State, on the relation of M. W. Gaillard, against Murray Weill, individually, and doing business as Serv-U Dental Laboratory, to exclude defendant from practicing dentistry without license. From a judgment for plaintiff, defendant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee State brought a quo warranto action in the Circuit Court, Montgomery County (Alabama) to prevent appellant dental technician from practicing dentistry without a license. The trial court rendered judgment for the State. The dental technician appealed.


OVERVIEW: The dental technician was not a licensed dentist and was repairing old dental appliances and constructing new dental appliances from molds made from old dentures without instructions or authorization from licensed dentists. The dental technician was delivering the newly constructed or repaired dental appliances directly to patients without authorization from a licensed dentist and charging the patients directly. He alleged that he was not practicing dentistry because he was not making impressions directly of patients' mouths. The court held that the dentist was practicing dentistry without a license. The statute did not require the making of an impression from the patient's mouth. The making of a mold from a pre-existing appliance was sufficient to constitute practicing dentistry without a license. The court held that the statute against practicing dentistry without a license was a valid exercise of the State's police power. The statute did not constitute an unconstitutional restraint on trade by requiring a license to practice dentistry. The right to practice dentistry was subject to the State's obligation to protect the public.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the State in its quo warranto action to prevent the dental technician from continuing to practice dentistry without a license.

Siebert v. State


CR-98-0868


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


778 So. 2d 842; 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 295



December 30, 1999, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected March 9, 2000. Rehearing Denied April 21, 2000. As Amended May 22, 2000. The Name of this Case has been Corrected by the Court June 22, 2000. Released for Publication January 30, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Talladega Circuit Court. (CV-92-319). William C. Sullivan, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appeal from a judgment of the Talladega Circuit Court (Alabama) denying appellant postconviction relief filed pursuant to Ala. R. Crim. P. 32 for his two capital murder convictions.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review from the circuit court's denial of his two petitions for postconviction relief filed pursuant to Ala. R. Crim. P. 32. The petitions challenged two capital murder convictions and sentences of death by electrocution. The court affirmed the conviction. The circuit court should not have addressed the rule's procedurally barred claims on the merits because the two-year statute of limitations had run. Considering those claims on the merits which were not procedurally barred, the court held, inter alia, that appellant's contention of jury misconduct was not newly discovered evidence because issues of bias and preconceived beliefs concerning the imposition of the death penalty could have been raised at trial and on direct appeal.


OUTCOME: The court denied appellant's petitions because the two-year statute of limitation barred appellant's claims of newly discovered evidence.

Thomas v. State


CR-96-0876


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


824 So. 2d 1; 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 298



December 30, 1999, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected February 14, 2000. As Amended May 22, 2000. As Amended June 22, 2000. Opinion on Remand of June 30, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 216. As Corrected July 1, 2002. Released for Publication August 9, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Mobile Circuit Court. (CC-96-1040). Edward B. McDermott, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appeal from the Mobile Circuit Court (Alabama), which convicted appellant of capital murder during a rape in the first degree and murder during a burglary in the first degree, and upon the jury's unanimous recommendation and view of four aggravating circumstances, sentenced appellant to death.


OVERVIEW: A victim of strangulation and knife cuts was found dead. DNA in her vaginal fluid was a one-in-three-hundred-million match with that of appellant, who was seen with items missing from victim's home. Appellant was convicted of capital murder during a rape in the first degree and murder during a burglary in the first degree. Noting four aggravating circumstances and following the jury's unanimous recommendation, the circuit court sentenced appellant to death. On appeal, the court found no basis for concluding that any error in the guilt phase of the trial that seriously affected the fairness, integrity, or public reputation of the proceedings. Indeed, the court said, reversal of appellant's conviction would have that effect. However, pursuant to the attorney general's request, the case was remanded so that a proper and complete sentencing order could be entered that met the requirements of Ala. Code § 13A-5-47.


OUTCOME: The court remanded to the circuit court, but only so that a proper and complete sentencing order could be entered, because in the guilt phase of appellant's trial the court found no basis for concluding that any error seriously affected the fairness, integrity, or public reputation of the proceedings.

 

920 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Woods v. State


CR-97-0027


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


789 So. 2d 896; 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 276



December 10, 1999, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 28, 2000. As Amended May 22, 2000. As Corrected February 5, 2001. Released for Publication July 19, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from St. Clair Circuit Court. (CC-96-108A). Robert E. Austin, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the St. Clair Circuit Court (Alabama), convicting him of murder made capital because the murder was committed during the course of a robbery, Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(2) (1975), and sentencing him to death by electrocution.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of capital murder for killing a convenience store clerk during the process of robbing the store. As a result, defendant was sentenced to death by electrocution. Defendant first argued that the trial court erred in denying his application for treatment under the Youthful Offender Act. The court found that the trial court complied with the law and that its decision was not arbitrary. Defendant next argued that his indictment should have been quashed because the venire from which the grand and petit juries were chosen failed to reflect a fair cross-section of the community. The court found no evidence supporting this contention. Next, defendant argued that the State's failure to transcribe the grand jury proceedings denied his right to due process, his right to a fair trial, and his right to confront the witnesses against him. The court stated that in Alabama there was no statute requiring that testimony before a grand jury be recorded.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed; court found no reversible error on defendant's numerous arguments.

 

921 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Perkins v. State


CR-93-1931


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


808 So. 2d 1041; 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 253



November 19, 1999, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected April 7, 2000. Released for Publication February 21, 2002. As Corrected April 8, 2002. As Corrected June 10, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Tuscaloosa Circuit Court. (CC-92-478). Gay M. Lake, Jr., TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Tuscaloosa Circuit Court (Alabama) for murder made capital because it was committed during the course of a kidnapping in the first degree, Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of capital murder. The jury, by a vote of 10-2, recommended that defendant be sentenced to death. In affirming defendant's conviction and sentence, the court held inter alia: (1) it was constitutionally permissible for the jurors to agree on a unanimous verdict without necessarily unanimously agreeing that defendant either had the intent to sexually abuse the victim or physically harm her since the two intents were conceptually similar for purposes of the intent element for first degree kidnapping; (2) the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant's motion for a change of venue; (3) the trial court did not err in allowing the victim's husband to sit at the prosecution's table during the trial; and (4) the evidence of defendant's alleged collateral rapes was material and logically relevant to show defendant's intent and motive in committing the charged crime.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and death sentence were affirmed. The trial court did not abuse its discretion by admitting testimony regarding the two rapes allegedly committed by defendant in the two weeks preceding victim's abduction and murder.

Bryant v. State


CR-98-0023


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


951 So. 2d 702; 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 254



November 19, 1999, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Released for Publication March 23, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Bryant v. State, 2000 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 3530 (Ala. Crim. App., Jan. 28, 2000)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by Ex parte Bryant, 951 So. 2d 724, 2002 Ala. LEXIS 195 (Ala., 2002)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by Bryant v. State, 2011 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 1 (Ala. Crim. App., Feb. 4, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Houston Circuit Court. (CC-97-403). S. Edward Jackson, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant criminal defendant challenged the Houston Circuit Court's (Alabama) conviction pursuant to Ala. Code § § 13A-5-40(a)(1) (1975) of murder made capital because it was committed during a kidnapping in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted pursuant to Ala. Code § § 13A-5-40(a)(1) (1975) of capital murder because it was committed during a first-degree kidnapping. On appeal, appellant claimed that the trial court erred in granting appellee state's challenge for cause as to a prospective juror. The record showed that although the man indicated that he could vote guilty and impose the death penalty in a circumstantial evidence case, his answers to other questions suggested that he would be unable to find defendant guilty and to recommend the death penalty. In light of the man's vacillating answers, and in deference to the trial judge, who in addition to hearing the words spoken by the prospective juror had the opportunity to observe his demeanor and appearance, his manner of speech and tone of voice, and his body language during his responses, the court did not find that the trial court abused its discretion.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in granting appellee state's challenge for cause as to a prospective juror whose answers were at times contradictory because the trial judge was in the best position to determine which of the juror's answers were said with the greatest certainty.

 

923 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Wilson v. State


CR-97-2569


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


777 So. 2d 856; 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 268



November 19, 1999, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 7, 2000. As Amended November 17, 2000. Released for Publication January 30, 2001. As Corrected August 6, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Madison Circuit Court (CC-97-164). Edward D. Fay, Jr., TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, convicted of capital murder for the killings of four men and sentenced to death, challenged the judgment of the Madison Circuit Court (Alabama), raising numerous issues on appeal.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of capital murder in the execution-style killing of four men and sentenced to death by electrocution. Appellant challenged the judgment of the trial court. The judgment was affirmed. The evidence amply supported that although appellant intentionally killed only one person, he was responsible as an accomplice for the murder of the other three decedents. The testimony of the survivors of appellant's rampage testified as to the torture the decedents suffered before their deaths, which was relevant in determining whether the especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel aggravating circumstances applied regarding the gravity of the sentence. It was determined that the degree of heinousness, atrociousness, and cruelty that characterized this offense exceeded that which is common to all capital offenses. Therefore, the sentence of death was neither disproportionate nor excessive. Searching the entire record for any error that may have adversely affected appellant's substantial rights, no error was found.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. Although appellant argued that he intentionally killed only one person, he was responsible, as an accomplice, for killing the other three decedents as per overwhelming evidence that amply supported the jury's conclusion. The capital offense was especially heinous, atrocious, and cruel, warranting imposition of the death penalty.

 

924 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Minor v. State


CR-95-1968


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


780 So. 2d 707; 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 252



October 29, 1999, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected January 14, 2000. Opinion After Remand of September 29, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 119. Released for Publication January 31, 2001. As Corrected August 6, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Tuscaloosa Circuit Court. (CC-95-1118). Thomas S. Wilson, TRIAL JUDGE.

This Opinion Substituted on Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of August 27, 1999, Previously Reported at: 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 219.



DISPOSITION: APPLICATION OVERRULED; MOTION DENIED; OPINION OF AUGUST 27, 1999, WITHDRAWN; OPINION SUBSTITUTED; AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of judgement of the Tuscaloosa Circuit Court (Alabama), convicting him of the capital offense of murder when the victim is less than 14 years old pursuant to Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(15) (1975), and sentencing him to death by electrocution.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of capital murder pursuant to Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(15) (1975). Appellant's new trial motion was denied. Appellant challenged, raising issues not presented at trial. The court held in capital cases, failure to raise claims at trial did not prevent review for plain error, although it weighed against defendant for claims of prejudice. The court discussed 41 separate issues. The court denied appellant's procedural claims and claims of improper admission of evidence because these issues were within the provenance of trial court which did not abuse its discretion in its rulings. The court discussed appellant's arrest and self-incriminating statement, and determined both had been obtained in compliance with constitutional mandates and were proper and admissible. The court determined that the venire was properly screened for bias and that peremptory strikes were not discriminatory. Finally, the court denied U.S. Const. amend. VIII claims, holding execution by electrocution was constitutional.


OUTCOME: Conviction and sentence affirmed, because the trial court did not abuse its discretion in procedural evidentiary issues, defendant's arrest and self-incriminating statement followed constitutional mandates, venire was properly screened for bias and jury selection was not discriminatory, and execution by electrocution was constitutional.

Nicks v. State


CR-96-2446


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


783 So. 2d 895; 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 235



October 1, 1999, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 12, 1999. As Corrected January 14, 2000. Released for Publication May 22, 2001. As Corrected August 6, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court, Bessemer Division (CC-83-359.60). Daniel J. Reynolds, Jr., TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner criminal defendant appealed from the Jefferson Circuit Court's (Alabama) denial of relief as to his conviction of capital murder.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of murder made capital because it was committed during a robbery. Following the jury recommendation, the trial court sentenced him to death. Petitioner's conviction and sentence were affirmed on appeal. Petitioner sought to file a post-conviction motion, which was denied. On appeal, petitioner claimed that the state's administration of lithium to him three days before trial created a substantial doubt as to his ability to consult with his lawyer with a reasonable degree of rational understanding. Petitioner also claimed ineffective assistance of counsel, based on his counsel's failure to move for a competency hearing. The court affirmed petitioner's conviction because it found that the trial court made an adequate inquiry into petitioner's competency to stand trial, and because it found that petitioner failed to establish that, but for counsel's performance, the outcome of his appeal would have been different.


OUTCOME: Petitioner's capital murder conviction was affirmed because the court found that the trial court made an adequate inquiry into petitioner's competency to stand trial, and because petitioner failed to establish that, but for counsel's performance, the outcome of his appeal would have been different.

 

926 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Brown v. State


CR-98-0343


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


807 So. 2d 1; 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 238



October 1, 1999, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected October 18, 1999. As Amended June 22, 2000. Released for Publication January 11, 2002. As Corrected April 8, 2002. As Corrected May 13, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Montgomery Circuit Court. (CC-87-1464.60). Charles Price, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant convicted felon appealed from the judgment of the Montgomery Circuit Court (Alabama), denying his petition for postconviction relief filed pursuant to Ala. R. Crim. P. 32, challenging his convictions and death sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant felon, on parole for a second time, murdered two females, was convicted and sentenced to death. Defendant filed a petition pursuant to Ala. R. Crim. P. 32 for postconviction relief challenging his convictions and the death sentence. Defendant argued that he was denied his right to a fair trial by having prospective jurors answer questions truthfully when one prospective juror, during voir dire, failed to disclose that he had been the victim of an armed robbery. Defendant also contended that his constitutional right to effective assistance of counsel at both the guilt and penalty phase of the trial was violated. Judgment was affirmed. The court concluded that defendant failed to provide evidence that he was prejudiced by one juror's involvement in a robbery 20 years previously, especially since the jury unanimously recommended that the death penalty be imposed. Defendant also failed to demonstrate that but for counsel's ineffective assistance, he would not have been sentenced to death.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. Juror-misconduct claim was invalid; there was no evidence that defendant was prejudiced by juror's involvement as victim of robbery 20 years prior to trial, and jury unanimously recommended death sentence. Defendant could not prevail on claim of ineffective assistance of counsel; defendant failed to show that he would not have been sentenced to death, but for counsel's ineffective assistance.

 

927 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Burnett v. State


CR-98-0543


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


807 So. 2d 573; 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 221



September 17, 1999, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected January 24, 2000. As Corrected March 9, 2000. As Corrected February 5, 2001. As Corrected April 26, 2002. As Corrected May 13, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Winston Circuit Court. (CC-95-190). Bobby R. Aderholt, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant-appellant sought review of the denial of his motion for a new trial following his conviction for vehicular homicide under Ala. Code § 32-5A-192 (1975) from the Winston Circuit Court (Alabama).


OVERVIEW: Defendant-appellant was convicted of three counts of vehicular homicide in violation of Ala. Code § 32-5A-192 (1975). He filed a motion for a new trial arguing that the vehicular homicide statute was unconstitutional because it imposed felony sanctions in the absence of a culpable mental state, that the State did not prove the corpus delicti of the homicides, that trial court erred in allowing evidence of a drag-sled test, and in the conditions placed on probation. Motion was denied and he sought review. Court affirmed finding that term "unlawfully" in statute defined necessary culpable state and, therefore, the statute was constitutional. Court found that State did prove the corpus delicti because evidence established the death of the victims' named in the indictment and that defendant-appellant caused the deaths. Finally, defendant-appellant did not preserve his objections to the drag-sled test or the probation conditions and the court would not review those arguments.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed finding that vehicular homicide statute was constitutional, that the State did prove the corpus delicti of the homicides, that the defendant-appellant did not properly preserve his objection to scientific evidence, and that defendant-appellant did not preserve his objection to conditions of probation.

Duncan v. State


CR-95-1544


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


827 So. 2d 838; 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 224



September 17, 1999, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 3, 1999. As Corrected February 5, 2001. Rehearing Denied February 8, 2002. Released for Publication September 12, 2002.
Affirmed by Ex parte Duncan, 827 So. 2d 861, 2001 Ala. LEXIS 81 (Ala., 2001)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by Duncan v. State, 925 So. 2d 245, 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 78 (Ala. Crim. App., 2005)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by State v. Duncan, 2014 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 65 (Ala. Crim. App., Sept. 5, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court. (CC-94-3624). Michael W. McCormick, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of judgment of the Jefferson Circuit Court (Alabama) that entered convictions for capital offenses, murder committed during a kidnapping and murder committed during a robbery, and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Victim was hitchhiking along interstate highway. Appellant and three other teenagers, who had been drinking alcohol and smoking marijuana, picked her up. They took her to a wooded area. They kicked and stomped her head and body for 30 minutes until she died. Subsequently, they mutilated her dead body. Appellants took vehicle to car wash, removed victim's belongings, and placed them in the woods. Medical examiner established cause of death as blunt force trauma to the head. On appeal, appellant argued that there was no evidence of kidnapping because victim was a willing passenger. Court found evidence that victim was held against her will. Appellant also argued that there was no evidence of robbery. Court disagreed because taking of property did not need to occur prior to killing. Jury could have reasonably inferred that stealing victim's luggage and personal items was part of overall scheme to dispose of incriminating evidence.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; court found sufficient evidence to support appellant's convictions and death sentence. Court found that trial court did not abuse its discretion in its admission of certain demonstrative evidence and hearsay testimony. Court also rejected appellant's challenge to racial composition of the jury.

Carroll v. State


CR-97-1019


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


852 So. 2d 801; 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 204



August 27, 1999, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected February 14, 2000. Opinion on Remand of November 19, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 263. Rehearing Denied January 28, 2000. Certiorari Granted April 20, 2001. Rehearing Denied November 21, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court. (CC-95-4275). Alfred Bahakel, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS TO THE CONVICTION; REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS AS TO SENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the Jefferson Circuit Court (Alabama) of capital murder in violating of Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(2) (1975), alleging it was improper to deny his motion to suppress certain custodial statements and to deny his motion for a judgment of acquittal.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for capital murder in violation of Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(2) (1975) and remanded the case for new findings on defendant's aggravating and mitigating circumstances and a reevaluation of the sentence. The court found that defendant's two custodial statements were voluntary and were properly admitted at trial after looking at the totality of circumstances. The statements were made after defendant was advised of his juvenile-Miranda rights, no favorable treatment was promised, and no coercion or inducement occurred. The court ruled that the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction because the evidence supported a finding that defendant intended to kill the victim and the evidence showed defendant was the triggerman. The court noted that the jury was properly instructed on complicity and the intent necessary for a capital conviction. The case was remanded because when the trial court overrode the jury's sentencing recommendation and imposed the death sentence, it had improperly considered defendant's youthful offender adjudications as convictions negating a mitigating circumstance of no history of prior criminal activity.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for capital murder was affirmed because sufficient evidence supported the verdict. The evidence showed defendant intended to kill the victim and that he was the triggerman. The court remanded the case for sentencing because the trial court improperly considered defendant's youthful offender adjudications as convictions to negate a mitigating circumstance of no significant history of prior criminal activity.

 

930 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


McWhorter v. State


CR-93-1448


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


781 So. 2d 257; 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 212



August 27, 1999, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 3, 1999. As Corrected March 9, 2000. As Corrected August 21, 2000. Released for Publication February 15, 2001. As Corrected August 6, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Marshall Circuit Court. (CC-93-77A). W.C. Gullahorn, Jr., TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the order of the Marshall Circuit Court (Alabama) convicting him of capital murder during the course of committing a robbery, in violation of Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(2).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of capital murder during the course of committing robbery, in violation of Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(2). Appellant brought 30 claims challenging his conviction. The court affirmed appellant's conviction because appellant failed to present any evidence as to why his conviction was erroneous. Among other things, appellant argued the trial court failed to instruct the jury on lesser included offenses. However, the court found no plain error where appellant's proposed instructions would have been incompatible with appellant's defenses in the case. In addition, appellant argued that the trial court improperly excluded a venireperson from serving on the jury. The appeals court held that appellant suffered no prejudice because of the removal of the juror and that she could have properly been struck for cause. Appellant argued he was denied due process and a fair trial due to the trial court's failure to order a change of venue. The court disagreed, holding that that appellant failed to show actual prejudice, or that the community was so saturated with pretrial publicity as to deny him a fair and impartial trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction of capital murder because he failed to provide any evidence that the conviction was imposed in error or that it was obtained in violation of his constitutional rights.

 

931 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Whitehead v. State


CR-95-2129


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


777 So. 2d 781; 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 213



August 27, 1999, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended October 18, 1999. Rehearing Denied October 22, 1999. Released for Publication January 30, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Marshall Circuit Court. (CC-95-200095). William D. Jetton, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the trial court's acceptance of the jury's recommendation of death after he was convicted of capital murder during a burglary in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of three counts of capital murder in connection with murder of a witness who had testified against him before a grand jury that had indicted appellant for theft. The murder was made capital (1) because it was committed during a burglary in the first degree; (2) because the victim, at the time of his murder, had testified before a grand jury that had indicted appellant for theft in the first degree; and (3) because the victim, at the time of his murder, had been subpoenaed to testify at appellant's trial on theft charge. The appellate court affirmed appellant's death sentence. The court rejected as meritless most of appellant's contentions that many pretrial rulings were erroneous. The court discussed appellant's objections to jury venire, the voir dire procedures, claims of juror bias, and trial court's refusal to grant a change of venue, and concluded that such objections were meritless. The court reviewed appellant's claims of double jeopardy, improper jury instructions, the presence of victim's family in courtroom, and the admission of certain evidence for plain error, because appellant failed to raise objections during trial, thus inviting error.


OUTCOME: In affirming appellant's death sentence, the court held that the pretrial publicity in the case did not so pervasively saturate the community as to render court proceedings nothing more than a hollow formality. Furthermore, the court rejected appellant's contention that his convictions for both burglary and capital murder based upon the same act violated double jeopardy; however, appellant was only convicted of capital murder.

 

932 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Hammonds v. State


CR-97-0722


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


777 So. 2d 750; 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 217



August 27, 1999, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected September 20, 1999. Rehearing Denied October 22, 1999. Released for Publication January 30, 2001.
Affirmed by Ex parte Hammonds, 777 So. 2d 777, 2000 Ala. LEXIS 238 (Ala., 2000)
Subsequent appeal at Hammonds v. State, 925 So. 2d 1009, 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 273 (Ala. Crim. App., 2005)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Judgment entered by, Motion denied by, As moot Hammonds v. Allen, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 41326 (M.D. Ala., Mar. 27, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Houston Circuit Court. (CC-96-712). Larry K. Anderson, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the Houston Circuit Court (Alabama), entering judgment of conviction of capital murder in violation of Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(3) and sentencing him to death.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted appellant of capital murder and sentenced him to die. On appeal, the court affirmed. The trial court did not violate appellant's rights against unlawful search and seizure under U.S. Const. amend. IV by refusing to suppress DNA within a blood sample taken while appellant was incarcerated. The state's interest in identifying criminals outweighed appellant's interest in the seizure of his blood, and although the blood was not drawn in accordance with promulgated regulations, the regulations did not supply appellant with substantive rights. Ala. Code § 36-18-25 did not create a right to refuse the blood sample. The trial court did not err by admitting the DNA evidence as the prosecution presented proof of the reliability and relevance of the population frequency statistical evidence under Ala. Code § 36-18-30. The trial court properly denied appellant's motion for a mistrial where the prosecutor said, referring to appellant, "let him testify," and the judge instructed the jury to disregard the remark. The court upheld the death sentence because no error injuring appellant's rights was apparent, and the sentence was not disproportionate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and sentence; the trial court properly allowed the prosecution to introduce DNA evidence because appellant could not show that the taking of the blood sample violated appellant's right to protection from unlawful search and seizure, or that he had a right to refuse the sample, and because the prosecution established the reliability and relevance of the statistical evidence.

City of Montgomery v. Norman


CR-98-0837


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


816 So. 2d 72; 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 220



August 27, 1999, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 10, 1999. As Corrected November 19, 1999. Released for Publication May 2, 2002. As Corrected July 27, 2002. As Corrected September 6, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Montgomery Circuit Court. (CC-98-5242). Tracy S. McCooey, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the city, sought relief from Montgomery Circuit Court (Alabama), which granted appellee's motion to dismiss charges filed against her for creating a public nuisance by having weeds over 12 inches high in her yard, a violation of a municipal code.


OVERVIEW: Appellee was convicted of creating a public nuisance by having weeds over 12 inches in her yard, a violation of a municipal code, Montgomery, Ala., Ordinance No. 37-91, Article VII, § 1. The municipal court fined appellee and ordered her to pay court costs. She appealed her conviction and moved to dismiss the charges against her, alleging that the ordinance was unconstitutional because it was vague, overbroad and violated her due process, equal protection, free speech, and property rights. The circuit court granted the motion to dismiss, and the city appealed. The court reversed, finding that the term "weed" contained in the ordinance was not vague or overbroad. Additionally, the court found that no taking of appellee's property occurred, and even if it did, the city was not required to compensate appellee. The ordinance was a reasonable exercise of the city's police power, and the city required appellee to cut the plants because they constituted a nuisance. Appellee's constitutional challenges to the ordinance lacked merit.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of charges against appellee, finding that the term "weed" contained in the ordinance was not vague or overbroad and finding that the ordinance was a reasonable exercise of the city's police power.

Ingram v. State

935 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Samra v. State


CR-97-1543


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


771 So. 2d 1108; 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 171



June 18, 1999, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 21, 2000. As Corrected March 16, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Shelby Circuit Court. (CC-97-384). J. Michael Joiner, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction for capital murder and of his death sentence, both entered in the Shelby Circuit Court (Alabama), challenging the validity of Ala. Code §§ 15-12-21, -22. Appellant also challenged the denial of his motion for a change of venue, the trial court's use of Witherspoon questions, the admission of photographs of the victims and a videotape of the crime scene, and the effectiveness of defense counsel.


OVERVIEW: The appellant and three codefendants planned to kill one man. To conceal this murder, they also killed three additional victims who were present at the scene. Appellant was convicted of capital murder because the jury found that he committed the killings by one act or pursuant to one scheme or course of conduct under Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(10) (1975). He was sentenced to death by electrocution. The reviewing court affirmed his conviction and sentence. It first rejected his claim that Ala. Code §§ 15-12-21, -22 (1975) was invalid, finding that the Alabama Supreme Court had approved the compensation scheme for attorneys representing indigent defendants. The court also upheld the denial of appellant's motion for a change of venue, finding that he failed to show either actual or presumptive prejudice toward him. Additionally, the court rejected appellant's claims that the trial court erred in propounding Witherspoon questions to potential jurors, and in admitting photographs of the victims and a videotape of the crime scene. His ineffective assistance of counsel claim was likewise rejected because the decisions his counsel made were trial strategy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction and death sentence, holding that no reversible error was committed in the denial of his motion for change of venue where he failed to show actual or presumptive prejudice. The court also rejected appellant's claims regarding his attorney's assistance and statutory limits on compensation, the admission of certain evidence, and the propounding of Witherspoon questions.

 

936 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Jackson v. State


CR-97-2050


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


836 So. 2d 915; 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 136



May 28, 1999, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected June 18, 1999. Rehearing Denied July 9, 1999. Released for Publication January 10, 2003. As Corrected May 21, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Montgomery Circuit Court. (CC-97-2300). TRIAL JUDGE: Willaim R. Gordon and Tracy S. McCooey.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed an appeal from a judgment of the Montgomery Circuit Court (Alabama), which convicted appellant of murder made captial because it occurred during the commission of a robbery in the first degree, convicted appellant of first-degree theft, sentenced appellant to death by electrocution for the capital offense, and sentenced appellant, as a habitual offender with three prior felony convictions, to life imprisonment for the theft.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, packing a pistol and driving a car stolen by appellant's fellow gang member upon appellant's request, was accompanied by his armed gang when he decided to rob victim because victim had a good stereo system in his car. Appellant followed victim's car, pulled the stolen car in front of victim's car, and shot victim. Appellant was convicted of capital murder during the commission of a robbery in the first degree. Although the jury, by a 12-0 vote, recommended life imprisonment without the possibility of parole, the trial court overrode the jury's recommendation and sentenced appellant to death by electrocution. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court found, among other things, that the trial court properly granted a motion in limine that prevented appellant from presenting evidence that victim was a drug dealer. A detective's misrepresentation about finding fingerprints did not make appellant's confession involuntary. Taken as a whole, the trial court's jury instruction properly conveyed the concept of reasonable doubt to the jury, and it did not lessen the state's burden of proof. The jury override provision of Ala. Code § 13A-5-47(e) (1975) was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that convicted appellant of capital murder and theft and sentenced appellant to death by electrocution and life imprisonment because the trial court's jury instruction properly conveyed the concept of reasonable doubt to the jury and the jury's recommended sentence was permissibly overridden.

 

937 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


State v. C.M.


CR-98-0447


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


746 So. 2d 410; 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 119



May 5, 1999, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Rehearing Denied July 2, 1999. As Corrected October 4, 1999. As Corrected October 18, 1999. Released for Publication January 21, 2000. As Amended March 27, 2000. As Corrected May 11, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Jefferson Circuit Court. (JU-96-52500.01 and 96-51630). Sandra R. Storm, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The parties challenged the judgment of the Jefferson Circuit Court (Alabama), which held that while not violative of the equal protection clause, 1998 Ala. Acts 98-489, an amendment to the Community Notification Act, Ala. Code § 15-20-20, did violate the ex post facto clause of the United States Constitution.


OVERVIEW: Appellees, juvenile sex offenders, sought to stay enforcement of 1998 Ala. Acts 98-489, an amendment to the Community Notification Act, Ala. Code § 15-20-20 (the Act). Appellees contended that the Act violated their right to equal protection of the law because the Act permitted a convicted adult sex offender to return to a home where a minor child resides, but did not afford them the same right as juveniles. While the trial court found that the Act did not deny appellees equal protection of the law, it did find that it violated the ex post facto clause of the United States Constitution because it created a penalty not prescribed when appellees were adjudicated. Appellant state challenged those portions of the trial court opinion that found the Act unconstitutional, and appellees challenged those portions that found the Act did not violate equal protection. On appeal, the court found that on its face, the Act violated the equal protection clause. The court held that even under the lowest tier of review, there was no rational basis for treating adult sex offenders differently than juvenile sex offenders. The court also found that the amendment violated the ex post facto clause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which found that the Community Notification Act was unconstitutional as applied to juveniles, because it violated both the equal protection clause and the ex post facto clause to the United States Constitution.

Greenhill v. State


CR-97-2310


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


746 So. 2d 1064; 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 46



April 30, 1999, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected May 14, 1999. As Corrected September 20, 1999. Released for Publication January 21, 2000. As Corrected January 24, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Franklin Circuit Court. (CC-98-006). John D. Jolly, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS TO CONVICTIONS FOR MURDER AND ATTEMPTED MURDER AND AS TO SENTENCE FOR THE MURDER CONVICTION; REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS FOR RESENTENCING ON THE ATTEMPTED MURDER CONVICTION. *



* Note from the reporter of decisions: On July 9, 1999, on return to remand, the Court of Criminal Appeals affirmed, without opinion. On August 6, 1999, that court denied rehearing, without opinion. On October 22, 1999, the Supreme Court denied certiorari review, without opinion (1982047).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision from the Franklin Circuit Court (Alabama), which convicted appellant of murder and attempted murder.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of murder and attempted murder after appellant shot the victim. He sought review of his convictions and argued that the trial court erred when it did not grant a witness immunity or admit the transcript of her grand jury testimony into evidence after she invoked her U.S. Const. amend. V right against self-incrimination. He also argued that the trial court provided an improper definition of reasonable doubt. Finally, appellant argued that the trial court erred when it granted the state's motion in limine to prevent the defense from raising allegations that the deceased was HIV positive. The court affirmed the convictions and found that the trial court did not err when it failed to grant a witness immunity or to admit her grand jury testimony because appellant failed to make an offer of proof that the witness's testimony was relevant to the subject matter of the prosecution. The trial court's definition of reasonable doubt was proper because when the instruction was read as a whole, there was no reasonable likelihood that the jury misapplied the instruction. The court did not review the motion made in limine because appellant waived the objection.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions for attempted murder and murder because the trial court properly instructed the jury on reasonable doubt and because appellant failed to preserve several issues for review. The court remanded for resentencing on the attempted murder conviction because the trial court did not sentence appellant to the mandatory minimum.

Benson v. City of Sheffield


CR-98-0280


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


737 So. 2d 1059; 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 48



April 30, 1999, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected August 20, 1999. Released for Publication August 27, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Colbert Circuit Court. (CC-98-250). N. Pride Tompkins, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Accepting defendant's plea of guilty to a charge of harassment in violation of a local ordinance that adopted Ala. Code § 13A-11-8(a)(1)(b) (1975), the Colbert Circuit Court (Alabama) imposed a sentence of 90 days' imprisonment, suspended "on general good behavior" for two years, and ordered defendant to pay a fine and court costs. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Based on his guilty plea, defendant was convicted of harassment in violation of a city ordinance that adopted Ala. Code § 13A-11-8(a)(1)(b) (1975). The trial court sentenced defendant to 90 days' imprisonment and ordered him to pay a fine and court costs. Defendant's sentence was suspended "on general good behavior" for two years. Defendant did not receive actual jail time in sentencing. Defendant appealed and argued that the trial court committed reversible error when it failed to inquire sua sponte into his indigency status and to appoint a lawyer to represent him before allowing him to enter a guilty plea. The court affirmed. The court held that there was no right to counsel under U.S. Const. amend. VI for defendant to affirmatively waive because defendant's sentence did not include actual imprisonment and because there were no conditions that resulted in defendant's imprisonment before he was placed on probation. Because the Sixth Amendment right to counsel did not exist, the trial court did not err by failing to conduct a sua sponte inquiry to determine whether defendant was indigent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and suspended sentence for harassment. The court held that the trial court did not err in failing to sua sponte inquire into defendant's indigency status because there was no Sixth Amendment right to counsel in a misdemeanor prosecution in which a suspended sentence was imposed.

 

940 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Harris v. State


CR-98-0637


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


741 So. 2d 1112; 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 49



April 30, 1999, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 4, 1999. As Amended October 11, 1999. As Corrected January 14, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court. (CC-96-5433). James H. Hard IV, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS TO CONVICTION AND SENTENCE; REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS TO IMPOSE FINE. *



* Note from the reporter of decisions: On June 18, 1999, on return to remand, the Court of Criminal Appeals affirmed, without opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Jefferson Circuit Court (Alabama), convicting him, upon a jury trial, of trafficking in cocaine, a violation of Ala. Code § 13A-12-231(2) 1975.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of his conviction and sentence for trafficking in cocaine, a violation of Ala. Code § 13A-12-231(2) 1975. The court affirmed the conviction, finding that the charge given by the trial judge to the jury was not improper as it did not suggest which way the verdict should be rendered nor was it in any way coercive or threatening. The court concluded that the trial judge did not have any idea as to which way the jury was leaning when the charge was given, so it could not have attempted to influence a verdict in either direction. The court also found that the evidence supported the conviction of appellant, even though much of it was circumstantial and two of the witnesses consisted of a convicted felon and an informant. The court determined that it was for the jury to determine the weight and sufficiency to be given to the witnesses and any motive they may have had for testifying. The court concluded that the circumstantial evidence was entitled to the same weight as direct evidence, provided it pointed to the guilt of appellant. The court remanded the matter for the imposition of mandatory fines in accordance with § § 13A-12-231(2)(a) and 13A-12-281.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of appellant for trafficking in cocaine, finding the charge given by the trial judge to the jury did not suggest which way the verdict should be rendered nor was it in any way coercive or threatening. The court concluded that the evidence supported the verdict as the jury determined the weight and sufficiency to be given to the testimony of a convicted felon and an informant.

Sneed v. State


CR-95-0587


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


783 So. 2d 841; 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 53



April 30, 1999, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected August 25, 1999. As Corrected August 21, 2000. Released for Publication March 5, 2001.
Reversed by, Remanded by Ex parte Sneed, 783 So. 2d 863, 2000 Ala. LEXIS 280 (Ala., 2000)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Morgan Circuit Court. (CC-93-1307). Sherrie W. Brown, TRIAL JUDGE.
Hardy v. State, 804 So. 2d 247, 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 25 (Ala. Crim. App., 1999)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court, Morgan County (Alabama), which convicted him of the capital offense of murder committed during a robbery in the first degree, Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(2) (1975), and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder committed during a robbery, Ala. Code § 13A-5-40 (a)(2) (1975), and sentenced to death. Defendant raised several arguments on appeal, including that the joinder of his trial with his codefendant over his objection violated his constitutional rights, that the method of selecting the grand jury foreperson was racially discriminatory, and that the prosecutor engaged in misconduct that deprived him of a fundamentally fair trial, due process, and a reliable sentence. The court ruled that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant's motions to sever because he did not meet his burden by showing specific prejudice that warranted a severance. Further, the court held that no prima facie case of discrimination was established. Also, the court found that the prosecutorial comments complained of, regardless of their origin, were accurate descriptions of the crime and supported by facts in the record, and that the comments were not improper under the circumstances. The court affirmed the judgment convicting defendant and sentencing him to death after finding no evidence that the death sentence was imposed under the influence of passion.


OUTCOME: Judgment convicting defendant and sentencing him to death was affirmed where the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant's motions to sever his trial from his codefendant's trial, there was no error warranting reversal, there was no evidence that the sentence was imposed under the influence of passion or prejudice, and the trial court's findings in support of the death sentence were supported by the evidence in the record.

Freeman v. State


CR-95-2080


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


776 So. 2d 160; 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 55

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal defendant appealed the judgment of the Montgomery Circuit Court (Alabama), which found him guilty of all six counts of capital murder charged in the indictment sentenced him to death by electrocution following the jury's recommendation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder committed during a robbery, murder committed during a burglary, murder committed during a rape, and the murder of two or more persons by one act or pursuant to one scheme or course of conduct, all capital offenses. After hearing evidence concerning aggravating and mitigating circumstances, the jury recommended that defendant be sentenced to death by electrocution. On appeal, in accordance with Ala.R.App.P. 45A, the court examined the record for any plain error. The court found no plain error or defect in either in the guilt phase or in the sentencing phase of the trial. The sentence was not imposed under the influence of passion, prejudice, or any other arbitrary factor. The court concluded that the findings and conclusions of the trial court were amply supported by the evidence. After independently weighing the aggravating circumstances against the statutory and non-statutory mitigating circumstances, the court concurred in the trial court's judgment that the aggravating circumstances outweighed the mitigating circumstances, and the sentence of death was neither excessive nor disproportionate to the penalty imposed in similar cases.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions of capital murder and the death sentence because there were no errors in the proceedings, either in the guilt phase or in the sentencing phase of the trial, and death was the appropriate sentence in the case.

Jones v. State


CR-95-1967


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


753 So. 2d 1174; 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 57



April 30, 1999, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 16, 1999. As Corrected August 25, 1999. Released for Publication May 5, 2000. As Amended October 16, 2000.
Writ of habeas corpus denied Jones v. Campbell, 2006 U.S. App. LEXIS 1381 (11th Cir. Ala., Jan. 20, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Blount Circuit Court. (CC-79-093.01). William E. Hereford, TRIAL JUDGE.
Jones v. Alabama, 488 U.S. 871, 109 S. Ct. 182, 102 L. Ed. 2d 151, 1988 U.S. LEXIS 3662, 57 U.S.L.W. 3235 (1988)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court, Blount County (Alabama), which denied his petition for postconviction relief pursuant to Ala. R. Crim. P. 32 that challenged his conviction for capital murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of capital murder. Defendant brought a petition for postconviction relief pursuant to Ala. R. Crim. P. 32. Defendant's Rule 32 petition was denied, and he appealed. He argued that the trial court erred in adopting the state's proposed findings of fact and conclusions of law in its order denying his petition, and that he was denied effective assistance of counsel. The court ruled that the trial court's findings of fact and conclusions of law were supported by the evidence and were not clearly erroneous. Further, the court held that defendant had the burden of showing that his counsel's assistance was ineffective, and that even if his counsel's performance was determined to be deficient, defendant was not entitled to relief unless he established that there was a reasonable probability that, but for counsel's unprofessional errors, the result of the proceeding would have been different. The court affirmed the conviction and concluded that there was a strong presumption that counsel's conduct was appropriate and reasonable and that defendant failed to prove ineffective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: Judgment denying defendant's petition for postconviction relief was affirmed where the trial court's findings of fact and conclusions of law were supported by the evidence and were not clearly erroneous, and defendant failed to prove that he was denied effective assistance of counsel because defendant presented no evidence to show how he was prejudiced by the allegations of ineffective assistance.

Norris v. State


CR-94-0871,


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


793 So. 2d 847; 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 23



March 26, 1999, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected May 14, 1999. The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published August 15, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court. (CC-93-3896). Alfred Bahakel, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Remanded for resentencing. *



* Note from the reporter of decisions: On April 28, 2000, on return to remand, the Court of Criminal Appeals affirmed, without opinion. On June 30, 2000, that Court denied rehearing, without opinion. On March 16, 2001, the Supreme Court denied certiorari review, without opinion (1991956).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the Jefferson Circuit Court (Alabama), which convicted him and sentenced him to death for three murders that arose pursuant to one scheme or course of conduct in violation of Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(10) (1975). Appellant argued that court improperly found, as an aggravating circumstance, that the capital offense was especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel when compared to other capital offenses.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of murdering three individuals by one act or pursuant to one scheme or course of conduct in violation of Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(10) (1975). The trial court sentenced appellant to death after it found, as an aggravating circumstance, that the capital offense was especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel when compared to other capital offenses. Appellant's sentence was vacated and remanded on appeal because the court found that the prosecution had failed to establish beyond a reasonable doubt, as required by Ala. Code § 13A-5-45(e), the aggravating circumstance that the capital offense was especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel when compared to other capital offenses. Specifically, the court found that the evidence was insufficient to satisfy the prosecution's burden of proving beyond a reasonable doubt that the homicides were conscienceless or pitiless homicides that were unnecessarily torturous to the victims. Therefore, the sentence was vacated and remanded for resentencing before the trial court without consideration of the aggravating circumstance that the murders were especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel compared to other capital offenses.


OUTCOME: The trial court's imposition of the death sentence upon appellant was vacated and remanded because the evidence was found to have been insufficient to support the trial court's aggravating circumstance finding that the murders for which appellant had been convicted of had been especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel when compared to other capital offenses.

Maples v. State


CR-97-0548


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


758 So. 2d 1; 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 31



March 26, 1999, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 28, 1999. Released for Publication June 16, 2000. As Amended August 31, 2000.
Affirmed by Ex parte Maples, 758 So. 2d 81, 1999 Ala. LEXIS 315 (Ala., 1999)
Writ denied by Ex parte Maples, 885 So. 2d 845, 2004 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 12 (Ala. Crim. App., 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Morgan Circuit Court. (CC-95-842). Glenn E. Thompson, TRIAL JUDGE.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his convictions on two counts of capital murder and the death penalty sentence imposed by the Morgan Circuit Court (Alabama).


OVERVIEW: Appellant did not specifically challenge sufficiency of the evidence to support his convictions; therefore, the court did not reiterate the evidence presented. However, the court did review the evidence and found it sufficient to support defendant's first-degree murder convictions and death penalty sentence. The court also noted that appellant failed to make appropriate objections during his trial to most of the thirty some points of error; therefore, the court reviewed those points of error for plain error pursuant to Ala. R. Crim. P. 45A. The search conducted by the police of appellant's hotel room was proper, as registered guest consented to search. The court concluded that appellant received a fair trial and affirmed appellant's convictions and sentence.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that appellant received a fair trial and that evidence was sufficient to support his first-degree murder convictions and death penalty. Furthermore, appellant did not show that community was so saturated with prejudicial publicity that he could not receive a fair trial or that any of pretrial publicity actually biased any of the prospective jurors against him, as the jurors were not required to be totally ignorant of facts.

Hardy v. State


CR-95-0589


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


804 So. 2d 247; 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 25



March 26, 1999, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 18, 1999. Released for Publication October 24, 2001. As Corrected July 1, 2002.
Related proceeding at Sneed v. State, 783 So. 2d 841, 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 53 (Ala. Crim. App., 1999)
Affirmed by Ex parte Hardy, 804 So. 2d 298, 2000 Ala. LEXIS 466 (Ala., 2000)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Request denied by Hardy v. Allen, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 145368 (N.D. Ala., Sept. 21, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Morgan Circuit Court (CC-93-1310). Sherrie W. Brown, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment from the Morgan Circuit Court (Alabama) that convicted and sentenced him for the capital offense of murder committed during a robbery, asserting his trial should have been severed from his co-defendant's, the trial court erred in allowing a police officer to identify appellant from a surveillance tape, and the prosecution improperly used the robbery as an element of the crime and as an aggravating circumstance.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of his conviction and sentence for the capital offense of murder committed during a robbery, asserting the joinder of his trial with his co-defendant's violated his rights, the police officer's identification testimony should have been excluded, and the prosecution improperly used the robbery as an element of capital murder and as an aggravating circumstance. The court held joinder of the trials was proper where appellant and his co-defendant were alleged to have participated in the same transaction, and their defenses were not antagonistic to the point of being mutually exclusive. The court held the admission of the police officer's identification testimony was not improper where the identification was cumulative of three other witnesses' identifications, which were clearly admissible because they were better qualified than the jury to correctly identify appellant. The court held the robbery could be considered as an aggravating circumstance where it was listed in Ala. Code § 13A-5-49, and the use of an element of capital murder in that way did not punish appellant twice. Accordingly, the conviction and sentence of death were affirmed.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction and sentence of death were affirmed because joinder of appellant's and his co-defendant's trials was proper where their defenses were not mutually exclusive, the admission of the police officer's identification testimony was not improper where the testimony was cumulative of the admissible testimony of other witnesses, and the prosecution was allowed to use an element of capital murder as an aggravating circumstance.

Melson v. State


CR-95-1681


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


775 So. 2d 857; 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 32



March 26, 1999, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected May 14, 1999. As Corrected May 11, 2000. Released for Publication January 16, 2001. As Corrected May 1, 2001.
Affirmed by Ex parte Melson, 775 So. 2d 904, 2000 Ala. LEXIS 146 (Ala., Apr. 14, 2000)
Post-conviction relief denied at Melson v. State, 902 So. 2d 715, 2004 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 2 (Ala. Crim. App., Jan. 6, 2004)
Related proceeding at Grayson v. Dunn, 156 F. Supp. 3d 1340, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 170914 (M.D. Ala., Dec. 22, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Etowah Circuit Court. (CC-94-925.01 through CC-94-925.06). William W. Cardwell, Jr., TRIAL JUDGE.
Peraita v. State, 725 So. 2d 1075, 1997 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 1569 (Ala. Crim. App., Sept. 26, 1997)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his convictions and death sentence for three counts of capital murder and his conviction of one count of attempted murder for which he received a 40-year prison sentence entered in the Etowah Circuit Court (Alabama).


OVERVIEW: Appellant raised several errors on appeal that were not raised during the trial; however, pursuant to Ala. R. App. P. 45A, his failure to object at trial did not bar appellate review because appellant was sentenced to death. The court discussed all of appellant's alleged errors and found them to be without merit, thus his conviction and sentence were affirmed. While most of the evidence linking appellant to the robbery and murders was circumstantial, that did not render the state's evidence insufficient. In order to obtain a change of venue, appellant was required to show that pre-trial publicity surrounding the case was inherently prejudicial. The court reviewed all of the evidence presented by appellant in support of his motion for change of venue and concluded that most of the reports of the murders and robbery were reasonably factual and objective and were not inflammatory or prejudicial in tone. Thus, the change of venue motion was properly denied. Furthermore, after carefully reviewing the record of the guilt and sentencing phases of the trial, the court found no evidence that the sentence was imposed under the influence of passion, prejudice, or any other arbitrary factor.


OUTCOME: The court reviewed each and every allegation of error as well as the cumulative effect of such alleged errors and found that the alleged errors were without merit. Furthermore, because no single instance of alleged error constituted reversible error, the court did not consider the cumulative effect to be any greater. Thus, appellant's convictions and death sentence on three counts of capital murder were affirmed.
