Pierce v. State


CR-96-1668


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


851 So. 2d 558; 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 20



March 2, 1999, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 30, 1999. Released for Publication July 23, 2003.
Rehearing denied by Pierce v. State, 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 3417 (Ala. Crim. App., Apr. 30, 1999)
Reversed by, Remanded by Ex parte Pierce, 2000 Ala. LEXIS 224 (Ala., May 26, 2000)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Geneva Circuit Court. (CC-88-093.60). P. Ben McLauchlin, Jr., TRIAL JUDGE.
Pierce v. Alabama, 510 U.S. 872, 126 L. Ed. 2d 158, 114 S. Ct. 201, 1993 U.S. LEXIS 5774 (1993)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Geneva Circuit Court (Alabama), denying his petition for post conviction relief filed pursuant to Ala. R. Crim. P. 32, after being convicted of capital murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of capital murder. Defendant filed a petition for post-conviction relief pursuant to Ala. R. Crim. P. 32, and the trial court denied the petition. The court affirmed the order of the trial court. The court held that defendant failed to prove that a sheriff had an improper association with the jurors, that the record did not show that the sheriff was a key state witness, and that defendant failed to show any evidence that he was actually prejudiced by any contacts between the sheriff and the jury. The court held further that defendant failed to prove that the alleged incomplete record of the post-conviction proceedings caused him prejudice. In addition, the court held that defendant's counsel did not render ineffective assistance of counsel. The court held that counsel adequately investigated and presented mitigating evidence and that there was no basis for defendant's claim that counsel did not discover and present exculpatory evidence. The court held further that because there was no rational basis under the evidence presented at trial for jury instructions on intoxication and manslaughter, counsel was not ineffective for not requesting them.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order denying defendant's petition for post-conviction relief, holding that defendant was not rendered ineffective assistance of counsel, was not prejudiced by any contacts between the sheriff and the jury, and was not prejudiced by an alleged incomplete record.

 

949 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Ex parte C.D.M.


CR-97-2402


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


727 So. 2d 897; 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 6



January 14, 1999, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 6, 1999. As Corrected June 1, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Jefferson Juvenile Court. (JU-96-51630). Sandra Ross Storm, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: PETITION FOR THE WRIT OF MANDAMUS DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, mother and son, filed for a writ of mandamus that would direct the court to order a judge to stay enforcement of the Community Notification Act, Ala. Code § 15-20-20 et seq., as applied to petitioner son, who was adjudicated a delinquent on the offense of sodomy, and to hold a full evidentiary hearing.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner son and petitioner mother asserted that the Community Notification Act (act), Ala. Code § 15-20-20(e), violated petitioners' constitutional rights and denied petitioner son equal protection under the law. Under § 15-20-20(e), petitioner son, as a 12 year old criminal sexual offender adjudicated for sodomy, could not live or work within 1000 feet of a public or private school or child care center. Plus, notification of his presence to people living within three miles of petitioners' residence was required. The judge made written findings and asked to stay the enforcement against petitioner son. The judge found the act to be unconstitutional as it applied to juveniles. The act violated the ex post facto clause of the federal constitution in that a 1998 amendment to the act created a penalty that was not proscribed when petitioner son was adjudicated a delinquent. The judge further found the provisions of the act relating to residency and notification requirement were unconstitutionally vague. The act interfered with the rights of parents and children to intimate association under the U.S. Const. amends. I, IX, and XIV. The petition was declared moot.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the petition for writ of mandamus because the judge had entered her written findings in which she asked the court to stay the enforcement of the order of notification as applied to petitioner son, a juvenile, because as applied to juveniles the Community Notification Act was unconstitutional.

 

950 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Ex parte C.M.


CR-97-2253


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


727 So. 2d 898; 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 7



January 14, 1999, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 6, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Jefferson Juvenile Court. (JU-96-52500.01). Sandra Ross Storm, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: PETITION FOR A WRIT OF MANDAMUS DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a mentally retarded 13-year-old adjudicated delinquent on an underlying offense of rape, filed a petition for a writ of mandamus directing the court to order a trial judge for the Tenth Judicial Circuit (Alabama) to stay enforcement of the Community Notification Act, Ala. Code § 15-20-20 et seq. (1975) as that act applied to petitioner. Petitioner's motion for a stay had been denied by the Jefferson Juvenile Court (Alabama).


OVERVIEW: After being adjudicated on an underlying offense of rape, petitioner was placed in the custody of the state youth services and ordered to participate in a sexual offender treatment program. After petitioner had successfully completed the terms of his sentence, he was released to the custody of his mother. After the trial court was notified that Ala. Code § 15-20-20 et seq. (the Act) applied to juvenile offenders, petitioner was transported to the sheriff's department to undergo DNA testing. Petitioner argued that the Act violated his constitutional rights. On receipt of the petition, the court stayed enforcement of the Act temporarily and directed the trial judge to make findings of fact concerning the allegations. The trial judge found that Act to be unconstitutional as it applied to juveniles because it violated the ex post facto clause of the U.S. Constitution and was unconstitutionally vague as to its residency and notification requirements. Therefore, the court found that petitioner had received the relief he requested in his petition for the writ of mandamus and there was no need for the court to stay enforcement of the Act because the petition had become moot.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed petitioner's petition for a writ of mandamus and held that the petition had become moot because the trial judge had found the statute at issue to be unconstitutional as applied to juveniles. Therefore petitioner was found to have received the relief requested.

 

951 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Pardue v. State


CR-97-0551


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


793 So. 2d 838; 1998 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 268



December 18, 1998, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published August 10, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Escambia Circuit Court. (CC-87-135). TRIAL JUDGE: Joseph B. Brogden.



DISPOSITION: REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS. *



* Note from the reporter of decisions: On March 26, 1999, on return to remand, the Court of Criminal Appeals affirmed, without opinion. On May 28, 1999, on application for rehearing, that court withdrew its no-opinion memorandum of March 26, 1999; substituted another memorandum, again affirming without opinion; and denied the application for rehearing. A certiorari petition was filed in the Supreme Court on June 15, 1999; that petition was dismissed on March 15, 2001.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the Escambia Circuit Court (Alabama), which denied his petition for post-conviction relief filed pursuant to Ala. R. Crim. P. 32, in which he attacked his convictions for second-degree escape, first-degree burglary, and first-degree theft of property.


OVERVIEW: Appellant filed a petition for post-conviction relief under Ala. R. Crim. P. 32 attacking his convictions for second-degree escape, first-degree burglary, and first-degree theft of property. Appellant contended that the trial court improperly denied his motions for post-conviction relief. The court remanded, holding that the trial court order denying the petition did not comply with Ala. R. Crim. P. 32. The court held that because the order of the trial court did not specify which claims its order of denial encompassed, nor did it make specific findings of fact with regard to each of those claims, the court must have remanded for the trial court to state the grounds, whether procedural or based on the merits, for its denial of the Ala. R. Crim. P. 32 petition.


OUTCOME: The court remanded, holding that the trial court's order denying post-conviction relief did not comply with the criminal rules in stating its grounds with sufficient specificity. Because the order did not specify which claims its order of denial encompassed, nor did it make specific findings of fact with regard to each of those claims, the court remanded for the trial court to state the grounds.

 

952 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Burgess v. State


CR-94-0475


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


811 So. 2d 557; 1998 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 274



December 18, 1998, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied February 5, 1999. As Corrected March 29, 1999. As Corrected February 14, 2000. Opinion on Remand of September 29, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 116. Released for Publication March 22, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Morgan Circuit Court. (CC-93-1270). TRIAL JUDGES: C. Bennett McRae and Sherrie W. Brown.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the Morgan Circuit Court (Alabama), which convicted appellant of murder made capital under Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(2) (1975), and sentenced appellant to death.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of murder made capital because it was committed during the course of a robbery in the first degree pursuant to Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(2) (1975). The jury recommended that appellant be sentenced to life imprisonment without parole, but the trial court sentenced appellant to death. Appellant raised several issues in his appeal which he did not raise in the trial court. However, because appellant was sentenced to death, his failure to object at trial did not bar the court's review of these issues. The court held that it did weigh against appellant as to any claim of prejudice he made on appeal. The court held that there was no evidence that the sentence was imposed under the influence of passion, prejudice, or any other arbitrary factor and that the findings and conclusions of the trial court were amply supported by the evidence. The court also concluded that the aggravating circumstance outweighed the mitigating circumstances and that death was the appropriate sentence. Therefore, the court affirmed the trial court's decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction and sentence because although appellant's failure to raise the issues at trial did not preclude the court's review, the court did not find that any of the issues raised by appellant required a different result.

 

953 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Drinkard v. State


CR-95-0055


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


777 So. 2d 225; 1998 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 275



December 18, 1998, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected February 8, 1999. Rehearing Denied January 15, 1999. As Corrected October 18, 1999. As Corrected January 14, 2000. As Corrected February 14, 2000. Released for Publication January 17, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Morgan Circuit Court. (CC-93-1308). TRIAL JUDGE: Steven E. Haddock.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the Morgan Circuit Court (Alabama), which convicted appellant of murder made capital because it was committed during a robbery in the first degree pursuant to Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(2) (1875), and sentenced appellant to death.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of the offense of murder made capital because it was committed during a robbery in the first degree under Ala. Code §13A-5-40(a)(2) (1975). Appellant waived his right to a sentencing hearing before the jury that convicted him. Following a sentencing hearing before the trial court, appellant was sentenced to death. Appellant raised several issues on appeal that were not preserved at the trial. However, the court held that because the case involved the death penalty, the court would review appellant's assertions for plain error. The court held that appellant's assertions as to the impropriety of the manner of selecting the jury and alleged prosecutorial misconduct did not warrant reversal as there was no plain error since the foreperson was chosen from a properly constituted jury; there was no evidence that appellant's sentence was imposed under the influence of passion, prejudice, or any other arbitrary factor. Therefore, the court affirmed the decision of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction and sentence because the court held that although the court must review appellant's assertions for plain error even though these issues were not preserved for appellate review, there was no plain error in the selection of the jury and there was no evidence that appellant's sentence was imposed under the influence of passion, prejudice, or any other arbitrary factor.

 

954 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Merrill v. State


CR-93-1054


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


741 So. 2d 1099; 1998 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 262



November 20, 1998, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at: 741 So. 2d 1099 at 1104. As Corrected January 14, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court. (CC-93-826). J. Richmond Pearson, TRIAL JUDGE.

Original Opinion of March 21, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 168.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS TO CONVICTION; SENTENCE OF DEATH VACATED; AND REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING. * 



* Note from the reporter of decisions: On March 26, 1999, on return to remand, the Court of Criminal Appeals affirmed, without opinion. On April 30, 1999, that court denied rehearing, no opinion. On August 20, 1999, the Supreme Court denied the State's certiorari petition, without opinion (1981281).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Jefferson Circuit Court (Alabama) convicted defendant of capital murder and attempted murder and sentenced him to death by electrocution. On appeal, the case was remanded to the trial court with instructions to enter a sentencing order in compliance with Ala. Code § 13A-5-47(d) (1975). The trial court filed its return with the appellate court.


OVERVIEW: Upon review, the appellate court held that defendant was correctly found guilty of capital murder and that the trial court erred in imposing the death sentence. The trial court's return stated that "the act itself" was an aggravating circumstance in the case. That finding was erroneous. The offense with which defendant was charged was not among the offenses specified in subsection Ala. Code § 13A-5-49(4) (1975). "The act itself" therefore could not have been an aggravating circumstance. Because defendant failed to raise the issue of his alleged lack of opportunity to challenge consolidation, the appellate court could not consider the argument on appeal. Because defendant's claims of improper consolidation could not be considered, his claim of cumulative errors associated with that consolidation also failed. Defendant failed to demonstrate prejudice from the trial court's refusal to allow him to individually voir dire members of the jury as to potential racial prejudice. Defendant was not prejudiced by his inability to further cross-examine and confront the attempted murder victim concerning his statement to the officer.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed and his sentence was vacated and remanded for resentencing.

 

955 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Dunaway v. State


CR-97-1223


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


746 So. 2d 1021; 1998 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 239



October 23, 1998, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied April 24, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 2912. As Corrected November 16, 1998. Application for Rehearing Denied December 18, 1999. Released for Publication January 21, 2000. As Amended March 27, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Barbour Circuit Court. (CC-97-075 and CC-97-076). William T. Gaither, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Barbour Circuit Court (Alabama) that convicted him on a jury verdict of two counts of capital murder, sentenced him to life imprisonment on one count, and to death by electrocution on the other.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, at first denying involvement, later claimed he accidentally shot his girlfriend twice, poured alcohol over her, laid her 22-month-old son near her, and set the home on fire. He claimed that "voices" told him to set the fire. Witnesses who knew him testified that he seemed normal at the time of the crime, and that they never thought he was mentally ill. The State's expert opined that he was sane; a defense expert opined that he was a schizophrenic. He was sentenced to death for the child's murder. The appellate court held that the evidence, including the testimony of the lay witnesses, was sufficient for the jury to conclude he was sane. The fact that defendant changed his story, and tried to cover up the crime, showed he knew his actions were wrong. He was not entitled to instructions on the lesser-included offenses of (1) reckless murder, as he had directed his actions toward these victims; or of (2) reckless manslaughter, as there was no evidence that the was intentionally committing a felony when he unintentionally killed the victims. In aggravation, the trial court properly considered his prior conviction, and that his murder of the child was especially cruel.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

956 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Moore v. State


CR-97-1791


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


739 So. 2d 536; 1998 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 249



October 23, 1998, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 6, 1999. As Amended December 21, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Montgomery Circuit Court (CV-97-2334). William R. Gordon, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Alabama Board of Pardons and Paroles issued a decision to bar petitioner inmate from parole consideration. The inmate sought a writ of certiorari in which he challenged that decision. The Montgomery Circuit Court (Alabama) summarily denied the petition. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The board denied the inmate's parol under Ala. Code § 15-22-27.1 which barred parole for certain repeat violent offenders. The inmate argued that § 15-22-27.1 was implicitly repealed by the Habitual Felony Offender Act (HFOA), Ala. Code § 13A-5-9, which denied parole for a more limited class of repeat offenders. The appellate court disagreed because Ala. Code Ann. § 15-22-27.1 and the HFOA did not conflict. Whereas § 15-22-27.1 denied parole eligibility upon the commission of certain offenses, the HFOA required imprisonment for life without parole only upon a conviction of a Class A felony after three prior felony convictions. Therefore the ordinary sentence of "life" under the HFOA required parole consideration but the same conclusion did not apply to a sentence for a term of years. Statutes other than the HFOA could affect a defendant's punishment, so long as they did not alter the range set out in the HFOA. In the case, denial of the inmate's parole eligibility did not change the fact that his sentence was within a proper range under the HFOA. Therefore, both Ala. Code Ann. § 15-22-27.1 and the HFOA applied without altering the terms of either statute.


OUTCOME: The court of criminal appeals affirmed the decision of the trial court.

 

957 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Shelton v. State


CR-97-1313


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


851 So. 2d 83; 1998 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 216



October 2, 1998, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] On Return to Remand May 28, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 128. As Corrected March 11, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Etowah Circuit Court. (CC-97-0365). TRIAL JUDGE: William W. Cardwell, Jr.



DISPOSITION: REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS. *



* Note from the reporter of decisions: On August 20, 1999, on the return to second remand, the Court of Criminal Appeals affirmed, without opinion. On September 24, 1999, that court denied rehearing, without opinion. On May 19, 2000, the Supreme Court granted certiorari review and AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; AND REMANDED (1990031). On October 27, 2000, the Supreme Court denied rehearing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for third-degree assault and sentence to 30 days imprisonment, suspended, with unsupervised probation for 2 years, conditioned on payment of fines, costs, and restitution, after receiving a trial de novo in the Etowah Circuit Court (Alabama).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the prosecutor's complaint was void because it did not include the language "to another person" in describing the intent element of the offense. The appellate court held that the complaint substantially tracked the language of the statute. The complaint contained sufficient facts and a sufficient description of the elements to inform defendant of the charge so that he could prepare a defense and invoke the Double Jeopardy Clause. Because the complaint contained all the essential elements of the charge, it was valid. Defendant was convicted of third-degree assault, a Class A misdemeanor, and was sentenced to 30 days imprisonment, suspended, and probation, conditioned on the payment of fines, costs, and restitution. The constitutional right to counsel applied in misdemeanor cases where the sentence of imprisonment was suspended conditionally. Therefore, defendant had a constitutional right to counsel. Nothing in the record indicated that defendant knowingly, understandingly, and voluntarily waived his right to counsel.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded for the circuit court to determine whether defendant made a knowing, intelligent, and voluntary waiver of his right to counsel.

 

958 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Farrior v. State


CR-97-0835


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


728 So. 2d 691; 1998 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 211



September 11, 1998, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Rehearing Denied October 23, 1998. Cert. Pending November 10, 1998. Released for Publication April 23, 1999. As Corrected July 7, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Montgomery Circuit Court. (CC-97-485). William R. Gordon, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the order of the Montgomery Circuit Court (Alabama) that convicted him of the crime of capital murder under Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(17) (1975) and sentenced him to life imprisonment without the possibility of parole.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of capital murder under Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(17) (1975) for his use of a deadly weapon while the victim was in a vehicle. The circuit court accepted the jury's recommendation of life imprisonment without the possibility of parole. On appeal, defendant argued that the evidence was not sufficient to support his conviction, that the circuit court improperly refused to give his requested jury instructions on provocation, that his Batson challenge was improperly denied, and that his videotaped confession was wrongly admitted into evidence. The court affirmed, holding that there was sufficient evidence from which the jury could have found defendant guilty of capital murder. The court held that the circuit court properly refused to give defendant's requested instructions because provocation was thoroughly covered in the oral charge to the jury. It was also held that defendant did not establish a prima facie case of discrimination and did not show that the denial of his Batson motion was clearly erroneous, and that there was no error in the admission of defendant's videotaped confession because there was evidence that the confession was voluntary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the circuit court that convicted defendant of the crime of capital murder and sentenced him to a term of life imprisonment without the possibility of parole.

 

959 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Thomas v. State


CR-93-0823


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


766 So. 2d 860; 1998 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 212



September 4, 1998, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 23, 1998. As Corrected February 11, 1999. As Corrected August 21, 2000. Released for Publication August 21, 2000. As Corrected February 5, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Limestone Circuit Court. (CC-85-74.01). Henry W. Blizzard, Jr., TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant prisoner sought review of a decision from the Limestone Circuit Court (Alabama) that denied his petition under Ala. R. Crim. P. 32 contesting the validity of his conviction for capital murder and sentence of death as well as his convictions for first degree arson, first degree robbery, and first degree sexual abuse and resulting sentence. The convictions and sentences were affirmed by the state supreme court.


OVERVIEW: Prisoner was charged in a four-count indictment with intentional murder of an elderly woman during the course of a burglary, arson in the first degree, robbery in the first degree, and sexual abuse in the first degree. He was found guilty on all counts and the jury unanimously recommended death as punishment. The convictions and sentences were affirmed by the court as well as the state supreme court. The U.S. Supreme Court denied prisoner's petition for certiorari review and the circuit court denied his petition filed under Ala. R. Crim. P. 32. Upon review, petitioner asserted that he received ineffective assistance of counsel at both the trial and appellate level. Additionally, prisoner claimed that he was incompetent to stand trial. The court held that prisoner failed on his ineffectiveness claim by not establishing, under Strickland, both that his counsel's performance was deficient and that he was prejudiced as a result of the deficiency. Further, proof of the incompetency involved more than simply showing that the accused had mental problems or psychological difficulties. Thus, prisoner was found competent to stand trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.

 

960 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Pilley v. State


CR-96-1781


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


789 So. 2d 870; 1998 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 148



August 14, 1998, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 2, 1998. As Corrected February 14, 2000. Opinion on Remand of September 29, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 118. Released for Publication January 31, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court. (CC-95-1236). James S. Garrett, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the Jefferson Circuit Court (Alabama) of capital murder and his sentence to death by electrocution.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted that the trial court made erroneous rulings on the admission of evidence, denial of defense motions, in instructing the jury, in removing certain jurors but not others, that the imposition of death was erroneous, and that the death penalty was unconstitutional. All of defendant's claims of error were rejected and his conviction and sentence affirmed. The circumstantial evidence was legally sufficient to sustain the conviction for capital murder when it established his presence just before the killings, he had discussed obtaining weapons and easy money, the victims were killed execution-style, defendant had certain denominations of dollar bills that were similar to a victim's, and a co-defendant turned over another victim's jewelry to police. Thus denial of a motion of acquittal was also proper. It was not an abuse of discretion to deny a mistrial motion where there was contact between a member of the district attorney's office and a juror because they were friends, the juror declined to discuss the case, and the juror did not know what the member did for a living or where the district attorney's office violated an agreed upon discovery order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of capital murder and sentence to death.

 

961 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Goodwin v. State


CR-96-0574


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


728 So. 2d 662; 1998 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 153



August 14, 1998, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 23, 1999. As Corrected August 25, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Lauderdale Circuit Court. (CC-96-292). Larry Mack Smith, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS. *



* Note from the reporter of decisions: On October 2, 1998, on return to remand, the Court of Criminal Appeals affirmed, without opinion. On November 20, 1998, that court denied rehearing, no opinion. On February 26, 1999, the Supreme Court denied certiorari review, without opinion (1980429).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his jury conviction in the Lauderdale Circuit Court (Alabama) for the felony offense of driving while under the influence of alcohol, a violation of Ala. Code § 32-5A-191(a)(2), (h) (1975), and driving while his license was revoked, a violation of Ala. Code § 32-6-19 (1975). He also appealed his one-year sentence for driving while his license was revoked because it exceeded the statutory limit for a § 32-6-19 conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the felony offense of driving while under the influence of alcohol, a violation of Ala. Code § 32-5A-191(a)(2), (h) (1975), and driving while his license was revoked, a violation of Ala. Code § 32-6-19 (1975). The court affirmed his convictions and found that the circuit court did not err in denying his motion to suppress the evidence gathered as a result of his arrest, which he based on his contention that the officer who stopped his vehicle lacked the reasonable suspicion required to temporarily detain and question him. Under the circumstances, the stopping officer had a reasonably warranted suspicion that defendant was at the time that the officer stopped him, and previously may have been, engaged in criminal conduct. In addition, there was sufficient evidence to convict him on the driving while under the influence charge, and the circuit court did not err in denying his motion for an acquittal on that charge. The court remanded his case and directed the circuit court to resentence him on the charge of driving while his license was revoked because his one-year sentence on that charge exceeded the statutory limit for a conviction under § 32-6-19.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for the felony offense of driving while under the influence of alcohol and for driving while his license was revoked, but remanded his case for resentencing for his conviction on the charge of driving while his license was revoked.

 

962 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Hagood v. State


CR-95-1915


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


777 So. 2d 162; 1998 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 160



August 14, 1998, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected. Rehearing Denied November 20, 1998. Released for Publication January 17, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Walker Circuit Court. (CC-94-124). James C. Brotherton, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS TO CONVICTION; REVERSED AS TO SENTENCE; AND REMANDED FOR NEW SENTENCING PROCEEDINGS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from the Walker Circuit Court (Alabama), which convicted appellant of the capital offense of murder during a kidnapping in the first degree, a violation of Ala. Code §13A-5-40(a)(1) (1975). Appellant challenged his conviction on multitude grounds.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of murder during a kidnapping and sentenced to death. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction but reversed the sentence. The court held, among other things, that (1) the trial court did not err in granting the prosecution's challenges for cause of prospective jurors, based on their opposition to the death penalty, because each of the jurors ultimately indicated that he or she could not recommend the death penalty; (2) the trial court did not err in denying appellant's challenges for jurors based on their feelings regarding the imposition of the death penalty because each juror indicated that he or she could follow the trial court's sentencing instructions; (3) the prosecution did not use its peremptory strikes in a racially discriminatory manner; (4) the trial court did not err in the charges given to the jury on the offenses of intentional murder, reckless murder, and criminally negligent homicide; but (5) that reversal of appellant's sentence was required because the trial court's instruction on the aggravating circumstance that the capital offense was committed during a robbery was incomplete by not defining "theft" for the jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction but reversed his sentence and remanded the case to the trial court for new sentencing proceedings.

 

963 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Battles v. City of Mobile


CR-97-0466


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


771 So. 2d 498; 1998 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 168



August 14, 1998, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 2, 1998. The Name of this Case has been Corrected March 9, 2000. As Corrected March 9, 2000. As Amended March 27, 2000. Released for Publication September 21, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Mobile Circuit Court. (CC-97-2424). Edward B. McDermott, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On appeal from Mobile Circuit Court (Alabama), defendant challenged his convicted of failing to obey an order of a police officer, a violation of Mobile, Ala., Ordinance no. 39-54, claiming the ordinance was overbroad.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found that, under the facts of this case, defendant was not "directly affected" by any overbreadth of Ordinance no. 39-54. Defendant could not claim that he was "directly affected" by the overbreadth of the ordinance because, regardless of how the ordinance is construed, the officer at issue clearly had the authority to ask the appellant to answer questions about his headlights. Regardless of the overbreadth of Ordinance no. 39-54, defendant had the legal duty to follow the officer's orders; refusal to do so was illegal. Defendant failed to show that police officers would use the ordinance to encroach upon First Amendment protections and failed to show that Ordinance no. 39-54 was unconstitutional on its face. Defendant also failed to show how the ordinance itself violated any of his rights to equal protection. The ordinance's terms were facially neutral, applying equally regardless of race or any other classification. Even if evidence of officer character was admissible, its exclusion was harmless, as it would have had no effect on defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The lower court decision was affirmed.

 

964 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Ex parte Land


CR-97-1473


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


775 So. 2d 840; 1998 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 144



July 2, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected September 20, 1999. As Corrected January 14, 2000. Released for Publication January 16, 2001. As Corrected May 1, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Jefferson Circuit Court. (CC-92-4671.60). TRIAL JUDGE: James H. Hard IV.



DISPOSITION: PETITION DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant's murder convictions and death sentence were affirmed on appeal. Defendant sought post conviction relief pursuant to Ala. R. Crim. P. 32. Defendant filed a discovery motion requesting access to all of the files, from all of the state agency, with information regarding his case. The Jefferson Circuit Court (Alabama) granted the motion only as to district attorney's files. Defendant filed a petition for a writ of mandamus.


OVERVIEW: There was nothing in Ala. R. Crim. P. 32 or any other Rule of Criminal Procedure that allowed the "unlimited" discovery the defendant sought in his post-conviction proceeding. There was no postconviction right to "fish" through official files for belated grounds of attack on the judgment, or to confirm mere speculation or hope that a basis for collateral relief may exist. Defendant was attempting to retry his case. The court stated that discovery in a post-conviction proceeding was only allowed when "good cause" was shown. The trial court's discovery order granting defendant access to the district attorney's files gave defendant more than he was lawfully entitled to obtain in a post-conviction proceeding. Accordingly, since defendant established no "clear legal right" to the discovery he sought in his post-conviction proceeding, his petition for a writ of mandamus was denied.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's petition for a writ of mandamus.

 

965 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


City of Fort Payne v. Bouldin


CR-97-0509


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


717 So. 2d 883; 1998 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 124



May 29, 1998, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 7, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from DeKalb Circuit Court. (CC-97-551). David A. Rains, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The city appealed from the order of the DeKalb Circuit Court (Alabama) that affirmed an order of the municipal court (Alabama) that granted defendant's motion to dismiss harassment charges against defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant approached a 16-year-old girl at a library. After striking up a conversation with the girl, defendant said he was in the library to see how many orgasms a woman could have, and bragged that he once had a woman have 20 orgasms. The librarian called for the girl to come to her, after which defendant left the library. Later that day, defendant pulled his car beside the girl at a drive-in restaurant. Defendant left the restaurant after the girl complained to a waitress. The city charged defendant with harassment under Ala. Code § 13A-11-8(a)(1)(b) (1975). The municipal court granted defendant's motion to dismiss, which the circuit court affirmed. The city argued that the statute should apply to obscene language as well as fighting words. However, the court held that it was unable to address the applicability of the harassment statute because none of the courts below held that the statute was unconstitutional. The court noted that the city did not have the right to appeal the municipal court's grant of defendant's motion to dismiss to the circuit court under Ala. R. Crim. P. 30.1(b) because the municipal court did not hold the harassment statute to be unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the city's appeal of the affirmation of the grant of defendant's motion to dismiss harassment charges the city brought against defendant.

 

966 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Dill v. State


CR-96-1130


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


723 So. 2d 787; 1998 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 125



May 29, 1998, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 14, 1998. Released for Publication January 20, 1999. As Corrected May 14, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Montgomery Circuit Court. (CC-96-1164). Eugene W. Reese, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND JUDGMENT RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Montgomery Circuit Court (Alabama), which convicted him of violating the Alabama Code of Ethics for Public Officials (Ethics Act), Ala. Code §§ 36-21-1 to -30, and of perjury in the first degree. Defendant argued that there was insufficient evidence to convict him, a duplicitous indictment, and that the Ethics Act was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, the state insurance commissioner, was convicted of violating the Ethics Act by knowingly and willfully associating with a business he regulated as insurance commissioner and by knowingly and willfully accepting something of value from a person associated with a business that he regulated. Defendant was also convicted of two counts of perjury in the first degree. On appeal, defendant argued that there was insufficient evidence to convict him, a duplicitous indictment, and that the Ethics Act was unconstitutionally vague. The court agreed that there was insufficient evidence and reversed the conviction. On the ethics charges, the court found that the state had failed to prove that defendant had an association with a "business" as defined in Ala. Code § 36-25-1(2) (1975), and that he had the requisite criminal intent when he accepted a check from his daughter. On the perjury charges, the court held that the state failed to prove the falsity of defendant's testimony. Next, the court held that the state should have elected only one of the two charges on perjury. Lastly, the court held that the Ethics Act was constitutional and not void for vagueness.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction because there was insufficient evidence to convict him of violating the Ethics Act and of perjury. The indictment was also duplicitous. The Ethics Act itself, however, was constitutional.

 

967 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Cole v. State


CR-96-1863


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


721 So. 2d 255; 1998 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 105



May 8, 1998, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected June 1, 1998. Rehearing Denied June 19, 1998. S.C. Denied Cert. August 28, 1998. Released for Publication December 23, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Cullman Circuit Court. (CC-96-451,-452,-453,-454, and -455; CC-97-125,-126, and -127). H. Frank Brunner, Jr., TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his convictions in Cullman Circuit Court (Alabama) on charges related to the use of children to produce obscene material.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of four charges of the production of obscene matter containing a visual reproduction of a person under 17 years of age, a violation of Ala. Code § 13A-12-197 (1975); one charge of permitting his minor child to engage in the production of obscene matter involving that child, a violation of Ala. Code § 13A-12-196 (1975); and three charges of enticing a child under the age of 16 to enter his residence for immoral purposes, a violation of Ala. Code § 13A-6-69 (1975). On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions and sentences. The court found that the jury had sufficient evidence, if believed, on which to find defendant guilty of each of the charges under §§ 13A-12-196, 13A-12-197 without the introduction of photographs. The court also noted that Ala. Code § 13A-12-190(13) (1975) required only that the depictions of alleged sexual conduct lack "serious literary, artistic, political, or scientific value" to be "obscene" and did not have to meet the Miller standard, which applied to depictions of breast nudity. Therefore, the trial court properly instructed the jury on the obscenity standard.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions on charges related to the use of children to produce obscene material.

Burton v. State


CR-96-0597


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


728 So. 2d 1142; 1998 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 83



April 3, 1998, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected June 19, 1998. Released for Publication January 20, 1999. As Corrected August 25, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Tallapoosa Circuit Court. (CC-96-16.60). Philip Dale Segrest, TRIAL JUDGE.

Original Opinion April 18, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 192.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the order of the Tallapoosa Circuit Court (Alabama) that convicted and sentenced him as a habitual offender for possession of cocaine, Ala. Code § 13A-12-212 (1975), and possession of a pistol after having been convicted of a crime of violence, Ala. Code § 13A-11-72(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for possession of cocaine, Ala. Code § 13A-12-212 (1975), and for possession of a pistol after having been convicted of a crime of violence, Ala. Code § 13A-11-72(a). Defendant was found guilty of both counts and was sentenced to consecutive sentences of life imprisonment as a habitual offender for the first count and to five years' imprisonment on the second count. Defendant's post-conviction petition under Ala. R. Crim. P. 32, which collaterally attacked the legality of his convictions, was denied. The court affirmed, holding that defendant was appropriately sentenced under the Habitual Felony Offender Act, and that there was no error in the denial of defendant's post-conviction petition. The court found no merit in defendant's allegation that he was denied the right to appeal because there was uncontradicted testimony to the effect that defendant repeatedly told his trial counsel that he did not want to appeal. The court stated that there was also no merit to defendant's allegation of ineffective assistance of counsel because the record indicated that defendant, with the advice of his counsel, made a conscious and informed decision not to appeal his case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the circuit court that convicted and sentenced defendant as a habitual offender for the crimes of possession of cocaine and possession of a pistol after having been convicted of a crime of violence.

 

969 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. State


CR-95-0093


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


756 So. 2d 892; 1998 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 88



April 3, 1998, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected May 12, 1998. Rehearing Denied May 29, 1998. As Corrected August 21, 2000.
Affirmed by Ex parte Smith, 1999 Ala. LEXIS 268 (Ala., July 30, 1999)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Madison Circuit Court. (CC-95-187). C. Lynwood Smith, TRIAL JUDGE.

Original Opinion of December 19, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 370.
Smith v. State, 756 So. 2d 892, 1997 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 370 (Ala. Crim. App., 1997)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Madison Circuit Court (Alabama), which convicted defendant of murder committed during the course of a robbery in violation of Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(2), and sentenced defendant to death by electrocution. Upon remand, the circuit court determined that the indictment was not irreparably tainted and that the terms of a plea agreement between the State and a co-defendant had not been misrepresented to the jury.


OVERVIEW: Defendant piston-whipped and killed a man, in spite of the fact that the man had begged for his life. A jury convicted defendant of capital murder and recommended a sentence of life imprisonment without the possibility of parole. The circuit court overrode the recommendation and sentenced defendant to death. Upon remand, the circuit court found that the indictment was not irreparably tainted and that the terms of a plea agreement with a co-defendant had not been misrepresented to the jury. The court affirmed the conviction and the sentence of death by electrocution. The court upheld the finding of aggravating circumstances, which were that the murder was committed during the course of a robbery and that the murder was especially heinous, atrocious, and cruel. The court found that the aggravating circumstances substantially outweighed the mitigating circumstances and the jury recommendation. There was no plain error any of the errors alleged by defendant, including the charge to the jury, the denial of motions to suppress, and the effectiveness of defendant's counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting defendant of murder committed during the course of a robbery and sentencing defendant to death by electrocution.

 

970 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Moore v. City of Montgomery


CR-96-2378


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


720 So. 2d 1030; 1998 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 70



March 20, 1998, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 8, 1998. Cert. pending May 27, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Montgomery Circuit Court. (CC-96-5251). Charles Price, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Montgomery Circuit Court (Alabama), which found him in violation of Montgomery, Ala., Municipal Code § 27-6(a), operating his car radio at a level that was plainly audible at a distance of five feet. The trial court denied defendant's motion to dismiss the charges against him based on his contention that the noise ordinance was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to operating his car radio at a level that was plainly audible at a distance of five feet, a violation of Montgomery, Ala., Municipal Code § 27-6(a). The court affirmed the judgment and held that the ordinance was not unconstitutionally vague because the distance standards in ordinance defined what constituted a violation of the ordinance with sufficient detail to put a person of ordinary intelligence on notice of what conduct was prohibited. The statute prohibited any sound coming from a device that was s plainly audible at the proscribed distance. The statute specifically provided that a violation occurred if the music was plainly audible to any person. If a law enforcement officer heard sounds from a musical device at the proscribed distance, then the ordinance was violated. Further, the ordinance was not overly broad, as the challenged portion of the ordinance covered only noise coming from radios, musical instruments, and similar devices, and not protected speech. The breadth of the ordinance was not unreasonable even though it did not limit its application to certain times or to certain areas.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that defendant operated his car radio at a level that was plainly audible at a distance of five feet in violation of a city ordinance.

 

971 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Ex parte Washington


CR-97-0615


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


716 So. 2d 253; 1998 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 90



March 16, 1998, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected November 16, 1998. As Corrected. Released for Publication September 11, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Coffee Circuit Court. (CC-97-202; CC-97-114; CC-97-115; and CC-97-7). Robert W. Barr, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: PETITION GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants filed a petition for a writ of mandamus against respondent judge of the Coffee Circuit Court (Alabama), which denied defendants' motions to dismiss the indictments against them on unrelated offenses. Defendants sought to compel the judge to dismiss their indictments. One defendant was indicted for theft, one was indicted for possessing a controlled substance and carrying a pistol without a license, and one was indicted for burglary.


OVERVIEW: 1996 Ala. Acts 96-454, which set up the county's system of calling prospective jurors from the county as a whole and not solely from the division of the county where the offense occurred, was declared unconstitutional by the Alabama Supreme Court (Supreme Court). Defendants were indicted on their offenses before the Act was declared unconstitutional. The trial court denied defendants' motions to dismiss the indictments. Thereafter, defendants filed a petition for a writ of mandamus to compel such dismissal, which the court granted. The court held that the Supreme Court's decision would be applied retroactively to defendants because the Act was no more constitutional before it was successfully challenged than it was after the Supreme Court issued its opinion that declared it unconstitutional. The retroactive application of the Supreme Court's decision would not result in undue hardship on the county, and there was an overwhelming preference for the retroactive application of judicial decisions. The re-indictment of defendants by a constitutionally empaneled grand jury did not dismiss the first indictments, whose disposition the court held had to be reflected in the record.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendants' petition for a writ of mandamus to compel the judge to dismiss the indictments against defendants.

 

972 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Turner v. State


CR-96-1700


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


792 So. 2d 1138; 1998 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 48



March 6, 1998, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected April 22, 1998. As Corrected May 11, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court. (CC-96-2360). James H. Hard IV, TRIAL JUDGE.

This Opinion Substituted by the Court for Withdrawn Opinion of November 14, 1997, Previously Reported at: 1997 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 355.



DISPOSITION: OPINION WITHDRAWN; OPINION SUBSTITUTED; AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Jefferson Circuit Court (Alabama), which was entered on the jury's verdict that convicted defendant of trafficking in marijuana, in violation of Ala. Code § 13A-12-231 (1975), and of failing to affix a tax stamp, in violation of Ala. Code § 40-17A-4 (1975). Defendant was sentenced to prison, but given probation on a portion of his trafficking conviction sentence and on all of his tax stamp sentence.


OVERVIEW: A package that contained marijuana was seized by police officers pursuant to a search warrant for defendant's apartment. Defendant was convicted of trafficking in marijuana and of failing to affix a tax stamp. In its substituted opinion, the court affirmed the judgment of conviction. It also remanded the matter for the imposition of a fine pursuant to Ala. Code § 13A-12-281 (1975). The court held that the search warrant was executed on nine months before the Alabama Supreme Court held that anticipatory search warrants were invalid. Thus, the officers did not have knowledge, nor could they be charged with knowledge, that the warrant was invalid because of its anticipatory nature. The officers acted in good faith when they searched defendant's residence, and defendant's motion to suppress the evidence seized from his apartment was properly denied. There was sufficient evidence to present the case to the jury on the issue of defendant's constructive possession of the marijuana. The officers testified that defendant told them, without opening the package, that it contained about four pounds of marijuana, and that he had mailed $ 2,100 to the seller for a prior shipment.


OUTCOME: The court, in its substituted opinion, affirmed the trial court's judgment, which convicted defendant of trafficking in marijuana and failing to affix a tax stamp. The court remanded the matter to the trial court for the imposition of a mandatory fine.

Roberts v. State


CR-93-1766


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


735 So. 2d 1244; 1998 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 50



March 6, 1998, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected May 12, 1998. On 2d Return to Remand May 8, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 100. As Corrected October 18, 1999.
Reported at: 735 So. 2d 1244 at 1266.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Marion Circuit Court. (CC-92-130). Bobby R. Aderholt, TRIAL JUDGE.

Original Opinion May 23, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 206.



DISPOSITION: REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS AS TO SENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the sentencing order of the Marion Circuit Court (Alabama), which imposed the death penalty for defendant's murder conviction.


OVERVIEW: In a sentence-phase hearing, defendant called witnesses to prove that at the time of the killing he was under the influence of extreme mental or emotional disturbance and that he had acted under the extreme duress of another person. The trial court overrode the jury's recommendation of life imprisonment without parole and sentenced defendant to death. On appeal, defendant first argued that the trial court failed to consider mitigating evidence of remorse and other nonstatutory mitigating evidence. The court held that the trial court allowed defendant to present mitigating evidence and duly considered it. Defendant also claimed that the trial court's imposition of the death sentence, after the jury returned with a life imprisonment recommendation, was unconstitutional. The court held that the Eighth Amendment did not define the weight that the sentencing judge must accord to an advisory jury verdict. Defendant also contended that the trial court erred in considering his robbery conviction as an element of capital murder and as an aggravating circumstance. The court held that this practice, known as "double counting," did not violate defendant's rights against double jeopardy.


OUTCOME: The court searched and found no error adversely affecting the rights of defendant in the sentencing proceedings. However, the court remanded to the trial court for the entry into the record of specific findings as to the existence or nonexistence of any nonstatutory mitigating circumstances that were considered in imposing the death sentence on defendant.

 

974 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. State


CR-94-2205


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


727 So. 2d 147; 1998 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 53



March 6, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected March 27, 1998. Rehearing Denied May 8, 1998. Released for Publication March 29, 1999. As Corrected June 18, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Marshall Circuit Court. (CC-95-200104). W.C. Gullahorn, Jr., TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Marshall Circuit Court (Alabama), which found him guilty of murder, made capital because it was committed during a robbery, and sentenced him to death upon the jury's recommendation. Defendant argued that the trial court committed numerous errors in both the trial and sentencing phases.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that his arrest was illegal, pursuant to Ala. Code § 15-10-1 (1975), because the arresting officer was not acting within his respective county when he arrested him. The court disagreed and held that, while § 15-10-1 provided support for defendant's argument, the enactment of Ala. R. Crim. P. 3.3 removed the county limitation on the officer's arrest powers. Accordingly, defendant's arrest was proper because the officer had probable cause to believe that defendant had committed a felony. Further, the court found that the trial court did not err when it refused to instruct the jury on any lesser-included offenses because there was no reasonable theory on which to base the offense of manslaughter; the jury could have only found defendant guilty or not guilty of the capital offense. The court also found that the trial court had properly removed three jurors for cause because they had indicated that they were unable to impose the death penalty. The court addressed defendant's remaining contentions and found that no plain error or defect had occurred in either the guilt or sentencing phases of defendant's trial.


OUTCOME: The judgments of conviction and sentence were affirmed.

 

975 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Henry v. State


CR-95-1539


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


714 So. 2d 1002; 1998 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 54



March 6, 1998, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected November 16, 1998. As Corrected April 22, 1998. Released for Publication August 4, 1998. As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Covington Circuit Court. (CC-94-109). Jerry E. Stokes, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, after pleading guilty to burglary in the third degree and being given a suspended sentence and probation, appealed from an order of the Covington Circuit Court (Alabama) revoking his probation on the grounds that he had committed two new offenses: the unlawful possession of a pistol after having been convicted of a crime of violence and menacing.


OVERVIEW: At the probation revocation hearing, the State presented evidence showing that defendant approached a group of boys, and after being informed that an associate of defendant's had just run away, threatened them with a gun. He told them that if they spoke to the associate again he would kill them or put them in the hospital. He also told the boys that he would kill the associate or put him in the hospital. The trial court stated that defendant's probation was revoked because of his possession of a gun after being convicted of a crime of violence. On appeal, the court held that the State failed to meet its burden of showing that the acts underlying defendant's third-degree burglary conviction would have constituted a burglary before the new Criminal Code so as to be included in the language defining a crime of violence. The court determined that since the enactment of the new Criminal Code, it was insufficient for the trial court to simply look at the name of an offense and rule that it was a crime of violence. The court concluded, therefore, that the trial court improperly revoked defendant's probation on the sole grounds that he possessed a gun after committing a crime of violence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's revocation order and remanded the case for a new probation revocation hearing, with instructions that if the trial court should conclude that defendant violated his probation, it was to enter a written order containing its specific reasons for revoking defendant's probation.

Davis v. State


CR-96-1093


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


720 So. 2d 1006; 1998 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 55



March 6, 1998, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected March 27, 1998. As Corrected March 29, 1999.
Certiorari Denied February 22, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 1177.
Writ of certiorari denied Davis v. Alabama, 525 U.S. 1149, 119 S. Ct. 1049, 143 L. Ed. 2d 55, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 1177 (1999)
Writ of habeas corpus granted, in part, Writ of habeas corpus denied, in part, Claim dismissed by Davis v. Jones, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 46495 (M.D. Ala., July 7, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Coosa Circuit Court. (CV 92-14). John E. Rochester, TRIAL JUDGE.
Davis v. Alabama, 498 U.S. 1127, 111 S. Ct. 1091, 112 L. Ed. 2d 1196, 1991 U.S. LEXIS 1240, 59 U.S.L.W. 3582 (1991)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of capital murder and was sentenced to death. Defendant filed a petition for post-conviction relief pursuant to Ala. R. Crim. P. 32. The Coosa Circuit Court (Alabama) denied the petition, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant raised numerous issues including substantive claims alleging errors in his trial and claims that his trial and appellate attorneys were ineffective. The court held: (1) defendant's substantive claims, including his claims that he was denied his right to a fair and impartial judge, that his rights were denied because he was not timely presented to the court after his arrest, that the trial court's failure to disqualify the prosecutor entitled him to a new trial, and that the juvenile court improperly transferred him to the circuit court, were procedurally barred because the claims had not been raised at trial and they had been raised and addressed on appeal; (2) defendant's ineffective assistance of counsel claims failed because counsel was not professionally unreasonable, nor had defendant proven to a reasonable probability that, but for errors of counsel, a different result as to judgment, sentence or appeal would have occurred; and (3) defendant's Brady violation claims failed because he had not established that the undisclosed evidence was material or that it was reasonably probable that disclosure of such evidence would have changed the result of the trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of defendant's petition for post conviction relief.

Ex parte Foreman


CR-97-0708


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


715 So. 2d 235; 1998 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 47



March 5, 1998, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 11, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: St. Clair Circuit Court. (CC-96-95). William E. Hereford, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: PETITION DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a petition for a writ of mandamus ordering the judge of the St. Clair Circuit Court, Thirtieth Judicial Circuit (Alabama), to dismiss the indictment returned against defendant for capital murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for capital murder by a county grand jury. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the indictment claiming that because the county was divided into two judicial divisions, the grand jury that indicted him should have been called only from the division where the offense occurred, and not from the county as a whole. He further claimed that calling the grand jury from the county as a whole violated his rights under Ala. Const. art. I, § 6 (1901). The trial court denied the motion. Defendant then filed his petition for a writ of mandamus, and the court denied the petition. The court held that based on the language of 1907 Ala. Acts 53, which created the two divisions in the county, two separate judicial districts were not created for purposes of venue. Rather, the Act divided the county into two divisions for purposes of economy and convenience. Thus, the Act did not violate Ala. Const. art. I, § 6 (1901), and it was proper to call prospective jurors for each division from the county at large.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's petition for a writ of mandamus ordering the trial judge to dismiss the indictment against defendant.

Hyde v. State


CR-95-2036


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


778 So. 2d 199; 1998 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 29



January 30, 1998, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 20, 1998. As Corrected March 27, 1998. As Corrected June 1, 1998. Released for Publication January 30, 2001.
Affirmed by Ex parte Hyde, 778 So. 2d 237, 2000 Ala. LEXIS 78 (Ala., 2000)
Post-conviction proceeding at Hyde v. State, 2004 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 133 (Ala. Crim. App., July 23, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Marshall Circuit Court (CC-95-200099). William D. Jetton, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged and found guilty of capital murder. The jury recommended a sentence of life imprisonment without the possibility of parole. The trial court overrode the jury's recommendation and sentenced defendant to death. Defendant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with capital murder. The murder was made capital because it occurred during a burglary, the victim was a grand jury witness, the victim had been subpoenaed to testify at the trial of co-defendant, and the victim was a police officer. Defendant was found guilty because the murder was committed during a burglary, the victim was a grand jury witness, and the victim was going to testify at the trial against co-defendant. The jury recommended a sentence of life imprisonment without the possibility of parole. The trial court overrode the jury's recommendation and sentenced defendant to death. Defendant sought review. On appeal, the court affirmed holding that the trial court did not err in refusing to instruct the jury on the lesser-included offense of intentional murder. The court opined that that the trial court properly considered the two convictions in sentencing defendant to death by electrocution. The court found that the facts of the case did not preclude a conviction for the capital offense of murder committed during a burglary. The court denied the remainder of defendant's contentions on appeal.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence of death by electrocution was affirmed.
