Formby v. State


CR-96-0204


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


750 So. 2d 581; 1997 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 371



December 19, 1997, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected October 18, 1999. Opinion After Remand of October 29, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 250.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from St. Clair Circuit Court. (CC-96-153). Robert Austin, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS. * 



* Note from the reporter of decisions: On May 8, 1998, on return to remand, the Court of Criminal Appeals affirmed, without opinion. On August 14, 1998, that Court denied rehearing, without opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the St. Clair Circuit Court (Alabama) for felony offense of driving while under the influence of alcohol (DUI), after having been convicted of three prior DUI. violations within the past five years. The trial court sentenced defendant to four years' imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court erred by failing to give limiting instructions to the jury regarding its consideration of his three prior DUI convictions. On appeal, the court noted that defense counsel did not object, nor did he request any limiting instructions concerning the jury's consideration of defendant's prior DUI convictions. Thus, defendant's assertion that the trial court erred by failing to give special limiting instructions to the jury regarding its consideration of the three prior DUI convictions was not preserved for review. Further, the felony DUI statute and the punishment provided for in Ala. Code § 32-5A-191 were constitutional. However, the trial court sentenced defendant to four years' imprisonment, but failed to impose the statutorily mandated fine. Thus, the case had to be remanded.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded with directions that the trial court hold a hearing to allow the State, defendant, and his counsel the opportunity to address what would be an appropriate fine, and for the trial court to impose a fine.

 

980 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Manuel v. State


CR-96-0616


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


711 So. 2d 507; 1997 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 360



November 14, 1997, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended. Released for Publication May 7, 1998.
Post-conviction proceeding at Manuel v. State, 854 So. 2d 1220, 2002 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 530 (Ala. Crim. App., Mar. 15, 2002)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Manuel v. Thomas, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 63079 (S.D. Ala., Aug. 31, 2006)
Related proceeding at Manuel v. State, 114 So. 3d 168, 2011 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 1633 (Ala. Crim. App., Sept. 16, 2011)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Manuel v. Danford, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 172694 (S.D. Ala., Nov. 1, 2013)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Related proceeding at Manuel v. Alabama, 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 14925 (M.D. Ala., Jan. 3, 2014)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Related proceeding at Manuel v. Furman, 2017 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 102472 (S.D. Ala., June 28, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Mobile Circuit Court. (CC-96-3172). Edward B. McDermott, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Mobile Circuit Court (Alabama), which convicted him of murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of murder. He appealed, arguing that one of the trial court's jury instructions created a mandatory rebuttable presumption that impermissibly relieved the State of its burden of proving every element of its case beyond a reasonable doubt. The court agreed and found that the instruction created a mandatory presumption because a reasonable juror could have understood it to require a finding that defendant had the specific criminal intent to commit murder if the prosecution proved that he was carrying a pistol without a license. Reviewing the instruction on its face, the court found that proof of a defendant's possession of a pistol without a license was clearly insufficient to support the presumption that the defendant had the criminal intent to commit murder where self-defense has been injected as a defense. The State contended that the instruction was harmless because the evidence of defendant's guilt was overwhelming. The court concluded that the State did not present overwhelming evidence of guilt to the extent that the trial court's improper instruction could have been considered harmless.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the cause for additional proceedings.

 

981 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Hayes v. State


CR-96-0298


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


717 So. 2d 30; 1997 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 337



October 17, 1997, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected December 21, 1998. Rehearing Denied December 19, 1997. Cert Pending January 6, 1998. Released for Publication October 6, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Houston Circuit Court. (CC-95-0980). S. Edward Jackson, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Houston Circuit Court (Alabama), which convicted him under Ala. Code § 13A-6-90 (1975) of stalking his ex-wife and placed him on five years probation. Over defendant's objections, the trial court had admitted photos that showed the injuries defendant had inflicted on his ex-wife in an assault six and a half years earlier as well as evidence of a prior harassment charge of which defendant had been acquitted.


OVERVIEW: Defendant did not object to his ex-wife's testimony at trial regarding the earlier assault. The trial court denied defendant's motions for acquittal and for a new trial. On appeal, the court held that the state had made out a prima facie case of stalking. The court noted that the evidence showed defendant had repeatedly followed and harassed his ex-wife and threatened her in stores and at her workplace. It also showed that he had shouted insults at her, printed a flyer about her and distributed it around the town, and threatened, with both words and gestures, to shoot her and her boyfriend. The court found that the ex-wife knew defendant owned a shotgun and that she had been placed in reasonable fear of death or bodily harm. The court held that it was not necessary to prove defendant actually intended to kill or injure her. The court also held that the admission of the photos was proper since they were extremely probative and were offered to prove essential elements of stalking. The court noted that the evidence of the prior assault was not too remote in time to be admissible. Finally, the court rejected defendant's argument that he had received ineffective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that convicted defendant of stalking his ex-wife and placed defendant on five years probation.

 

982 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


State v. Parker


CR-95-1435


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


740 So. 2d 421; 1997 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 271



September 26, 1997, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Reported at: 740 So. 2d 421 at 424.
As Amended. As Corrected April 22, 1998. As Corrected March 29, 1999. Released for Publication October 4, 1999. As Corrected January 14, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Houston Circuit Court. (CC-95-488). Edward Jackson, TRIAL JUDGE.

Original Opinion of September 27, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 260.



DISPOSITION: APPLICATION GRANTED; RULE 39(k) MOTION DENIED; OPINION EXTENDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the decision of the Houston Circuit Court (Alabama). The appellate court held that former Ala. Code § 32-5A-191(f) (now Ala. Code § 32-5A-191(h)) created a substantive felony offense and that the prior convictions for driving under the influence constituted elements thereof, and had to be charged in the indictment. The case came before the court on application for rehearing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that former Ala. Code § 32-5A-191(f) (now Ala. Code § 32-5A-191(h)) was unconstitutional because it violated his right to due process, and was void for vagueness. The appellate court concluded that the language, the procedure, and the intent of the challenged statute, wherein felony driving under the influence was defined, were constitutional and did not violate the rights to due process or those establishing the doctrine of void for vagueness. The language of the challenged statute provided fair warning of what was forbidden and would inform ordinary people of the prohibited conduct. Defendant had no legitimate ground to complain that the statute was unclear as to his conduct.


OUTCOME: The application was granted.

 

983 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Stewart v. State


CR-90-415


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


730 So. 2d 1203; 1997 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 272



September 26, 1997, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended. Rehearing Denied November 14, 1997. Cert Pending December 2, 1997. As Corrected August 20, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Talladega Circuit Court. (CC-90-630.81). William C. Sullivan, TRIAL JUDGE.

Rehearing Denied December 30, 1992. Certiorari Granted September 3, 1993. Return to Remand March 22, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 76.

Original Opinion of May 1, 1992, Reported at: 1992 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 254.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court, Talladega County (Alabama), convicting him of murder and sentencing him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder, and he was sentenced to death. Defendant appealed, arguing that the trial court improperly admitted photographs that served only to inflame the jury. The court ruled that photographic evidence, if relevant, was admissible even if it had a tendency to inflame the minds of the jurors. Further, the court held that a photograph could be gruesome and ghastly, but that was not a reason to exclude it as long as the photograph was relevant to the proceedings, even if it tended to inflame the jury. The court affirmed the judgment convicting defendant, holding that the photographs admitted into evidence by the trial court were relevant to defendant's testimony that he and the victim struggled and that he accidentally shot her, and that they provided relevant information, based upon scientific testimony, about the location of the gun when the victim was shot. The court concluded that there was no plain error in admitting the photographs of the victim into evidence.


OUTCOME: Judgment convicting defendant and sentencing him to death was affirmed.

 

984 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Barnes v. State


CR-95-0510


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


704 So. 2d 487; 1997 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 265



September 5, 1997, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended. Released for Publication January 29, 1998. As Corrected May 12, 1998.
Remanded by Barnes v. Alabama, 2016 U.S. LEXIS 3468 (U.S., May 23, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Mobile Circuit Court. (CC-94-2913). Braxton Kittrell, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Mobile Circuit Court (Alabama) convicted defendant of capital murder and entered a sentence of death by electrocution. Defendant was convicted of two counts of murder made capital because the murder was committed during a burglary in the first degree, Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(4) (1975), and because the murder was committed during a rape in the first degree, Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(3) (1975). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a juvenile at the time of his arrest, alleged the trial court committed reversible error in admitting certain evidence at trial. The court reversed and remanded. The court found that the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to suppress his custodial confession based on an alleged unreasonableness of the time he was in custody before being transferred to a youth detention facility because evidence established that defendant was capable of understanding his rights despite his mental and physical disabilities. The court, however, found that the trial court erred in admitting testimony over defendant's objection concerning swabs of DNA taken from the victim's body during an autopsy. The court stated that because the medical examiner who allegedly gathered the specimens did not testify at trial (1) defendant, in violation of the Confrontation Clause, was denied the opportunity to cross-examine the medical examiner regarding the specimens; and (2) the improper admission of the DNA evidence was highly prejudicial to defendant's defense of the murder and rape charges.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for capital murder and remanded the case for further proceedings. The trial court committed reversible error in admitting testimony concerning swabs of DNA taken from the victim's body during an autopsy.

May v. State


CR-95-2162


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


710 So. 2d 1362; 1997 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 390



August 22, 1997, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected June 19, 1998. Rehearing Denied October 17, 1997. S.C. Denied Cert. February 20, 1998. Released for Publication June 19, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Tuscaloosa Circuit Court. (CC-94-1627). Robert B. Harwood, Jr., TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Tuscaloosa Circuit Court (Alabama), which convicted him of capital murder, pursuant to Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(17) (1975), in connection with the shooting death of the victim while the victim was in a vehicle. The trial court sentenced defendant to life imprisonment without the possibility of parole.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence. The court held that Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(17) (1975) was constitutional. The court found that there was a rational basis for the legislature's recognition of killers whose victims were killed while in a vehicle as a separate class, and for its decision that the offense should be punishable by either life imprisonment or the death penalty. The court also found that the statute did not proscribe any legally protected activities and did not involve any legally cognizable "suspect" class. The court found that the trial court properly denied defendant's request for a statistical expert to determine if the jury venire was a fair cross-section of the community because he did not make a threshold showing that there was a reasonable probability that the statistical expert would be of assistance to his fair cross-section challenge. Defendant only asserted that there was a variance between the percentage of young black males on the venire and the percentage in the community, and the trial court determined that young black males were not a distinctive group for fair cross-section purposes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant of capital murder and sentenced him to life imprisonment without the possibility of parole.

 

986 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Burgess v. State


CR-93-1147


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


723 So. 2d 742; 1997 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 396



August 22, 1997, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected. Rehearing Denied October 17, 1997. As Corrected May 14, 1999.
Affirmed by Ex parte Burgess, 723 So. 2d 770, 1998 Ala. LEXIS 235 (Ala., 1998)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Decision reached on appeal by, Remanded by Burgess v. Comm'r, 2013 U.S. App. LEXIS 15515 (11th Cir. Ala., July 30, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court, (CC-94-781). Inge P. Johnson, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant on one count of attempted murder, Ala. Code § 13A-4-2 (1975), and three counts of capital murder by one act or pursuant to one scheme or course of conduct, § 13A-5-40(a)(10). By an 8-4 vote, the jury recommended that defendant be imprisoned for life without parole. Nonetheless, the Jefferson Circuit Court (Alabama) sentenced defendant to death. Defendant appealed from the capital murder conviction and death sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's girlfriend and her two daughters were beaten and strangled to death. Although the girlfriend's two-year-old son was badly beaten, he managed to survive the attack. Soon thereafter, defendant stole a shotgun and shot himself, leaving a suicide note explaining "the reason for this." Following a jury trial, in addition to the attempted murder of the boy, defendant was convicted of the capital murder of his girlfriend and her two daughters by one act or pursuant to one scheme or course of conduct. Considering the jury's recommendation of life imprisonment without parole as a non-statutory mitigating circumstance, the trial court nevertheless decided to impose a sentence of death. Defendant appealed, raising numerous assignments of error, most of which were reviewed for plain error because defendant failed to object at trial. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, holding that the evidence was more than sufficient to convict defendant of the crimes. Moreover, the trial was free from reversible error. Finally, after independently weighing the aggravating and mitigating circumstances, the court concluded that the trial court appropriately imposed the death sentence.


OUTCOME: Finding no reversible error, the court affirmed defendant's capital murder conviction and death sentence.

Campbell v. State


CR-94-2290


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


718 So. 2d 123; 1997 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 385



August 22, 1997, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected. Released for Publication October 6, 1998. Certiorari Denied November 16, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 7358. As Corrected February 8, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Houston Circuit Court. (CC-95-079 through CC-95-092). S. Edward Jackson, TRIAL JUDGE.

This Opinion Substituted on Grant of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of August 23, 1996, Previously Reported at: 1997 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 215.



DISPOSITION: OPINION OF AUGUST 23, 1996, WITHDRAWN; OPINION SUBSTITUTED; APPLICATION FOR REHEARING GRANTED; RULE 39(k) MOTION DENIED; AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Houston Circuit Court (Alabama) on 14 separate indictments charging sexual offenses with underage girls. Defendant argued that the indictments should not have been consolidated, that there should have been a change of venue, that the tape-recordings of telephone conversations with a victim should have been suppressed, and that the second-degree rape statute, Ala. Code § 13A-6-62, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a schoolteacher, was convicted of 14 sexual offenses involving underage female students. The court denied each of his arguments and affirmed his conviction. First, all 14 indictments could be consolidated under Ala. R. Crim. P. 13.3(c) because if each were tried separately, evidence of the other acts would have been relevant and admissible to show his motive, intent, and propensity for sexual misconduct. Second, denial of a change of venue was not an abuse of the trial court's discretion because defendant did not show actual prejudice. The jury voir dire excluded prejudiced individuals, leaving jurors that promised to render an impartial verdict; it was not required that jurors be ignorant of the newspaper accounts. Third, taped telephone conversations with a victim were admissible without Miranda warnings because Miranda only applied if defendant was being interrogated while in custody; it did not apply to voluntary statements while defendant was at liberty and being investigated, even if obtained by deception. Nor did § 13A-6-62 violated equal protection simply because it imposed more severe penalties on men than on women; the difference reflected valid societal goals.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction on all indictments. All of defendant's allegations of error were without merit and the court independently determined that the evidence was sufficient to convict.

McNair v. State


CR-95-0470


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


706 So. 2d 828; 1997 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 255



July 3, 1997, RELEASED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended. Released for Publication April 2, 1997. On Application for Rehearing August 22, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 384. S.C. Denied Cert. November 21, 1997. Rehearing Overruled August 22, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Ala. Crim. LEXIS 384. As Corrected June 19, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Henry Circuit Court. (CC-90-086.60). S. Edward Jackson, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision by the Henry County Circuit Court (Alabama), which denied his petition for post-conviction relief under Ala. R. Crim. P. 32. The circuit court found that all of the issues raised in the petition were barred, except as to ineffective assistance of counsel, failure to turn over exculpatory evidence, and unconstitutionality of the death penalty. The circuit court denied the petition those issues as well.


OVERVIEW: A defendant asserted many arguments for post-conviction relief, including prejudice of the jury because portions of the Bible were read during deliberations, ineffective assistance of counsel, that the jury did not represent a cross-section of the community as required by the Sixth Amendment because of racial bias, and that the prosecution withheld evidence under Brady. The court affirmed the circuit court's denial of the defendant's petition, agreeing that most of the arguments were barred because they were raised and addressed at trial and because they could have been but were not raised on appeal. The court found that the jury's reading from the Bible and praying was not of such a character as to indicate bias or corruption or misconduct that might have affected the verdict or as to constitute prejudice. The court further ruled that the allegations of ineffective assistance of counsel were general and conclusory and that defendant asserted no facts to support the allegations. The court also found that defendant did not met his burden of proving that the jury was not a cross-section of the community or that the prosecution withheld any evidence that was exculpatory under Brady.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's denial of defendant's petition for post-conviction relief.

Price v. State


CR-92-0882


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


725 So. 2d 1003; 1997 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 224



June 20, 1997, RELEASED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended. Released for Publication June 20, 1997. As Corrected March 27, 1998. As Corrected April 13, 1998. As Corrected September 28, 1998. As Corrected May 14, 1999. As Corrected August 20, 1999.
Rehearing denied by, 11/14/1997
Affirmed by Ex parte Price, 725 So. 2d 1063, 1998 Ala. LEXIS 243 (Ala., 1998)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Certificate for question declined at, Decision reached on appeal by Price v. Allen, 675 F.3d 1266, 2012 U.S. App. LEXIS 6547 (11th Cir. Ala., 2012)
Related proceeding at, Magistrate's recommendation at Price v. Thomas, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 38305 (S.D. Ala., Feb. 24, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Fayette Circuit Court. (CC-92-003 through -006). Clatus Junkin, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Fayette Circuit Court (Alabama) of capital murder, in violation of Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(2) (1975), for intentional murder during a first degree robbery. He was also convicted of robbery in the first degree, in violation of Ala. Code § 13A-8-41 (1975). The trial court sentenced defendant to life imprisonment without parole for the robbery conviction and to death for the murder conviction. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court held that: 1) the trial court did not err in denying a mistrial for jury misconduct; 2) the trial court did not err in charging the jury on intent, reasonable doubt, the State's burden of proof, or the jury's duty to evaluate the voluntariness of defendant's statements and the credibility of witnesses; 3) the trial court did not err by not excluding potential jurors or by excusing other jurors regarding their death penalty views; 4) the trial court did not misinform the jury that its sentencing verdict was a recommendation; 5) the prosecutor did not act improperly in closing argument; 6) the evidence supported a finding of an aggravating circumstance; 7) defendant's participation was not relatively minor; 8) the admission of seized evidence and photographs of the crime scene was proper; 9) defendant's statement to police was voluntary; 10) the trial court properly denied a change of venue and a continuance; 11) the trial court was not required to give a charge on intentional murder; 12) considering robbery as both an element of the capital offense and as an aggravating circumstance was not unconstitutional; and 13) defendant failed to show a Batson violation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and sentence.

Roberts v. State


CR-93-1766


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


735 So. 2d 1244; 1997 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 206



May 23, 1997, RELEASED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended. Released for Publication May 23, 1997. On Return to Remand March 6, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Ala. Crim App. LEXIS 50. On 2d Return to Remand May 8, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 100. Rehearing Denied June 19, 1998. As Corrected October 18, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Marion Circuit Court. (CC-92-130). Bobby R. Aderholt, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Marion Circuit Court (Alabama) after jury verdicts convicting defendant of two counts of capital murder in violation of Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(2) (1975) and Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(9)(1975), and recommending a sentence of life imprisonment without parole. The circuit court judge overrode the jury recommendation and sentenced defendant to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had been convicted of murder during a robbery under § 13A-5-40(a)(2) and during an arson under § 13A-5-40(a)(9), based on evidence that he robbed and killed a fellow houseguest, then set the victim and the room on fire. Defendant asserted error in the denial of a motion to dismiss a juror after a non-transcribed conference with the judge, admission of photos, jury instructions, comments by the prosecutor, and exclusion of evidence offered in mitigation during the penalty phase as hearsay. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction but reversed the sentence and remanded. The court held that the omitted conference with the juror was not a substantial and significant portion of the record and did not affect defendant's substantial rights. The court found the admission of gruesome photos to be within the trial court's discretion. The court found it was unnecessary to define "intent" and "during" to the jury. The court found no prejudice in comments such as "I think" and references to what was in the defendant's "head". However, the court held that the exclusion of hearsay offered in mitigation was error and reversible in light of the sentence imposed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction in the circuit court of two counts of capital murder, but reversed the circuit court's sentence of death, and remanded with instructions.

 

991 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Duffy v. City of Mobile


CR-96-0180


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


709 So. 2d 77; 1997 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 218



May 23, 1997, RELEASED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended. Rehearing Denied August 22, 1997. S.C. Denied Cert. December 12, 1997. Released for Publication April 2, 1998. As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Mobile County Circuit Court. (CC-96-848). Robert E.L. Key, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND JUDGMENT RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Mobile County Circuit Court (Alabama), which convicted defendant of violating Mobile, Ala., Code § 39-96 (1991), an antinoise ordinance. Defendant contended that the ordinance was overbroad and violated his due process rights because it prohibited amplified speech more broadly than necessary to achieve the governmental interests and because it regulated without reference to time, place, and manner.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of violating the city's antinoise ordinance for preaching on the sidewalk in the city. Defendant challenged the ordinance's constitutionality. The court reversed the conviction and held that the antinoise ordinance, Mobile, Ala., Code § 39-96 (1991), was unconstitutionally overbroad because the standard implemented by the city regulated without reasonable reference to time, place, and manner, and because it regulated constitutionally protected speech more broadly than necessary to achieve the governmental interest in regulating noise. The court found that, absent a permit, the ordinance was an absolute prohibition of any amplified sound that was plainly audible at greater than 50 feet anywhere in the city and at any time of day or night. The sweeping restriction of sound was not narrowly drawn, and restricted constitutionally protected speech beyond the point necessary to accomplish the objective for which the ordinance was created. The court suggested that the city, in amending the ordinance, insert an intent and purpose section in addition to reasonable time, place, and manner restrictions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's conviction of defendant for violating the city's antinoise ordinance.

 

992 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Travis v. State


CR-92-958


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


776 So. 2d 819; 1997 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 173



April 18, 1997, RELEASED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended. As Corrected May 11, 2000. Released for Publication January 16, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Conecuh Circuit Court. (CC-92-004). Samuel H. Welch, Jr., TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court, Conecuh County (Alabama), convicting him of capital murder and sentencing him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of capital murder, and he was sentenced to death. Defendant appealed, arguing that the trial court abused its discretion by impermissibly limiting the questions he propounded to prospective jurors during voir dire relating to their attitudes concerning the death penalty. The court ruled that the scope of the voir dire examination of veniremembers was left largely to the discretion of the trial court and was not disturbed on appeal on the ground that voir dire examination was limited absent an abuse of that discretion. Further, the court held that the right to question veniremembers regarding their qualifications to serve on the jury or their interest or bias was limited by propriety and pertinence and was to be exercised within the sound discretion of the trial court. The court affirmed the judgment convicting and sentencing defendant, concluding that in most of the instances cited by defendant, the trial court appeared to be attempting to clarify improper, leading, or misleading questions propounded by the defense and that the trial court was not attempting to unreasonably limit the scope of defendant's voir dire.


OUTCOME: Judgment convicting and sentencing defendant was affirmed.

Ellis v. State


CR-95-0429


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


705 So. 2d 843; 1997 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 188



April 18, 1997, RELEASED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] As Amended. Released for Publication January 23, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Russell Circuit Court. (CC-94-356). Paul Miller, TRIAL JUDGE.

Original Opinion of May 10, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 133. On 2d Return to Remand January 17, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 30.

This Opinion Substituted on Grant of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of January 17, 1997, Previously Reported at: 1997 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 30. On Return to Remand September 27, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 267. On 3d Return to Remand August 22, 1997.



DISPOSITION: OPINION OF JANUARY 17, 1997, WITHDRAWN; OPINION SUBSTITUTED; APPLICATION FOR REHEARING GRANTED; RULE 39(k) MOTION GRANTED; REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state filed an application for rehearing for reconsideration of the court's ruling that defendant's appeal from the Russell Circuit Court (Alabama) had become moot. The state requested that the court remand the matter to the trial court for a second time with instructions to set aside the trial court's order granting defendant a new trial and to enhance defendant's sentence in accordance with the prior instructions of the court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of distribution of a controlled substance (cocaine) and was sentenced as a habitual offender to 10 years' imprisonment. The trial court failed to enhance his sentence even though there was undisputed evidence that the sale had occurred within three miles of a school. The court remanded the case for resentencing. On remand, the trial court resentenced defendant to 15 years' imprisonment but ordered a "reverse split" of the sentence. Accordingly, the court remanded a second time. While defendant's sentence was pending on the second remand, he filed a motion in the trial court to set aside the verdict and to grant a new trial. The court, upon receiving a return to its remand showing that the trial court had entered an order setting aside the verdict and ordering a new trial, determined that the appeal had become moot and dismissed the appeal. The state filed an application for rehearing. The court found that the trial court had no jurisdiction to modify the original or base sentence imposed or to take any action beyond the express mandate of the court. It had no jurisdiction to grant a new trial or to attempt to dispose of the case in another manner.


OUTCOME: The court withdrew its prior opinion, granted the state's application for rehearing, and remanded the matter to the trial court.

Sterling v. State


CR-95-1923


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


701 So. 2d 71; 1997 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 158



March 21, 1997, RELEASED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended. Rehearing Denied May 2, 1997. S.C. Denied Cert. August 15, 1997. Released for Publication November 21, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Randolph Circuit Court. (CC-94-201). Philip Dale Segrest, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order from the Randolph Circuit Court (Alabama) that convicted him of disorderly conduct in violation of Ala. Code § 13A-11-7(a) (1975) after he spoke in a loud voice to the sheriff while in the courthouse.


OVERVIEW: When defendant's application for a pistol permit was denied, he spoke to the sheriff in a loud voice in the hallway of the courthouse. His loud voice caused employees in other offices along the hallway to stop their work. Defendant was convicted in the district court, and in a trial de novo, a jury found him guilty. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that § 13A-11-7(a), which described the offense of disorderly conduct, was not unconstitutionally vague nor overbroad. The court also had no trouble concluding that defendant made "unreasonable noise" in the hallway of the courthouse for which he was ultimately arrested. Such a restriction on "unreasonable noise" was a proper time, place, and manner regulation of speech.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that convicted defendant of disorderly conduct after he spoke in a loud voice to the sheriff in the courthouse.

 

995 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Finley v. State


CR-96-0099


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


695 So. 2d 258; 1997 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 164



March 21, 1997, RELEASED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 27, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Montgomery Circuit Court. (CC-96-1146). William R. Gordon, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Montgomery Circuit Court (Alabama), which convicted defendant of driving under the influence of alcohol in violation of Ala. Code § 32-5A-191 (1975).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of driving under the influence of alcohol (DUI), a violation of § 32-5A-191. He was sentenced to six months' imprisonment, which sentence was suspended. His driver's license was suspended for 90 days, and he was fined $ 500 and was ordered to pay court costs. Defendant contended that the provisions of § 32-5A-191, setting fines for a violation of that section, which were substantially increased in 1995 pursuant to 1995 Ala. Acts 95-784, were unconstitutional because they amounted to a revenue raising measure. The court disagreed, holding that the primary purpose of the increase in fines for DUI convictions brought about by 1995 Ala. Acts 95-784 was to deter persons from driving under the influence and further held that the primary purpose of the Act was not to collect revenue. Even though the DUI statute generated revenue in the form of fines, the revenue generated from the fines imposed under the statute was incidental to its primary purpose. 1995 Ala. Acts 95-784 was not a revenue bill within the meaning of Ala. Const. amend. IV, § 70 (1901).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant of driving under the influence of alcohol.

 

996 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


MacEwan v. State


CR-95-1093


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


701 So. 2d 66; 1997 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 35



February 28, 1997, RELEASED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended. Rehearing Denied April 18, 1997. S.C. Denied Cert. July 25, 1997. Released for Publication November 21, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court. (CC-95-1761). Michael W. McCormick, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Jefferson Circuit Court (Alabama), which convicted her of capital murder, specifically the murder of a child under the age of 14, in violation of Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(15) (1975), in connection with the death of her two and one-half year old daughter.


OVERVIEW: At defendant's trial, the evidence revealed that her daughter had had numerous medical problems that were attributed to an extremely rare genetic disorder, that defendant had told her boyfriend that she had given the child extra Phenobarbital and Benadryl because she would not stop crying, that a lethal concentration of Benadryl was present in the child's blood, and that the child's cause of death was Benadryl intoxication. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction. The trial court did not err in refusing to give defendant's requested jury instruction concerning heat-of-passion manslaughter, as she had failed to advance any reasonable theory from the evidence to support the charge. Also, the trial court did not err in denying defendant's request for a jury selection consultant, as she had failed to show that there was a reasonable probability that an expert would have been of assistance to her defense or that the denial of a consultant had deprived her of a fair trial. Moreover, the State had presented adequate evidence to submit the capital murder case to the jury. Also, the statute under which defendant was convicted was not unconstitutionally arbitrary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

997 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Cothren v. State


CR-95-1083


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


705 So. 2d 849; 1997 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 24



January 17, 1997, RELEASED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended. Application for Rehearing Overruled, Opinion Extended, April 18, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 189. S.C. Granted Cert. August 22, 1997. S.C. Denied Rehearing October 24, 1997. Released for Publication February 27, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Shelby Circuit Court. (CC-94-117). J. Michael Joiner, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision by the Shelby Circuit Court (Alabama), which convicted defendant of murder made capital because the murder was committed during the course of a robbery in violation of Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(2) (1975). The trial court sentenced defendant to death by electrocution.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court erred in receiving into evidence defendant's statement to the police, in denying his motion to dismiss the indictment, and in denying his oral motion to quash the jury venire. The court found that the trial court correctly received defendant's confessions into evidence. The record reflected that defendant initiated further contact with police. Moreover, if the trial court did err in admitting the confession, the error was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt. The court stated that capital punishment had been upheld against constitutional attacks that the death penalty was cruel and unusual punishment. The record indicated that the jury venire was randomly selected from a list of licensed drivers in Shelby County. The court had repeatedly upheld this method of random selection against constitutional challenges. The prospective jurors in the case were questioned extensively regarding their knowledge of the case and any effect that pretrial publicity might have had on their ability to be fair and impartial. The trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion for a change of venue. The court affirmed the judgment of conviction and sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for murder and his sentenced to death by electrocution.

 

998 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Boyd v. State


CR-94-1523


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


715 So. 2d 825; 1997 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 23



January 17, 1997, RELEASED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected February 16, 1998. Released for Publication September 4, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Talladega Circuit Court. (CC-94-258). Jerry L. Fielding, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Talladega Circuit Court (Alabama), which convicted him of capital murder for the intentional murder during a kidnapping in the first degree and sentenced him to death by electrocution. Defendant argued erroneous admission of evidence, errors in the jury selection, and errors in his sentencing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of capital murder for the intentional murder during a kidnapping in the first degree, and was sentenced to death by electrocution. On appeal, defendant argued errors in all aspects of his trial and sentencing. The court found no reversible error and affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence. First, the court held that certain evidence, such as photographs of the victim, prior bad acts, defendant's flight, were admissible because they were relevant and went to show either motive or consciousness of guilt. Next, the court held that there was no gender or race discrimination in the selection of the jury because there was no indication of purposeful discrimination by the prosecutor. The court also found no error in the jury instructions, particularly on lesser-included offenses and on the theory of reasonable doubt. The court then held that the trial court properly considered mitigating and aggravating factors during the sentencing phase of defendant's trial. Finally, the court held that death by electrocution was not cruel and unusual punishment. The court concluded that none of defendant's substantial rights were violated warranting reversal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence. There were no reversible errors in the admission of evidence, jury selection, or jury instructions during defendant's murder trial, nor any reversible error in the consideration of mitigating and aggravating factors in his sentencing.

 

999 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Thornell v. City of Montgomery


CR-95-1998


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


695 So. 2d 253; 1996 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 326



December 20, 1996, RELEASED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 17, 1997. S.C. Denied Cert. May 9, 1997. Released for Publication June 27, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Montgomery Circuit Court. (CC-95-5080). Charles Price, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the sentence imposed upon him by the Montgomery Circuit Court (Alabama) after he entered a guilty plea to driving under the influence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of driving under the influence (DUI) in the municipal court and appealed for a trial de novo in the circuit court. In the circuit court he entered a guilty plea to the charge and was sentenced. Defendant appealed asserting that the statute under which he was sentenced, Ala. Code § 32-5A-191 (1975), was enacted after the city ordinance under which he was charged, and therefore it should not have applied to him. On appeal, the court affirmed finding that the city ordinance addressing the adoption of state law into the municipal code indicated that amendments to the state statutes referenced therein were to be encompassed in the ordinance. The court found that the sentence imposed pursuant to Ala. Code § 32-5A-191 was appropriate because that section allowed a municipality to charge persons who had committed a misdemeanor without having to formally adopt that state law as an ordinance of the city.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1000 of 1819 DOCUMENTS


Walker v. City of Montgomery


CR-95-1999


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


695 So. 2d 251; 1996 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 329



December 20, 1996, RELEASED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 17, 1997. S.C. Denied Cert. May 23, 1997. Released for Publication June 27, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Montgomery Circuit Court. (CC-95-5264). Charles Price, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Montgomery Circuit Court (Alabama) that convicted him, following a trial de novo, of driving under the influence pursuant to the Montgomery, Ala. Municipal Ordinance 125-79, which incorporated by reference Ala. Code § 32-5A-191 (1975). Defendant also appealed his punishment of unsupervised probation for one year and payment of court costs and a fine.


OVERVIEW: The municipal ordinance under which defendant was convicted for driving under the influence incorporated Ala. Code § 32-5A-191 (1975). Defendant contended that the penalty provisions included in § 32-5A-191 were enacted after the city's adoption of the ordinance, and, therefore, could not lawfully be applied to him. He contended that the circuit court had jurisdiction to hear his case based on the ordinance alone and not on the state statute, because, he said, the ordinance was not amended to reflect the amendments to § 32-5A-191 enacted after the adoption of the ordinance. After a review of the record, the court noted that the uniform traffic ticket and complaint, the charging instrument, specifically charged defendant with violating one of those sections of § 32-5A-191 that was adopted after the effective date of the ordinance in question. The court thus rejected defendant's argument. It held that the language of the ordinance clearly indicated that any amendments to the state statutes were to be encompassed in the ordinance; therefore, defendant's sentence, imposed pursuant to § 32-5A-191, was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for driving under the influence.
